1 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Vance v. Federal Nat'l Mortg. Ass'n


No. 90,916


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1999 OK 73; 988 P.2d 1275; 1999 Okla. LEXIS 91



September 21, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TULSA COUNTY HONORABLE DAVID PETERSON, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: THE COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS' OPINION IS VACATED; THE DISTRICT COURT'S JUDGMENT IS REVERSED; AND THE CAUSE IS REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS NOT INCONSISTENT WITH TODAY'S PRONOUNCEMENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant appealed decision of Court of Civil Appeals, Division 3 (Oklahoma), that affirmed trial court grant of summary judgment to appellee in foreclosure action.


OVERVIEW: Appellee sought to foreclose its note and mortgage against appellant wife and husband. Although service was issued to both appellants, it was personally served only upon appellant wife. Appellant wife did not answer or otherwise plead to the foreclosure action. Appellee secured a default judgment. Appellee did not communicate with appellant husband -- although his business address was at all relevant times known to it -- until after foreclosure process was completed. Upon becoming aware of the foreclosure and the default judgment, appellants instituted an action seeking vacatur. Appellee moved for summary judgment which was given. Appellants appealed. Court held that due process under U.S. Const. amend. XIV, § 1 and Okla. Const. art. I, § 7, required proper notice, and appellant wife's contest of her ability to understand, due to mental infirmity, the notice imparted by appellee's service of process raised a factual issue that made summary judgment inappropriate.


OUTCOME: Reversed; court held that appellant's contest of her ability to understand, due to mental infirmity, the notice imparted by appellee's service of process in foreclosure action raised a factual issue which made summary judgment inappropriate.

 

2 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Fent v. Oklahoma Capitol Improvement Auth.


No. 92,390


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1999 OK 64; 984 P.2d 200; 1999 Okla. LEXIS 77; 70 O.B.A.J. 2224



June 28, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected July 8, 1999. As Corrected July 15, 1999. Certiorari Denied November 29, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7813.


PRIOR HISTORY: ACTION TO ASSUME ORIGINAL JURISDICTION AND TO DETERMINE STATUTES AND BONDS UNCONSTITUTIONAL.



DISPOSITION: ORIGINAL JURISDICTION ASSUMED; STATUTES AND BOND PROPOSAL ISSUES HELD CONSTITUTIONAL.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The taxpayers brought an original proceeding to challenge the constitutionality of Okla. Stat. tit. 73, §§ 168.3; 301 (1998), alleging that the statutes were revenue generating debts through the issuing of bonds that violated Okla. Const. art. X, §§ 23- 25; art V, § 33.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers sought disapproval of bonds issued pursuant to and a ruling of unconstitutionality of Okla. Stat. tit. 73, §§ 168.3; 301 ("the provisions"). The court assumed original jurisdiction and upheld the provisions. The provisions did not create an unconstitutional debt that violated Okla. Const. art. X, §§ 23- 25; art V, § 33. The bonds that were proposed were not legally binding, requiring only moral obligations to repay according to the annual legislative appropriations for government agencies, which were not guaranteed by the statutes. The bonds proposed were not created in order to raise revenue, as they would be repaid by annual appropriations rather than through raising taxes. At most, the bonds were appropriation-risk, or moral obligations, which did not create a debt in the constitutional sense. Finally, the two proposed bond issues aggregated $ 165 million dollars, which fit within the limits of either § 168.3 or § 301.


OUTCOME: The court assumed original jurisdiction over the matter and found the bond proposal issues constitutional, because the proposals did not authorize the creation of debt or the raising of revenue.

 

3 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Macy v. Board of County Commissioners


No. 89,496


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1999 OK 53; 986 P.2d 1130; 1999 Okla. LEXIS 66; 70 O.B.A.J. 1820



June 1, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] ON APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT, OKLAHOMA COUNTY. Donald L. Worthington, trial judge (sitting by designation).



DISPOSITION: THE TRIAL COURT'S SUMMARY JUDGMENT IS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant board of county commissioners sought review of a ruling from the District Court, Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which concluded that appellant could not deny payment of claims for appellee district attorney's salary supplement so long as funds were available up to the appropriated amount and declared the included supplemental to be free from constitutional restraint.


OVERVIEW: A controversy arose between appellee district attorney and appellant board of county commissioners over appellant's refusal to approve payment of appellee's budgeted salary supplement during the 1996-1997 fiscal year. Appellee submitted to appellant an estimate of office needs for said fiscal year. Appellant denied that supplement, but included in its reported county budget the full amount that appellee requested for the salary supplement. The county excise board later approved the figure. In January 1997, appellant receded in part from their earlier resolution by approving appellee's salary request but only for the first six months. Appellee pressed for a judicial declaration. The district court granted summary relief to appellee. Appellant sought review. The court found that appellee's salary supplement for said fiscal year was effectively converted to an efficacious appropriation. The court found that appellant's January 1997 resolution was ineffective because it came too late and that any increase in salary supplement brought by appellant's budgetary process under Okla. Stat. tit. 19, § 215.30 would stand unaffected by the restrictions imposed by Okla. Const. art. 23, § 10.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment concluding that appellant could not deny payment of claims for appellee's salary supplement because the supplement could be increased by appellant's budgetary process because the statute that allowed appellant to supplement appellee's state-paid salary was enacted before appellee's term of office had begun.

 

4 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Presley v. Board of County Comm'rs


No. 92,675


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1999 OK 45; 981 P.2d 309; 1999 Okla. LEXIS 53; 70 O.B.A.J. 1669



May 18, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY.

Honorable Nancy Coats, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county officers sought review of a decision from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which found in favor of appellee commissioners in their declaratory judgment action to determine the validity of a proposed pay increase to all public officials, despite the apparent prohibition of mid-term salary increases to appellants pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 19, § 180.77.


OVERVIEW: On review, appellant county officers contended that Okla. Stat. tit. 19, § 180.77, which would have produced differing pay scales for mid-term elected officials and those beginning terms after the statute's effective date, did not violate federal and state equal protection guarantees. The appellate court agreed and held that the statutory mandate in Okla. Stat. tit. 19, § 180.77 was rationally related to the important government interests in ensuring the integrity and independence of elected officials. Accordingly, the appellate court expressly overruled Kirk v. Board of County Commissioners, 1979 Okla. 80, 595 P.2d 1334, which had held that a statutory scheme providing for two differing pay scales based upon when an official entered office violated equal protection. The court reversed the order of the lower court allowing pay increases to all county officials regardless of their term status, holding that Okla. Stat. tit. 19, § 180.77, which prohibited mid-term salary increased for public officials, did not violate equal protection guarantees in the federal and state constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision which allowed appellee board to pay wage pay increases to all county officials, regardless of their status as mid-term officials, on the ground that the challenged wage statute, which prohibited pay increases to mid-term officials such as appellant county officers, did not violate equal protection guarantees.

 

5 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Oklahoma Elec. Coop., Inc. v. Oklahoma Gas & Elec. Co.


No. 90,985


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1999 OK 35; 982 P.2d 512; 1999 Okla. LEXIS 39; 70 O.B.A.J. 1366



April 27, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected May 5, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF MCCLAIN COUNTY, THE HONORABLE CANDACE L. BLALOCK, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff electric cooperative appealed a judgment of the District Court of McClain County (Oklahoma), denying its request for an injunction to enjoin the expansion of defendant electric company.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff electric cooperative sought an injunction against the expansion of defendant electric company. The trial court denied the injunction request, finding that defendant was not required to obtain a voter-approved franchise to expand its services within the city limits. The court reversed and remanded, holding that the trial court erred in concluding that defendant had the right to use the city's public ways to expand its electric facilities without a voter-approved franchise. The court held that voter approval was required by Okla. Const. art. 18, § 5(a). The court held that the right granted to defendant was a franchise and not a license, and therefore, defendant could not avoid the voter approval by claiming the grant was a license.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment denying plaintiff electric cooperative's request that defendant electric company be enjoined from expanding its service, holding that expanding defendant's right to use the city's public ways to expand its electric facilities without a voter-approved franchise violated the Oklahoma Constitution.

 

6 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Oklahoma State Bureau of Investigation v. Warren


No. 89,049


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK 133; 975 P.2d 900; 1998 Okla. LEXIS 139; 70 O.B.A.J. 66



December 22, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF KAY COUNTY, OKLAHOMA, HONORABLE D. C. REVARD, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT OF THE DISTRICT COURT REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant applicant sought review of a decision by the District Court of Kay County (Oklahoma), which affirmed appellee Oklahoma State Bureau of Investigation's denial of a concealed handgun license applied for by appellant pursuant to the Oklahoma Self-Defense Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1290.1 et seq.


OVERVIEW: Appellant applicant requested a concealed handgun license under the Oklahoma Self-Defense Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1290.1 et seq. Appellee Oklahoma State Bureau of Investigation denied the application under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1290.11(A) (Supp. 1997), which rendered appellant ineligible for a license due to his felony arrest within the last three years. Both a hearing examiner and the trial court upheld appellee's denial of the permit, despite the fact that appellant had been acquitted of the felony charge. Appellant sought review. Reviewing U.S. Const. amend. II and Okla. Const. art. II, § 26, the court found no absolute constitutional right to carry loaded weapons at all times in all circumstances, or to carry a concealed handgun on or about the person. Thus, the state could exercise its police power to regulate the carrying of weapons in the interest of public safety. The court ruled that § 1290.11(A) was constitutionally invalid as applied to appellant because there was no rational basis to prevent him from obtaining a concealed handgun license given that there was no connection between the charge for which he was acquitted and any firearm. The judgment was reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment upholding appellee Oklahoma State Bureau of Investigations' denial of a concealed handgun license to appellant applicant because the preclusive provisions of the Oklahoma Self-Defense Act were constitutionally invalid as applied to appellant given that there was no rational basis to prevent him from obtaining a license given the lack of a connection between the offense for which he was acquitted and any firearm.

 

7 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Edmondson v. Oklahoma Corp. Comm'n


No. 90,039


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK 118; 971 P.2d 868; 1998 Okla. LEXIS 130; 69 O.B.A.J. 4198



December 8, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected December 10, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. HONORABLE BRYAN C. DIXON, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state, through attorney general, challenged a decision from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which found an amendment to the state constitution increasing the salaries of Corporation Commissioners to be valid.


OVERVIEW: The state legislature enacted an amendment to the state constitution to increase the salaries of the Corporation Commissioners during their term of office. After the legislature enacted a wage increase, a commissioner sought an opinion as to the legality of the act. Appellant attorney general ruled the amendment unconstitutional. Since this ruling left the salaries of two commissioners in limbo, appellant filed an action for declaratory judgment. The trial court found the amendment constitutional. On appeal, the court held that although the constitution granted authority to the legislature to enact changes in salaries for the commissioners, this authority was limited where the authority contravened other provisions of the constitution. The legislature lacked constitutional authority to amend Okla. Const. art. 9, § 18a to increase the salaries of the commissioners during the current term of office because it violated Okla. Const. art. 23, § 10. It also ruled that commissioners were part of the executive branch and salaries could not be tied to the judicial branch. Thus, the decision was reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision and held that the amendment which granted increases in salary to commissioners who were currently in office was unconstitutional because it violated other provisions of the state constitutional which prohibited such pay increases.

 

8 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Polymer Fabricating, Inc. v. Employers Workers' Compensation Ass'n


No. 89,585


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK 113; 980 P.2d 109; 1998 Okla. LEXIS 124; 69 O.B.A.J. 4068



November 24, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] ON APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT, OKLAHOMA COUNTY. James B. Blevins, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: THE TRIAL COURT'S SUMMARY JUDGMENT IS REVERSED AND THE CAUSE REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS TO BE CONSISTENT WITH TODAY'S PRONOUNCEMENT.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Employer Workers' Compensation Association sought review of a judgment of the District Court, Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee employer in an action initiated by the employer contending that the Association's rules, organized under the Oklahoma Workers' Compensation Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 61 (Supp. 1994), which required the employers to pay deficit assessments, was unenforceable.


OVERVIEW: The Association, which was organized under the Oklahoma Workers' Compensation Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 61 (Supp. 1994), required the employers to pay deficit assessments to pool their workers' compensation payments. The employer initiated an action contending that such payments were unenforceable. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of the employer, and the Association sought review. The court determined that it reviewed summary judgment issues de novo and further found that the employer was entitled to summary judgment only if there was no substantial controversy over any material fact. The court held that the amendment to the Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 149.1(C) (Supp. 1996), was a clarifying enactment that authorized security for workers' compensation benefits to be provided for employees who were engaged by employers of self-insurance associations. The court determined that, where an earlier legislative enactment was unclear and a later enactment attempted to remove the ambiguity, the amendatory statute constituted a clarifying enactment, which was to be given retrospective force. The court reversed and remanded the judgment of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded a judgment of the trial court and held that the deficit assessments, which the Association required the employer to make under the Oklahoma Workers' Compensation Act were enforceable.

 

9 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Freeman v. State Election Bd.


No. 91,823


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK 107; 969 P.2d 982; 1998 Okla. LEXIS 116; 69 O.B.A.J. 3794



October 27, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected November 17, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPLICATION TO ASSUME ORIGINAL JURISDICTION AND PETITION FOR WRIT OF MANDAMUS.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ASSUMED, PETITION FOR WRIT OF MANDAMUS DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent State Election Board of the State of Oklahoma disqualified petitioner candidate from an election and removed his name from the ballot because the candidate failed to file a preliminary declaration of candidacy as required by Okla. Stat. tit. 26, § 5-107 (1998). The candidate filed an application for the state supreme court to assume original jurisdiction as well as a petition for writ of mandamus.


OVERVIEW: The candidate's father, who had the same name as the candidate, was a district judge who had filed for reelection. Two days after his father filed for reelection and only a few minutes before the time for filing for office expired, the candidate filed for the office held by his father. Subsequently, the father filed a formal withdrawal of his candidacy, leaving his son as the only candidate. On appeal, the issue was whether the candidate's failure to file the preliminary declaration of candidacy three weeks before the filing period opened, as required by Okla. Stat. tit. 26, § 5-107 (1998), disqualified him from filing a declaration of candidacy during the filing period. Upon review, the state supreme court held that the board correctly determined that the candidate's failure to comply with § 5-107 disqualified him from filing a declaration of candidacy during the filing period. The board's use of § 5-107 to disqualify the candidate served to prevent any appearance of unfairness to other potential candidates who did not file, and, thereby, lost the opportunity to be elected to what turned out to be a vacant office.


OUTCOME: Jurisdiction was assumed and the candidate's petition for writ of mandamus was denied.

 

10 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Herbst v. Sayre (In re Herbst)


No. 89,548


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK 100; 971 P.2d 395; 1998 Okla. LEXIS 110; 69 O.B.A.J. 3508



October 13, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF GARVIN COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE R. B. McCLAIN, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CERTIORARI PREVIOUSLY GRANTED. OPINION OF THE COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS VACATED. JUDGMENT OF THE TRIAL COURT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant grandfather appealed an order of the District Court of Garvin County, Oklahoma, affirming the trial court's denial of his application for grandparental visitation based upon the trial court's ruling that Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 5(A)(1) (Supp. 1996) was unconstitutional as applied.


OVERVIEW: The grandfather sought visitation with his grandchild. The parents opposed the visitation and sought dismissal of his application. The trial court denied the application and the appellate court upheld the decision. The state supreme court found that § 5(A)(1) allowed court ordered grandparent visitation against the wishes of both parents in an intact nuclear family. The application of the statute was an unconstitutional infringement on the parents' rights to the custody and management of their minor child. A vague generalization about the positive influence many grandparents have upon their grandchildren fell far short of the necessary showing of harm that would warrant the state's interference with the parents' decision regarding who may see their child. There was no harm or threat of harm to the child and no unfitness on the part of the parents.


OUTCOME: The order of the appellate court was vacated and the trial court's denial was affirmed.

 

11 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Whitehead v. Tulsa Pub. Sch.


No. 89,856


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK 71; 968 P.2d 1211; 1998 Okla. LEXIS 76; 69 O.B.A.J. 2510



July 7, 1998, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] MOTION TO DISMISS PETITION FOR REVIEW DENIED; REVIEW PROCEEDING SHALL PROCEED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, an employer, its insurer, and the Workers' Compensation Court, sought a ruling on their motion to dismiss petitioner injured employee's review proceeding of an order from the Workers' Compensation Court (Oklahoma) under Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 990A(B) (1996).


OVERVIEW: The injured employee sought review of an order from the Workers' Compensation Court and attempted to begin the review proceedings by depositing her petition for review in the mail on the twentieth day after the order was mailed. The petition was not mailed by certified mail, return-receipt-requested. Respondents filed a motion to dismiss the petition, contending that it was not timely filed pursuant to § 990A(B). The court denied the motion, holding that the date of mailing as established by the postmark affixed by the Unites States Post Office constituted the date of filing, despite the failure to send it by certified mail, return-receipt-requested. The court held that the injured employee was not required to send the petition for review by certified mail in order to properly commence the proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court denied the motion to dismiss the petition for review, and allowed the review to proceed.

 

12 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Truelock v. City of Del City


No. 87,875


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK 64; 967 P.2d 1183; 1998 Okla. LEXIS 74; 69 O.B.A.J. 2402



June 30, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS, DIVISION III.



DISPOSITION: CERTIORARI PREVIOUSLY GRANTED, COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS OPINION VACATED, JUDGMENT OF THE TRIAL COURT AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART, THE TRUELOCKS' APPLICATION FOR APPEAL RELATED ATTORNEYS' FEES DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff homeowners were granted a writ of certiorari to review the judgment of the Oklahoma Court of Civil Appeals, Division III, reversing that part of a judgment awarding them attorneys' fees and personal injury damages of inconvenience, annoyance, and discomfort in an action under Okla. Stat. tit. 51, § 154, alleging that defendant city improperly maintained a sewer and storm system. The city appealed from the denial of attorneys' fees.


OVERVIEW: The homeowners sued the city after their house was repeatedly damaged by rain water and sewage that backed up from the drainage and sewer system. The homeowners were not living in the house during the time specified in the complaint because they had moved out due to prior damage. On the jury's verdict for the homeowners, they were awarded $ 25,000 in property damages, $ 42,800 in personal injury damages for inconvenience, annoyance, and discomfort, and $ 23,000 in attorneys' fees. The appellate court ruled, however, that they were limited to the $ 25,000 in property damages allowed by the Governmental Tort Claims Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 51, § 154.A.1. On further review, the supreme court agreed that, under Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 940, which limited attorney fee awards to those for loss of property, the $ 25,000 limitation of § 154.A.1 precluded a fee award where that maximum was already awarded. However, damages for inconvenience, annoyance, and discomfort were personal injury damages, even though the homeowners did not live in the house, for which the $ 100,000 limitation of § 154.A.2 applied. The city was not entitled to attorneys' fees.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was vacated, that part of the judgment of the trial court awarding personal injury damages to the homeowners and denying attorneys' fees to the city was affirmed, and the trial court's award of attorneys' fees to the homeowners was reversed.

 

13 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


In re OKLAHOMA CAPITOL IMPROVEMENT AUTH.


No. 90,101


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK 25; 964 P.2d 873; 1998 Okla. LEXIS 65; 69 O.B.A.J. 2340



June 23, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Modified August 21, 1998.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Motion denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, two taxpayers, filed a motion to stay the effectiveness of the court's order ruling in favor of appellant state improvement authority in an action contesting the approval of revenue bonds for the construction and improvement of roads and highways.


OVERVIEW: The state improvement authority received approval for revenue bonds for the construction, improvement, maintenance, and repair of state roads, highways, and bridges. In an action contesting the approval, the court ruled against the two taxpayers and denied a petition for rehearing. The taxpayers filed a notice of intent to appeal to the highest federal court and filed a motion to stay mandate. On review, the court treated the motion as a motion to stay the effectiveness of the order and denied the motion. The court held that federal constitutional claims were not raised until the filing of the petition for rehearing and were barred. The court stated that the court's decision was based on independent and adequate state grounds and a stay would have merely caused undue delay. The court further decided that adequate relief was available through an application for a stay under 28 U.S.C.S. § 21-01(f).


OUTCOME: The court denied the two taxpayers' motion to stay the effectiveness of the court's order ruling in favor of the state improvement authority in an action contesting the approval of revenue bonds for the construction and improvement of roads and highways.

 

14 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Oklahoma Bar Ass'n v. Minter


SCBD # 4229


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK 59; 961 P.2d 208; 1998 Okla. LEXIS 59; 69 O.B.A.J. 2097



June 9, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] This Opinion Substituted On Grant Of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of December 24, 1997, Previously Reported at: 1997 Okla. LEXIS 149.



DISPOSITION: RESPONDENT PUBLICLY CENSURED; ORDERED TO PAY COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Complainant Oklahoma Bar Association initiated an action against respondent attorney alleging two counts of misconduct by the attorney in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 5, § 1 (1991), and recommended a six month suspension from the practice of law.


OVERVIEW: The Association initiated an action against the attorney contending that the attorney had violated two counts of misconduct of Okla. Stat. tit. 5, § 1 (1991). The Association recommended a six month suspension from the practice of law. The court found that, because the purpose of attorney disciplinary proceedings was for the protection of the courts, the public, and the profession, strict rules of procedure were to be relaxed to the end that the determination of the proper discipline was based on the legal and ethical merits. The court found that similar levels of misconduct had merited public reprimands instead of suspension. The court found that the attorney's due process rights had not been violated because he had been subjected to a fair and open hearing before a trial panel with notice and an opportunity to present evidence and argument. The court determined that attorneys were not a suspect class and that the disciplinary process complied with the Equal Protection Clause because all similarly situated attorneys received the same treatment. The court held that the attorney had violated two counts of misconduct but held that public reprimand was the appropriate discipline.


OUTCOME: The court granted judgment in favor of the Association and held that the attorney had violated two counts of misconduct. The court determined that public reprimand was the appropriate discipline instead of a six month suspension from the practice of law.

 

15 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Tulsa County Deputy Sheriff's Fraternal Order of Police, Lodge No. 188 v. Board of County Comm'rs


No. 90,930, Cons. w/90,935


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK 44; 959 P.2d 979; 1998 Okla. LEXIS 49; 69 O.B.A.J. 2025



May 28, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM DISTRICT COURT, TULSA COUNTY. Honorable David Peterson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: TRIAL COURT REVERSED; CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, Tulsa County Deputy Sheriff's Fraternal Order of Police and taxpayers, challenged a decision of the District Court, Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which held that appellee Tulsa County Criminal Justice Authority (TCCJA) was not properly created to operate a jail in appellants' action seeking an injunction and a declaratory judgment that delegation of the construction of a jail to a private entity was unconstitutional. Both parties appealed.


OVERVIEW: Appellants brought an action in the district court seeking a declaratory judgment that the delegation to a private entity was unconstitutional and that the TCCJA was created under the wrong statutory provisions. Opponents also sought an injunction against appellee County Commissioners and the TCCJA from taking further action towards privatization. On cross motions for summary judgment, the trial court held that the TCCJA was not properly created to operate the Tulsa County jail, and that it was therefore unnecessary to decide the delegation issues. Both parties appealed, and the court held that the TCCJA was created under the proper statutes, and that the trial court erred in not addressing the delegation issues regarding the operation and maintenance of a jail system by a private for-profit corrections corporation. The court held that the TCCJA was properly created under Okla. Stat. tit. 60, § 178 because it authorized a public trust even though Okla. Stat. tit. 19, §§ 904.1 through 904.2 did not.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's holding that the TCCJA was not properly created and remanded for a determination of delegation issues.

 

16 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Ethics Comm'n v. Keating


No. 90,010


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK 36; 958 P.2d 1250; 1998 Okla. LEXIS 40; 69 O.B.A.J. 1672



May 5, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected August 20, 1998.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] ORIGINAL JURISDICTION ASSUMED AND DECLARATORY RELIEF GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted the joint application to assume original jurisdiction filed by state governor and state ethics commission to decide a controversy involving the use of transportation provided to the governor by the state department of public safety.


OVERVIEW: The state ethics commission (commission) had a rule prohibiting the use of public property for partisan political fundraisers. The state governor appeared at partisan political fundraisers using transportation provided by the department of public safety (DPS), which statutorily provided him with transportation. Both parties filed a joint application to the court to assume original jurisdiction over the matter. The court assumed jurisdiction and held that the transportation provided to the state governor by the DPS did not violate the commission's rule. The court held that the commission's rules, insofar as they controlled those subjects constitutionally placed in its control, had no less weight than statutes, but that they could not override the powers of the legislature on subjects over which the commission had no constitutional grant of authority. The court held that statutory provisions for the governor's security were in the latter category and that the commission's rule could not be applied to him because it would have deprived him of, or dictated the form of, his security statutorily provided by the DPS.


OUTCOME: The court assumed original jurisdiction of the controversy, granted declaratory relief, and held that the transportation provided to the governor by the state department of public safety did not violate rules promulgated by the state ethics commission.

 

17 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Muskogee Fair Haven Manor Phase I, Inc. v. Scott


No. 86,993


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK 26; 957 P.2d 107; 1998 Okla. LEXIS 31; 69 O.B.A.J. 1167



March 31, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS, DIV. III. APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF MUSKOGEE COUNTY, STATE OF OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE THOMAS H. ALFORD, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: THE COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS' OPINION IS VACATED; JUDGMENT BY THE TRIAL COURT IS REVERSED; CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS TO DISMISS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers challenged a decision of the Court of Civil Appeals, Division III, (Oklahoma), which reversed the trial court's judgment against appellee county assessor. The trial court's judgment had declared the taxpayers' property exempt from taxation.


OVERVIEW: The county assessor notified the taxpayers that their property would no longer be listed on the tax rolls as exempt. The appellate court had reversed the trial court's decision because the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction. On appeal, the taxpayers argued that the trial court had jurisdiction to grant declaratory relief in a challenge to the county assessor's refusal to recognize an exemption claimed under a self-executing provision of the Oklahoma Constitution. The court vacated the appellate court's opinion, reversed the trial court's declaratory judgment, and remanded for a dismissal. In doing so, the court held that the legislatively prescribed judicial remedies afforded to the taxpayers under the Ad Valorem Tax Code were adequate and exclusive, and that the trial court therefore lacked subject matter jurisdiction to entertain the declaratory judgment action. The court held that the taxpayers should have appealed the board of equalization's adverse ruling under Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 2880.1 (1991) or paid the tax under protest and sued for a refund pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 2886 (1991).


OUTCOME: The court vacated the appellate court's opinion, reversed the trial court's declaratory judgment, and remanded the action with directions to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction.

 

18 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


In re OKLAHOMA CAPITOL IMPROVEMENT AUTH.


No. 90,101


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK 25; 958 P.2d 759; 1998 Okla. LEXIS 28; 69 O.B.A.J. 1183



March 20, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied April 30, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Okla. LEXIS 38.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] BOND PROPOSAL ISSUE HELD CONSTITUTIONAL.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Applicant capital improvement authority filed an application for approval of proposed authorization of an issuance of highway bonds over opponents' objections pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 73, § 168.6 (Supp. 1997).


OVERVIEW: Applicant capital improvement authority sought approval for its proposed authorization of a highway bond issuance pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 73, § 168.6 (Supp. 1997), over pro se opponents' objections. The court granted applicant's approval, concluding the authorized bonds did not create a prohibited debt under the state constitution provisions, Okla. Const. art. 10, §§ 23, 24 and 25. The court explained the statute did not bind future legislatures to make anticipated appropriations. The court observed the funding for the improvement of highway infrastructure was derived from pre-paid user fees, direct taxes, the transportation fund, and the bond issuance. The court further observed the objectors bore a heavy burden to establish statute invalidity because every presumption must be indulged in favor of constitutionality. The court further explained the legislature had the right and responsibility to declare state fiscal policy and the court does not question sagacity of expressed policy. The court found the authorization was within constitutional debt limitation provisions because it accomplished a lawful result through an innovative, but permissible self-liquidating method.


OUTCOME: The court approved capital improvement authority applicant's authorization of proposed highway bond issuance over pro se opponents' objections because the issuance did not impermissibly bind future legislatures and was within constitutional debt limitation provisions through a self liquidating feature.

 

19 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Brandon v. Ashworth


NO. 90,381


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK 20; 955 P.2d 233; 1998 Okla. LEXIS 24; 69 O.B.A.J. 933



March 10, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected March 12, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] ON APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT IN STEPHENS COUNTY, OKLAHOMA, THE HONORABLE JACK L. BROCK PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: TRIAL COURT'S JUDGMENT REVERSED; JUDGMENT ENTERED FOR DEFENDANTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, school district and superintendent, sought review from a decision of the District Court in Stephens County (Oklahoma) declaring that the superintendent's work contract was unconstitutional under Okla. Const. art. 10, § 26 and void. A dispute arose as to whether plaintiff taxpayers had the standing needed to bring this action.


OVERVIEW: Some taxpayers brought an action against a school district and superintendent asserting that the superintendent's work contract was unlawful under Okla. Const. art. 10, § 26 because he was reemployed under a continuing contract. The trial court found that the contract was void, but the court reversed this decision. The court held that the taxpayers had standing to bring their action for declaratory relief under the Declaratory Judgment Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 1651 (1991) because they demonstrated that there was actual injury for which relief could be granted and their interest was in a constitutionally protected zone. Nonetheless, the court held that the contract as written did not violate the requirements of Okla. Const. art. 10, § 26. Further, the court found that administrators were not teachers and that the statutory language of Okla. Stat. tit. 70, § 6-101 concerning teachers had no effect upon administrators. Even if the superintendent's work contract was void, the court found that it was replaced by a subsequent contract because that contract fully covered the material of the earlier one and therefore rescinded it.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, finding that the taxpayers had standing to bring their action and that the disputed contract was not unconstitutional or void.

 

20 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Crawford v. Guardian Life Ins. Co. of Am.


No. 84,563


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK 10; 954 P.2d 1235; 1998 Okla. LEXIS 11; 69 O.B.A.J. 469



February 3, 1998, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] CERTIORARI PREVIOUSLY GRANTED, COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS' OPINION VACATED, TRIAL COURT'S JUDGMENT REVERSED AND MATTER REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant reinsurer sought review of a decision by the Court of Civil Appeals, Division Four (Oklahoma), which held that appellant's reinsurance agreement with an insurance company in receivership involved a lending or renting of surplus. Therefore, it entered judgment against appellant in appellee receiver's action and imposed a continuing obligation on appellant to pay the benefits due on every life insurance policy it had agreed to reinsure.


OVERVIEW: Appellee receiver brought an action against appellant reinsurer, seeking a declaratory judgment that appellant had no right to offset claims against premiums under its reinsurance agreement with an insolvent insurance company, but rather was obligated to pay all of the claims thereunder and could only collect premiums far later, if at all, as the insolvent company's creditor. The court reversed the judgment that was in appellee's favor, remanded with instructions to enter judgment for appellant, and held that Okla. Stat. tit. 36, § 1928.B.4 could not be applied retroactively so as to deprive appellant of its contractual offset right. The court found that appellant's contract with the insolvent company pre-dated § 1928.B.4, which was an amendment to Okla. Stat. tit. 36, § 1928. Section 1928.B.4 would have deprived appellant of the right to offset its debts against amounts owed to it by the failed insurer where the debt was the result of their reinsurance agreement that was structured to avoid reasonable risk transfer and indemnification criteria. Because § 1928.B.4 did not apply retroactively, appellant was entitled to offset credits and debts with the insolvent company.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of appellee receiver and remanded with directions to enter judgment in favor of appellant reinsurer because appellant's contract with an insolvent insurance company was made when the controlling state statute allowed appellant to offset credits and debts with the insolvent company. A later amendment that forbade such offsets did not operate retroactively.

 

21 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Nelson v. Nelson


No. 88,764


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK 10; 954 P.2d 1219; 1998 Okla. LEXIS 12; 69 O.B.A.J. 452



February 3, 1998, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF NOWATA COUNTY. Honorable James L. Sontag, Associate District Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART; REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged a decision of the District Court of Nowata County (Oklahoma), which entered a default judgment against the father in a divorce action filed by appellee mother. The judgment denied visitation of the parties' children to the father.


OVERVIEW: Thinking the parties were going to settle the divorce action, the father did not file an answer to the petition. The petition anticipated that the father would have visitation with the children. The father failed to attend a court-ordered parenting seminar, and the trial court granted custody to the mother and denied the father visitation on that basis. On appeal, the father argued that Okla. Administrative Order CV-95-1 (1995) and Okla. Stat. tit. 43, § 107.2 (Supp. 1997), which required divorcing parents with children to attend classes intended to help minors to cope with divorce, were unconstitutional. The court reversed that part of the judgment wherein the trial court refused to vacate the default judgment as to visitation, and remanded the action. In doing so, the court held that both rule and the statute were constitutional because neither violated constitutional standards of equal protection or due process nor did they constitute a prohibited delegation of the legislative authority. However, because the father was not on notice that visitation was at issue, the court held that the trial court abused its discretion in refusing to vacate that part of the default judgment.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the default judgment insofar as it denied the father visitation. The action was remanded for a consideration of the father's application for visitation. The judgment was affirmed in all other respects.

McNeill v. City of Tulsa


No. 87,119


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK 2; 953 P.2d 329; 1998 Okla. LEXIS 1; 69 O.B.A.J. 208



January 13, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] PETITION TO REVIEW CERTIFIED INTERLOCUTORY ORDER FROM THE DISTRICT COURT, TULSA COUNTY, HONORABLE JANE WISEMAN, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CERTIORARI PREVIOUSLY GRANTED. TRIAL COURT REVERSED AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent employee asserted that Okla. Stat. tit. 72, § 67.13a (1991) was applicable to petitioner city and its retirement plan. Petitioners, city, retirement plan board, and employee benefit manager, appealed a decision of the District Court, Tulsa County (Oklahoma) finding that § 67.13a compelled municipalities to credit retirees for their military service.


OVERVIEW: A state employee asserted that Okla. Stat. tit. 72, § 67.13a (1991) compelled petitioner city to credit veterans for their service in its retirement plan. The trial court entered judgment for the employee, and the city, its retirement plan board, and its employee benefit manager all appealed from this decision. The court reversed and remanded the trial court's decision, noting that in construing legislation it looked to all relevant enactments in order to effectuate the legislature's will. In analyzing the trial court's decision the court noted that Okla. Stat. tit. 11, § 48-102 (1991), which directed cities to devise retirement plans, did not compel them to credit veterans for their military service. Further, the court noted that the legislature explicitly compelled state governments to consider military service in devising their retirement plans under Okla. Stat. tit. 74, § 902(22), 902(23) (1991).


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's decision that municipalities were required to credit retirees for military service.

 

23 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


In re University Hosps. Auth.


No. 90,212


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK 162; 953 P.2d 314; 1997 Okla. LEXIS 152; 69 O.B.A.J. 59; 69 O.B.A.J. 446



December 30, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Concurring Opinion of Kauger Dated January 29, 1998.



DISPOSITION: JURISDICTION ASSUMED, AND RELIEF GRANTED PER OPINION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, hospital authority and public trust, sought approval of a lease of the university hospitals from the trust to a private health entity pursuant to § 3225 of the University Hospitals Authority Act (Act), Okla. Stat. tit. 63, § 3201 et seq., specifically at Okla. Stat. tit. 63, § 3225. Protestant citizen groups opposed the transaction.


OVERVIEW: The hospital authority and public trust agreed to lease the university hospitals to a private health entity, obtained approval from a contingency review board, and sought the court's approval as required by the Act. Various citizen groups raised public policy issues, and legal and constitutional arguments. The court, after determining that it had jurisdiction, and that the decision was not advisory, entered a declaratory judgment that the proposed agreement was valid and in accordance with the Act and Oklahoma laws. In response to the public policy concerns, the court determined that its review was limited to whether the Act violated other laws or was unconstitutional and refused to pass on the wisdom or business advisability of the transaction. The transaction did not violate open meetings or records laws because the citizen groups were given notice and copies of the contract. The transaction did not violate Okla. Const. art. 10, § 15 because the state received consideration.


OUTCOME: The court entered a declaratory judgment that the proposed agreement was valid and in accordance with the Act and Oklahoma laws. The court limited its review to whether the Act violated other laws or was unconstitutional and refused to review public policy issues. The transaction did not violate the open meetings or records acts.

 

24 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Oklahoma Bar Ass'n v. Minter


SCBD # 4229


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK 157; 1997 Okla. LEXIS 149; 69 O.B.A.J. 19



December 24, 1997, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [**1] RESPONDENT SUSPENDED FOR THREE MONTHS AND ORDERED TO PAY COSTS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Complainant, state bar association, alleged two counts of misconduct warranting discipline against respondent attorney. The state bar sought enhancement of the discipline based on two prior reprimands by the Professional Responsibility Commission. The Professional Responsibility Tribunal (PRT) recommended a six month suspension.


OVERVIEW: The PRT found the attorney's prior reprimands to be a valid consideration and recommended that the attorney be suspended form the practice of law for six months. On appeal, the court found a three-month suspension to be the appropriate discipline. The court held that strict rules of procedure should be relaxed so that determination of the proper discipline was based on the legal and ethical merits, when an attorney's due process rights were not violated. While the court agreed with the attorney that the state bar should follow the rules which applied to proceedings brought by it, the purpose for including facts of prior disciplinary proceedings was to aid the court in its decision-making process. The purposes of attorney discipline would not be met if the court did not consider the prior reprimands. For these reasons, it was proper that the court considered the attorney's two previous private reprimands in formulating the proper discipline. Further, the attorney's due process rights were not violated merely because he was not informed of all the potential evidence against him and he risked suffering a harsher discipline if he did not agree to the private reprimand.


OUTCOME: The attorney was suspended from the practice of law for three months and ordered to pay costs.

 

25 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. Fieker


NO. 88,420


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK 156; 952 P.2d 505; 1997 Okla. LEXIS 151; 69 O.B.A.J. 34



December 23, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Supplemental Opinion on Rehearing of January 27, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Okla. LEXIS 7.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE JAMES B. BLEVINS, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGEMENT OF DISTRICT COURT AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART; WRIT OF MANDAMUS IS GRANTED AGAINST COMMISSIONER OF OKLAHOMA STATE BOARD OF HEALTH.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, 23 state legislators, a physician, and a woman who suffered injury from an abortion performed in a clinic, sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which found that Okla. Stat. tit. 63, §§ 1-731, 1-737, requiring that abortions be performed in certain facilities, were unconstitutional and denied a writ of mandamus compelling appellee state commissioner of health to enforce the statutes.


OVERVIEW: The judgment also dismissed individual members of the state board of health from the action. The commissioner of health refused to enforce the statutes regarding abortion facilities based on opinions of the Oklahoma Attorney General that the statutes were unconstitutional. Appellants argued that mandamus was an appropriate remedy in this case and that §§ 1-731 and 1-737 were constitutional. The court affirmed in part, reversed in part, and granted the writ of mandamus. The denial of a writ of mandamus to require the commissioner to promulgate standards was moot and the dismissal of individual board members was proper because such standards had been issued. Sections 1-731 and 1-737 were constitutional. Under decisional law, a statute restricting abortions constituted an undue burden if, in a large fraction of the cases in which the law was relevant, it operated as a substantial obstacle to a woman's choice to undergo an abortion. The evidence in this case was insufficient to show that the statutes at issue placed an undue burden on a woman's right to abortion. Mandamus was proper against the commissioner to require that he enforce the statutes.


OUTCOME: The court granted mandamus relief to compel enforcement of the statutes, reversed that part of the judgment finding that the statutes at issue were invalid, and affirmed that part of the judgment dismissing the individual members of the state board of health from the action and denying mandamus relief to compel issuance of standards regulating abortion.

Wagnon v. State Farm Fire & Cas. Co.


No. 89,362


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK 160; 951 P.2d 641; 1997 Okla. LEXIS 148; 69 O.B.A.J. 49



December 23, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected April 3, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CERTIFIED QUESTION OF LAW FROM THE UNITED STATES COURT OF APPEALS FOR THE TENTH CIRCUIT.



DISPOSITION: CERTIFIED QUESTION ANSWERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant insurer and appellee insureds both sought review of a judgment from the United States District Court for the Northern District of Oklahoma, which entered judgment on behalf of appellees on their breach of contract claim. Certified questions of law were submitted concerning the statute of limitations applicable to the theft provision of appellees' homeowners insurance policy.


OVERVIEW: Appellant insurer and appellee insureds both challenged the lower court judgment that entered judgment on behalf of appellees on their breach of contract claim and granted judgment to appellant on the bad faith claim. The court was asked to answer the certified question of law concerning whether theft coverage in appellees' homeowners insurance policy was subject to the one-year statute of limitations prescribed for fire insurance polices in Okla. Stat. tit. 36, § 4803(G). The court held that theft coverage was not subject to the one-year statute of limitations prescribed for fire insurance polices because there was a statutory distinction between the peril of fire and theft in the insurance policy. The court held that theft was defined as casualty insurance and according to Okla. Stat. tit. 8, § 3617, could not be limited to less than two years for bringing a court action.


OUTCOME: The court held that theft coverage was not subject to the one-year statute of limitations prescribed for fire insurance policies because theft was defined as casualty insurance and the statute of limitations could not be limited to less than two years.

 

27 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


First Am. Bank & Trust Co. v. Okla. Indus. Fin. Auth.


No. 87,070


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK 155; 951 P.2d 625; 1997 Okla. LEXIS 147; 69 O.B.A.J. 23



December 23, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected April 3, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS, DIVISION IV. APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY, STATE OF OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE JOHN M. AMICK, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CERTIORARI PREVIOUSLY GRANTED; COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS' OPINION VACATED; TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT REVERSED AND MATTER REMANDED FOR PROCEEDINGS CONSISTENT WITH THIS OPINION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county and others sought review of a judgment of the Oklahoma Court of Civil Appeals, Division IV, which affirmed a decision of the trial court that Okla. Const. art. 10, § 6 had the effect of extinguishing all county ad valorem real estate taxes assessed and owing against a property after appellee Oklahoma Industrial Finance Authority (OIFA) acquired the property.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that once the OIFA took title to a property, by foreclosure or otherwise, any outstanding ad valorem real estate taxes against the property were extinguished pursuant to a provision of the Oklahoma Constitution that stated that all county and municipal property of the state was exempt from taxation. The court of appeals affirmed. The court vacated, reversed, and remanded. The court noted the OIFA's authority to take title by foreclosure to any industrial development project where the acquisition was necessary to protect a loan made by it, and its authority to sell, transfer, and convey any such project to a responsible buyer. Okla. Stat. tit. 74, § 855(o) (1991). Nevertheless the tax exemption provision for state-owned property found in Okla. Const. art. 10, § 6 was prospective only. The legislature had the authority to require payment of taxes assessed against real estate while privately owned, but which remained unpaid when the state acquired the property for some legitimate governmental purpose. The county also had that same power. The assessed and unpaid ad valorem taxes were not automatically extinguished upon reacquisition of a property by the OIFA.


OUTCOME: The court granted certiorari, vacated the opinion of the court of civil appeals, and reversed the judgment of the trial court. The court remanded the case for further proceedings consistent with the opinion.

 

28 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Public Serv. Co. v. State ex rel. Corporation Comm'n


No. 89,340


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK 145; 948 P.2d 713; 1997 Okla. LEXIS 136; 68 O.B.A.J. 3885



November 25, 1997, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM OKLAHOMA CORPORATION COMMISSION.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a second challenge, appellant electric utility sought review of Okla. Corp. Comm. R. 60 as amended by appellee Oklahoma Corporation Commission after the court had struck down the prior rule requiring electric suppliers to pass on to consumers the costs of changing suppliers. At issue was whether Rule 60, requiring an acquiring supplier to buy the replaced supplier's equipment at a price fixed by the rule, violated Okla. Const. art. 9, § 18.


OVERVIEW: After the Oklahoma legislature enacted a law restructuring electric utilities, the Commission promulgated Rule 60, governing the change from one supplier to another. The utility challenged the rule, alleging that in requiring the acquiring supplier to purchase the replaced supplier's equipment, the rule contravened the state constitution by interfering with a utility's internal management decision whether to buy the replaced supplier's old equipment or replace it with new equipment. The utility argued further that the purchase provision resulted in arbitrary costs because the purchase price was based on a formula contained in the rule that did not permit an acquiring supplier to negotiate. The Commission argued that it was charged with protecting consumers and the rule was necessary in order to avoid expensive duplication of equipment. The court stated that although the Commission had power to guard the public interest with regard to utility rates, its power did not include the right to dictate internal management decisions of a public utility, and concluded that the portions of Rule 60 purporting to set the price to be paid by an acquiring supplier were unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the Commission in promulgating the rule relating to a consumer's change from one supplier of electricity to another. The Court held that the sections of the rule purporting to set the purchase price for a replaced supplier's equipment were invalid.

Ernest E. v. Oklahoma Tax Comm'n


No. 87,085


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK 126; 947 P.2d 525; 1997 Okla. LEXIS 117; 68 O.B.A.J. 3329



October 14, 1997, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] ORDER OF TAX COMMISSION AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers, who were Native American Indians, challenged the decision of appellee, the Oklahoma Tax Commission, which adopted findings, conclusions and recommendations of the administrative law judge (ALJ) dismissing the taxpayers' protest based on res judicata and statute of limitations grounds.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers filed their first claim for a refund in 1982, and then in 1983 filed a protest with the Commission. They claimed that the state had no authority to tax their income due to their status in that they both resided on Indian trust property and were employed by the Bureau of Indian Affairs on Indian Trust land. The Commission denied the claim in 1985, and the taxpayers did not appeal. In 1991, the taxpayers again claimed a refund, this time for the years 1979-1985, advancing the same arguments. The Commission argued that the second protest should be dismissed on res judicata and limitations grounds. The ALJ recommended dismissal, which the Commission adopted, and an appeal was taken. The court held that, despite the taxpayers' claim that the tax violated federal law, because they did not attempt to use any of the statutory refund remedies in a timely fashion, nor did they raise any argument that the state refund procedures were inadequate, the statutory remedies for refund of illegally collected taxes were sufficiently certain to withstand federal scrutiny. Thus, the court found that the taxpayers' 1991 claim for income tax refunds for the years 1979-1985 was untimely.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the Commission.

Sholer v. State ex rel. Dep't of Pub. Safety


No. 83,504 (Cons/w 83,505)


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK 152; 945 P.2d 469; 1997 Okla. LEXIS 85; 68 O.B.A.J. 2330



July 1, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected August 14, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Opinion of May 23, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Okla. LEXIS 64.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On rehearing to a challenge to multiple reinstatement fees, appellant Department of Public Safety asserted that appellee drivers were precluded from bringing suit in state court because they failed to follow the mandate of Okla. Stat. tit. 62, § 206 (1991).


OVERVIEW: The Department claimed that the drivers were required to follow § 206, and that by failing to give notice in writing at the time the fees were paid they were precluded from bringing suit in state court. The court disagreed, holding that the statute was not an impediment to the district court's exercise of jurisdiction under Okla. Const. art. 7 § 7. However, even if it were otherwise, the statute was a bar to recovery. The drivers, who were charged multiple reinstatement fees, correctly asserted that they were not required to follow § 206 because they were not claiming a fee to be unconstitutional or invalid. Rather, they disputed only the accounting practices of the Department in requiring the payment of multiple reinstatement fees. The court held that § 206 was not applicable to the drivers because there argument was: while one fee may have been validly recovered according to the terms of the statute, multiple fees were not.


OUTCOME: On rehearing, the court held that the drivers were permitted to bring suit in state court.

WILLIAMS NATURAL GAS CO. v. PERKINS


NO. 83,981


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK 72; 952 P.2d 483; 1997 Okla. LEXIS 71; 68 O.B.A.J. 2080



June 10, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected September 10, 1997. As Amended on Denial of Rehearing February 23, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Okla. LEXIS 17.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] CERTIORARI PREVIOUSLY GRANTED; COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS' OPINION VACATED; JUDGMENT REVERSED; POST-TRIAL ORDER OF THE TRIAL COURT VACATED; CAUSE REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS; MOTION FOR APPEAL-RELATED ATTORNEY FEES DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowner sought review of a decision of the Court of Civil Appeals Division Three (Oklahoma), which reversed and remanded the trial court's decision fixing the landowners' compensation at $ 3,800 in appellee gas company's condemnation proceeding.


OVERVIEW: The gas company initiated condemnation proceedings against the landowner. The trial court entered the jury verdict, which fixed the landowner's' compensation at $ 3,800. The landowner appealed and the appellate court reversed and remanded. The court granted certiorari. The court found that because Okla. Stat. tit. 66, § 53(D) provided a method for determining just compensation which was inconsistent with Okla. Const. art. 2, § 24 in proceedings involving partial takings, it was constitutionally infirm to the extent of the inconsistency. The court found that while the trial court's jury instructions regarding compensation was correct at law, the trial court committed fundamental error in modifying the uniform instruction to incorporate the constitutionally infirm statutory provisions of Okla. Stat. tit. 66, § 53(D). The court held that the trial court abused its discretion in excluding expert testimony regarding damage to the property. The court also found that the trial court erred in denying the landowners' motion for court costs, prejudgment interest, post-judgment interest, attorney fees, expert witness fees, and appraiser fees.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court fixing the landowners' compensation at $ 3,800 and vacated the opinion of the appellate court.

United Design Corp. v. Okla. ex rel. Okla. Tax Comm'n


No. 83,438


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK 43; 942 P.2d 725; 1997 Okla. LEXIS 32; 68 O.B.A.J. 984



March 18, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected June 19, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Okla. LEXIS 106.



DISPOSITION:  [***1] CERTIORARI PREVIOUSLY GRANTED; OPINION OF COURT OF CIVIL APPEALS VACATED; ORDER OF OKLAHOMA TAX COMMISSION AFFIRMED IN PART, REVERSED IN PART; CAUSE REMANDED TO TAX COMMISSION WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee, the Oklahoma Tax Commission, assessed a use and sales tax against appellant taxpayer. The taxpayer protested the assessment and after a hearing, the Commission adopted the administrative law judge's recommendations and granted in part and denied in part the taxpayer's protest. On appeal, the Court of Civil Appeals (Oklahoma) affirmed in part the Commission's decision and reversed it in part. The taxpayer sought review.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer was engaged in the design, manufacture, and sale of gift figurines. Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 1359 provided a manufacturer's exemption from the use and sales tax. The parties disagreed as to what constituted manufacturing for purposes of this exemption. On appeal, the court vacated the lower court's judgment and affirmed the Commission's decision in part and reversed it in part. The court found that the Commission's view of the taxpayer's integrated manufacturing process was contrary to a recent decision that if a manufacturing operation was an integrated production process, it should not be divided into discrete segments. Thus, the court reversed the Commission's exclusion of the taxpayer's development of molds, its packaging, its warehousing of the figurines, and its catalogue production and remanded for reconsideration in light of this case. However, the court upheld the Commission's decision that the taxpayer's sale of display items and its computer programming services did not qualify for the exemption. In addition, the court reversed the Commission's assessment of a use tax that did not deduct for the taxpayer's discounts.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the lower court's opinion and affirmed in part and reversed and remanded in part the Commission's order.

City of Anadarko v. FOP, Lodge 118


No. 86,046 (Comp. With 86,047, 86,093 and 86,094), No. 86,047 (Comp. With 86,046, 86,093 and 86,094), No. 86,093 (Comp. With 86,046, 86,047 and 86,094), No. 86,094 (Comp. With 86,046, 86,047, and 86,093).


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK 14; 934 P.2d 328; 1997 Okla. LEXIS 13; 159 L.R.R.M. 2431; 68 O.B.A.J. 583



February 18, 1997, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CADDO COUNTY.

APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF PONTOTOC COUNTY.

APPEALS FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF GRADY COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant unions, which represented city police officers and firefighters, challenged judgments arising out of the District Court of Caddo County (Oklahoma), the District Court of Pontotoc County (Oklahoma), and the District Court of Grady County (Oklahoma), which ruled in favor of appellee cities, and held that Okla. Stat. tit. 11, § 51-108 (Supp. 1994), concerning arbitration procedures between the cities and unions, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Section 51-108 permitted binding interest arbitration between cities and their police and firefighters as to collective bargaining agreements. The statute permitted each side to submit its best offer to an arbitrator and the arbitrator would select one offer. If the city's offer was not chosen, the city could hold an election, allowing the voters to select either the city's offer or the union's offer. In each case at bar, negotiations began between the union and the city for a new collective bargaining agreement. An impasse was declared and the union requested binding interest arbitration under § 51-108. The city sought a declaratory judgment, asking that § 51-108 be declared unconstitutional. In each case, the trial held that the statute offended the Oklahoma Constitution. On appeal, the court held as follows: (1) The court found that § 51-108 did not deny cities their constitutional right of access to the courts because judicial review was available. (2) Section 51-108 did not deny cities their right to a jury trial because that right was waivable, it depended on the nature of the dispute, and the court could not envision the use of a jury in the collective bargaining process.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial courts' judgments and remanded the causes to their respective trial courts.

In re Initiative Petition No. 364


No. 86,828


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1996 OK 129; 930 P.2d 186; 1996 Okla. LEXIS 144; 67 O.B.A.J. 3874



December 10, 1996, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] INITIATIVE PETITION NO. 364 DECLARED INVALID; ORDERED DENIED SUBMISSION TO THE PEOPLE. APPLICATION TO WITHDRAW SIGNATURES AND DISMISS APPEAL DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Protestant individual filed an action pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 34, § 8 (Supp. 1992) to challenge the legal sufficiency of an initiative petition. Proponent, the Chairman of the Oklahoma Term Limits, appealed the ballot title prepared by the Oklahoma Attorney General, pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 34, § 10.


OVERVIEW: The individual filed an action under Okla. Stat. tit. 34, § 8 (Supp. 1992), urging that the initiative measure violated U.S. Const. art. V and Okla. Stat. art. V, § 1. The individual contended that the initiative measure violated Okla. Stat. art. V, § 1 because it was neither a "law" nor an amendment to the Oklahoma Constitution and it sought to ultimately sought to amend the United States Constitution in a coercive manner. The individual also argued that the initiative measure violated U.S. Const. art. V by proposing to amend the United States Constitution by a process that did not conform to U.S. Const. art. V. The Chairman sought review of the Attorney General's preparation of the associated ballot title. The court declared the initiative petition invalid and denied submission of it to the people. The court held (1) that the measure violated U.S. Const. art. V, as it would have allowed the people to indirectly propose amendments to the United States Constitution; and (2) that the measure violated Okla. Stat. art. V, § 1, as it was beyond the power of the initiative granted the people.


OUTCOME: The court declared that the initiative petition was invalid. The court therefore denied submission of it to the people.

Park View Hosp. Trust Auth. v. State ex rel. Okla. Dep't of Labor


No. 81,539


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1996 OK 108; 925 P.2d 541; 1996 Okla. LEXIS 120; 67 O.B.A.J. 2927; 3 Wage & Hour Cas. 2d (BNA) 1084



October 1, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEALS, DIVISION 4. APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY, STATE OF OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE NILES JACKSON, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: CERTIORARI PREVIOUSLY GRANTED; COURT OF APPEALS' OPINION VACATED; TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT REVERSED AND MATTER REMANDED WITH A DIRECTION TO DISMISS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a hospital trust authority (hospital), appealed the ruling of the Court of Appeals, Division 4 (Oklahoma), which affirmed a trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of appellees, the Oklahoma Department of Labor and its Commissioner, in the hospital's action for a declaration that it was not subject to the Oklahoma Minimum Wages on Public Works Act (Little Davis-Bacon Act), Okla. Stat. tit. 40, § 196.1 et seq. (1991).


OVERVIEW: The hospital contended that the Little Davis-Bacon Act, ruled unconstitutional in another action during this action's appellate phase, did not apply to it, as no work had been on a contemplated building project to update its facilities and no contracts had been entered into. The Department argued that the trial court's ruling that the Little-Davis Bacon Act applied to the hospital should stand, because it had not previously raised the issue of the statute's constitutionality. The court vacated the trial court's ruling in favor of the Department. The court found that: (1) the Little Davis-Bacon Act was held unconstitutional in another action because it delegated power to the federal government to determine prevailing wage rates without setting a standard for exercise of that power; (2) there was no principled distinction between the action in which the Little-Davis Bacon Act was found to be unconstitutional and the action in question; and (3) because no contract had been negotiated or entered into and no expenses for labor or services had been incurred, any decision concerning the issue of whether the hospital was a public body under the Little Davis-Bacon Act was meaningless.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of the Department and remanded the cause to the trial court with an instruction to dismiss the action.
