Fraternal Order of Police v. City of Choctaw


No. 85,460 (comp. with 85,542 and 85,266), No. 85,542 (comp. with 85,460 and 85,266), No. 85,266 (comp. with 85,460 and 85,542)


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1996 OK 78; 933 P.2d 261; 1996 Okla. LEXIS 90; 159 L.R.R.M. 2553; 68 O.B.A.J. 301; 67 O.B.A.J. 2235



July 9, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected January 27, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPLICATION FOR EXTRA ORDINARY RELIEF; APPEAL FROM DISTRICT COURT.



DISPOSITION: The judgments of the District Courts in cases numbered 85,460 and 85,542 are reversed and the cases remanded for such further proceedings as may be consistent with this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In three separate actions, appellants sought review from decisions of the district courts (Oklahoma), which held that a section of the Fire and Police Arbitration Act, specifically, Okla. Stat. tit. 11, § 51-108 (Supp. 1994), was an unconstitutional infringement on local government.


OVERVIEW: District courts held that § 51-108 constituted an unconstitutional infringement on local government. Section 51-108, in effect, mandated binding interest arbitration. On appeal, the court held that because the rights contained in the Fire and Police Arbitration Act were matters of statewide concern, they did not violate the home rule provisions of Okla. Const. art. XVIII, § 3. The court further held that the Act's delegation of authority to an arbitrator was permissible because there were sufficient guidelines. On its face, § 51-108 did not violate either Okla. Const. art. X, § 20 or § 26. It did not expressly impose a tax on municipal citizens, nor did not expressly require that the city's debt limitation be exceeded. The court held that § 51-108 applied equally to all cities and to all police and firefighters involved in the collective bargaining process. Section 51-018 was not violative of Okla. Const. art. V, § 46. The court held that in no way did § 51-108 affect the rights, duties, and powers of state officials elected to represent their constituents. The Guarantee Clause did not apply to a municipal government. The court held that § 51-108 withstood constitutional attack.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments of the district courts and remanded the cases for further proceedings.

 

37 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


City of Oklahoma City v. State ex rel. Oklahoma DOL


No. 85,888


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


918 P.2d 26; 1996 Okla. LEXIS 104



May 14, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Original Opinion of October 10, 1995, Reported at: 918 P.2d 26; 1995 Okla. LEXIS 118.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney general, on behalf of the Department of Labor, asked on rehearing of a case involving appellees, Oklahoma City and the public trusts, that the court would clarify the retrospective contours of its pronouncement of October 10, 1995, when it condemned as unconstitutional the provisions of Okla. Stat. tit. 40, § 196.1 et seq. (1991), the Prevailing Wage Act, also known as the Little Davis-Bacon Act.


OVERVIEW: The attorney general urged that the court's opinion should be given a limited backward reach because it settled a significant first-impression controversy. Appellees did not challenge the call for limited retrospectivity of the court's sentence of nullity. The court opined that because appellees were adversely affected by the mandatory prevailing-wage clauses and were parties to the instant litigation, the court was free to consider sua sponte, at rehearing, how retrospective the 1995 pronouncement should be, but it rejected the attorney general's quest for sweeping prospectivity, stating that the only prospectivity-related issue it would decide was whether prevailing-wage contract clauses in pre-opinion contracts were subject to the sentence of nullity. The court concluded that public-construction contracts negotiated and executed before the opinion would be impervious to an attack on the constitutionality of their prevailing-wage clauses, and those contracts negotiated before but executed after the opinion would be equally safe from attack absent proof of a post-opinion downward contract price adjustment reflecting a pre-execution rejection of the prevailing-wage clause.


OUTCOME: The court decided that prevailing-wage clauses in contracts defined by timeline were to be impervious to a constitutional attack and that the opinion's sentence of nullity would govern the instant case and all constitutional challenges of the prevailing-wage clause's validity interposed by public builders, whose claims, counterclaims, or cross-claims were pending at the time of the original opinion.

 

38 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Keating v. Johnson


No. 86,628


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1996 OK 61; 918 P.2d 51; 1996 Okla. LEXIS 73; 67 O.B.A.J. 1680



May 14, 1996, FILED



DISPOSITION:  [***1] APPLICATION TO ASSUME ORIGINAL JURISDICTION DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, governor and two members of the Oklahoma legislature, filed an application with the court to assume original jurisdiction over their action requesting declaratory or other relief, which alleged that respondent Oklahoma legislature violated the separation of powers doctrine, Okla. Const. art. 4, § 1, when it vested in itself or legislative leadership the authority to make appointments to executive branch boards.


OVERVIEW: The governor and legislature members contended that the legislature violated the separation of powers doctrine when it enacted four statutory schemes that gave itself the power to appoint members to executive boards and the power to exercise executive functions. They contended that the court should exercise original jurisdiction based on the doctrine of publici juris, in that the question had great public importance and involved statewide concern. The court disagreed and held that although the question was of great public importance, the governor and legislature members failed to show that there was some immediacy involved that would call for the court to exercise its discretion to hear the matter at the present time. Moreover, the lack of urgency was demonstrated by the governor and legislature members' failure to claim that any vacancy existed in the offices involved, and their failure to claim that the governor had any inherent appointment authority to the offices.


OUTCOME: The court declined to exercise original jurisdiction over the governor and legislature members' separation of powers claim.

Washington v. State ex rel. Dep't of Corr.


No. 85,295


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1996 OK 139; 915 P.2d 359; 1996 Okla. LEXIS 59

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEALS, DIVISION IV. Honorable Steven W. Taylor, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: CERTIORARI PREVIOUSLY GRANTED; COURT OF APPEALS OPINION VACATED; TRIAL COURT REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged a decision of the Court of Appeals, Division IV (Oklahoma), which affirmed a decision of the trial court dismissing the inmate's lawsuit brought against appellee prison officials under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983.


OVERVIEW: The inmate brought suit against the prison officials under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, claiming that they had violated his civil rights during his incarceration. The officials filed a motion to dismiss the action for failure to state a claim, which the trial court granted. The inmate appealed, and the appellate court affirmed the dismissal. The inmate sought review. The court vacated the opinion of the appellate court, reversed the decision of the trial court, and remanded the matter. Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 2012 (1991) and Okla. R. Dist. Ct. 13, Okla. Stat. tit. 12, ch. 2, app. (1991), required the inmate to be given an opportunity to respond to the motion. The inmate should have been given at least 15 days to respond. The motion included matters that were outside of the pleadings that were considered by the trial court. The trial court erred when it dismissed the inmate's case without allowing him the opportunity to respond. Even assuming that the trial court did not consider matters outside the pleadings, the court found that the inmate's case was dismissed prematurely because not all of his claims appeared to be frivolous on their face or without merit.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the opinion of the appellate court, reversed the decision of the trial court, and remanded the matter.

SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA

The appeals court affirmed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the banks. On appeal, the court vacated and reversed. The court held that the taxpayer's response to the motion for summary judgment, in which he asserted his qui tam claim, should have been treated as a request to amend his pleadings.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the appeals court's decision and reversed the trial court's grant of summary judgment to four banks in the taxpayer's qui tam action.

 

41 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Shaffer v. Jeffery


NO. 81,275, NO. 83,219


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1996 OK 47; 915 P.2d 910; 1996 Okla. LEXIS 48



March 26, 1996, FILED



DISPOSITION:  [***1] CERTIORARI PREVIOUSLY GRANTED IN CAUSES NOS. 81,275 AND 83,219; OPINIONS OF THE COURT OF APPEALS IN NOS. 81,275 AND 83,219 VACATED; JUDGMENTS OF DISTRICT COURT ON APPEAL IN NOS. 81,275 AND 83,219 REVERSED; CAUSES REMANDED TO THE DISTRICT COURT


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, six adopting couples, sought review of two judgments of the court of appeals (Oklahoma), which dismissed the adopting couples' complaints against defendants, lawyer and law firm, and ordered arbitration.


OVERVIEW: Six adopting couples challenged two judgments dismissing their actions alleging fraud in the inducement of the attorney-client contract. The issue was whether a showing of fraud in the inducement of the attorney-client contract defeated the enforcement of the arbitration clause in that contract. On appeal, the court vacated the judgments and held that arbitration agreements could be voidable when either the arbitration provision itself or the contract containing that agreement was fraudulently induced. The court found that Okla. Stat. tit. 15, § 802A (1991) applied to both the arbitration agreement itself and to the contract containing the arbitration agreement. The court also found that the lawyer and his law firm did not dispute the fraud claims in any filed instrument, but only stated that there was no evidence before the court concerning fraud. The court further found that the district court did not consider the adopting couples' fraud claims prior to dismissing their actions. Thus, the court ruled that the district court was required to adjudicate the fraud claims prior to granting the lawyer and the law firm relief based upon the validity of the arbitration clause.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgments.

Public Serv. Co. v. Okla. ex rel. Corp. Comm'n ex rel. Loving


NO. 81,518


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1996 OK 43; 918 P.2d 733; 1996 Okla. LEXIS 43; 67 O.B.A.J. 1021



March 19, 1996, FILED



DISPOSITION:  [***1] RULING OF CORPORATION COMMISSION REVERSED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant utility company sought review of a ruling of appellee Oklahoma Corporation Commission, which amended Okla. Admin. Code §§ 165:35-1-2, 165L35-11-3 (Rule 60) to require that an acquiring electric supplier pass the costs of changing suppliers on to the consumer or user of the electricity.


OVERVIEW: The proposed amendments to Rule 60 changed language to close a perceived loophole in the rule because prior to the amendment some users of electricity could switch suppliers without paying the associated costs. On appeal, the court held that Rule 60 was invalid insofar as it would require an acquiring electric supplier to pass the costs of changing suppliers on to the consumer or user of the electricity. As to the Commission's failure to take sworn testimony, the court held that although there were no witnesses or sworn testimony, all present at the hearing were permitted to make their comments to the Commission and the comments were included in the transcript. The court held that the Commission was without authority to promulgate the original rule and the amendment, because it amounted to an interference with the internal management of a utility company. The court found that Rule 60 mandated that the changeover costs be passed on directly to the consumer, which clearly usurped the management function by forbidding the utility company from absorbing the costs.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the ruling.

Johnson v. Bd. of Governors of Registered Dentists of Okla.


No. 82,371


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1996 OK 41; 913 P.2d 1339; 1996 Okla. LEXIS 49; 67 O.B.A.J. 1027



March 19, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY, OKLAHOMA, Honorable Richard Freeman, Judge. This Opinion Substituted on Grant of Rehearing for Withdrawn Opinion of April 11, 1995, Previously Reported at: 1995 Okla. LEXIS 45.



DISPOSITION: TRIAL COURT'S JUDGMENT AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART; CAUSE REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff dentist and defendant dental board appealed the decision of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which found that the standard of proof in the disciplinary action against the dentist was proper, the complaint was void, and the competing board members should have been disqualified.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court affirmed in part. The trial court had jurisdiction pursuant to the Administrative Procedures Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 75, §§ 301-323 (1991), because the dentist alleged lack of due process, inadequate administrative relief, and irreparable injury. The board was not required to establish guidelines for the imposition of discipline. The trial court was within its discretion when it ordered the members of the board disqualified from hearing the proceeding against the dentist. However, the court reversed the trial court's approval of the board's use of preponderance of the evidence standard of proof. The proper standard of proof in disciplinary proceedings against a person holding a professional license was clear and convincing. The dentist faced the possible loss of a constitutionally protected property right, his livelihood and professional reputation. The state had an interest in the health and welfare of its citizens. However, there was high risk of error because the board was also was investigator, prosecutor, and decision-maker. The risk was increased because a competitor of the dentist was investigator and made prosecutorial recommendations to the board.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The trial court had jurisdiction, the board was not statutorily required to promulgate rules establishing disciplinary guidelines, the proper standard of was clear and convincing, and the trial court was acting within its discretion when it disqualified the board members.

Roach v. Jimmy D. Enters.


No. 83,534


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1996 OK 26; 912 P.2d 852; 1996 Okla. LEXIS 27; 67 O.B.A.J. 803



February 27, 1996, FILED

DISPOSITION: PETITION FOR CERTIORARI PREVIOUSLY GRANTED; CERTIFIED INTERLOCUTORY ORDER OF THE TRIAL COURT REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the mother of three deceased children and others, sought certiorari review of an interlocutory order from the District Court of Garfield County (Oklahoma) that held that, in the mother's wrongful death action against defendants, a driver and the owners of two drinking establishments, ruled that the mother could not recover punitive damages as prayed for, under Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 1053.


OVERVIEW: Three of the mother's children were killed when the car in which they were traveling was struck by the driver's car; the driver died in the accident. The mother alleged that the driver was negligent and intoxicated and filed suit against the driver's estate and the two establishments that allegedly sold the driver liquor. The mother prayed for punitive damages. The trial court granted defendants summary judgment on the issue of punitive damages, ruling that such damages were not available because they were not mentioned in the wrongful death statute for minors, Okla. The court then ruled that § 1055, which provided a cause of action for wrongful death of minors but which did not mention punitive damages, was to be read in conjunction with Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 1053, which created a cause of action for wrongful death of adults and which provided for punitive damages.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's interlocutory order.

 

45 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Bushert v. Hughes


No. 85,395


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1996 OK 21; 912 P.2d 334; 1996 Okla. LEXIS 32; 67 O.B.A.J. 700



February 20, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] ON APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT, NOBLE COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: THE MOTION TO DISMISS IS DENIED WITH PREJUDICE TO RENEWAL


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a decision by the District Court, Noble County (Oklahoma), which entered judgment in favor of appellee in appellee's breach of contract action. Appellee sought to dismiss the appeal as untimely.


OVERVIEW: Appellant filed a motion for a new trial after judgment was entered against him in a breach of contract action. The district court judge denied the motion in a signed memo to the parties. There was no indication in the record that either party received a copy of the judge's memo. Appellant brought his appeal within 30 days of receipt of the copy of an order drafted by appellee's counsel regarding the denial of a new trial. Appellee's counsel then filed the order with the court. Appellee argued that the appeal was untimely because it was not filed within 30 days of the court's order. On appeal, the court stated that the district court failed to follow any of the procedures set forth in Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 696.2(A) (1993). The court reasoned that the district court judge did not file the memo with the court and the court clerk did not send a certified copy to the parties. The court held that appellant's counsel was required to monitor the filings for the appealable order and the order filed by appellee's counsel did not meet the statutory requirements of § 696.2. In conclusion, the court held that by signing the non-statutory order appellant forfeited his right to the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court denied appellee's motion to dismiss appellant's appeal with prejudice to renewal.

 

46 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Rollings v. Thermodyne Indus.


NO. 82,774


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1996 OK 6; 910 P.2d 1030; 1996 Okla. LEXIS 10; 67 O.B.A.J. 399



January 23, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CERTIORARI TO THE OKLAHOMA COURT OF APPEALS, DIVISION III.



DISPOSITION: CERTIORARI PREVIOUSLY GRANTED; COA OPINION VACATED; JUDGMENT OF DISTRICT COURT REVERSED AND CASE REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patentee sought review of a judgment from the court of appeals (Oklahoma), which held an arbitration clause contained in an agreement between plaintiff and defendant manufacturer had not violated Okla. Const. art. 2, § 6 and Okla. Const. art. 23, § 8. In seeking review, plaintiff claimed the Oklahoma Constitution had been violated because the arbitration clause had deprived plaintiff of access to the courts for future controversies.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff patentee and defendant manufacturer entered into a agreement requiring the submission of disputes to statutory arbitration. When a dispute arose, plaintiff brought an action against defendant. Thereafter, defendant moved to compel arbitration pursuant to the agreement's requirement. When the appeals court held the arbitration clause contained in the agreement had not violated Okla. Const. art. 2, § 6 and Okla. Const. art. 23, § 8, plaintiff sought review, and the court vacated the judgment of the appeals court and remanded to the trial court. The court agreed with the appeals court and found the arbitration clause had not violated the Oklahoma Constitution by depriving plaintiff of access to the courts. In finding that the clause had not violated the Oklahoma Constitution, the court held that with the limited scope of review as provided by the Oklahoma Uniform Arbitration Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 15, § 801 et seq. (1991), the parties' agreement had been sufficient to pass muster under § 6. Moreover, the court found that the state had a strong public policy favoring arbitration and that § 6 afforded a judicial remedy for only those wrongs recognized by the legislature.


OUTCOME: After finding an arbitration clause had not violated the Oklahoma Constitution, the court vacated a judgment of the court of appeals, which had held the clause was unconstitutional, and remanded to the trial court. In finding that the clause had not violated the Oklahoma Constitution, the court held that with the limited scope of review provided by the Oklahoma Uniform Arbitration Act, the clause was sufficient to pass constitutional muster.

Cruse v. Bd. of County Comm'rs


No. 81,733


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK 143; 910 P.2d 998; 1995 Okla. LEXIS 164; 66 O.B.A.J. 4005



December 19, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] ON CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEALS, DIVISION III.



DISPOSITION: CERTIORARI PREVIOUSLY GRANTED; OPINION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS VACATED; JUDGMENT OF THE TRIAL COURT REVERSED; CAUSE REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, injured party and wife, sought review of a judgment of the Oklahoma Court of Appeals, which affirmed the district court's dismissal of the injured party's governmental tort claims action against appellee county board (Board). In affirming the district court's decision, the appellate court relied upon Okla. Stat. tit. 51, §§ 157, 170 (1991) of the Governmental Tort Claims Act (Act), Okla. Stat. tit. 51, § 151 et seq. (1991).


OVERVIEW: The injured party timely filed a governmental tort claims action against the Board, alleging that the Board failed to maintain the road and warn drivers of the washout, resulting in his injury. After dismissing his action, the injured party refiled the action two years later. The Board moved to dismiss, claiming that the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction because the refiled action was not filed within 180 days after the claim was deemed denied under Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 157 (1991). The injured party argued that the right to maintain his action was preserved upon timely compliance with the provisions of Okla. Stat. tit. 51, §§ 156, 157 (1991); that Okla. Stat. tit. 51, § 164 (1991) expressly subjected a timely filed governmental tort claims action to all Oklahoma civil procedure law; and that the Act did not expressly preclude application of Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 100 (1991) to allow refiling. The court held that Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 100 (1991) operated to allow the refiling of a timely filed governmental tort claims action within one year from the date the governmental tort claims action failed other than on its merits. Thus, the injured party's claim was timely.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the judgment of the appellate court and remanded the cause to the district court to determine whether the action was barred by the sovereign immunity exemption of the Governmental Tort Claims Act.

 

48 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Overton v. Gambill (In re Estate of Mae Little Bear)


No. 77,005


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK 134; 909 P.2d 42; 1995 Okla. LEXIS 154; 66 O.B.A.J. 3827



December 5, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEALS, DIVISION 1. APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OSAGE COUNTY, STATE OF OKLAHOMA. Honorable William H. Mattingly, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: CERTIORARI PREVIOUSLY GRANTED; COURT OF APPEALS' OPINION VACATED; TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Osage Indians challenged the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Oklahoma), which determined heirship and ordered a distribution of assets to appellee nephews from the estate of a decedent, who was an heir to an Osage Indian by marriage, but was not of Indian blood and was Caucasian. The case concerned the interpretation of the Osage Tribe of Indians Technical Corrections Act of 1984 (1984 Act), 98 U.S.C.S. § 3163.


OVERVIEW: The nephews were non-Indian as well. The Osage Indians objected to the distribution on the ground that the decedent's devise of her headright interest to the non-Indian nephews violated the 1984 Act and other relevant federal laws. The court interpreted the 1984 act, by examining its legislative history and other relevant acts, and determined that the 1984 Act did not limit a devise of a headright by a non-Indian testator, such as the decedent in the case, to a non-Indian devisee, to a life estate. The court vacated the appellate court decision and upheld the judgment of the trial court ordering the devise of the decedent's 1.25 headright interest to the nephews. The court determined that no Congressional intent existed in the 1984 Act to prohibit a non-Indian, such as the nephews, from receiving more than a life estate when the headright interest involved was devised by the will of a non-Indian, like the decedent, who lawfully owned the full beneficial interest in the headright at the time of death.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the decision of the appellate court and ordered that the judgment of the trial court devising the decedent's headright interest to the nephews was upheld.

 

49 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


R.R. Tway, Inc. v. Okla. Tax Comm'n


NO. 82,725


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK 129; 910 P.2d 972; 1995 Okla. LEXIS 147



November 21, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE OKLAHOMA TAX COMMISSION.



DISPOSITION: COMMISSION ORDER AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant construction contractor sought review of the judgment of appellee Oklahoma Tax Commission (Oklahoma), which granted the contractor's requested refund of state sales tax, but declined to refund any Oklahoma County sales tax. The Commission also refused to allow the county to be joined as a party in the refund proceeding.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court found that Okla. Stat. art. 68, § 1354 (1992) did not give the Commission the authority to compel an appearance of the county or issue orders requiring the county to make payments on tax refunds. The court found that the Legislature has not expressly given to taxpayers the remedy of compelling the appearance of counties and municipalities in refund and protest proceedings before the Commission where a taxpayer seeks a refund from local taxes. The court reasoned that the Legislature expressly gave to the Commission the authority to withhold certain local sales taxes for refunds but did not expressly give to the Commission the authority to withhold § 1354(1)(T) local sales taxes. The court rejected the contractor's request to judicially create a remedy for taxpayers in proceedings before the Commission adjudicating a refund. The court found that the timeliness of the contractor's application did not meet the express language of when an application for refund may be filed. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and declined to determine whether Okla. Stat. art. 62 § 365.1 (1991) to the county's argument.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Commission's order on all parts.

 

50 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


McMillian v. Holcomb


NO. 82,999


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK 117; 907 P.2d 1034; 1995 Okla. LEXIS 137; 66 O.B.A.J. 3471



October 31, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TULSA COUNTY.



DISPOSITION: MOTIONS TO DISMISS APPEAL DENIED; APPEAL SHALL PROCEED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant neighbors sought review of a decision of the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which entered judgment in favor of plaintiff landowners in the landowners' action that was brought to condemn an easement of necessity. The landowners filed a motion to dismiss the appeal.


OVERVIEW: The first issue on appeal was whether an order filed by the trial court that rendered judgment in favor of the landowners and directed the landowners' attorney to prepare a journal entry commenced the appellate clock. The court held that that order did not commence appeal time. The journal entry filed 15 days later commenced the time. The court noted that the neighbors had filed a premature motion for a new trial when a motion to reconsider and to vacate the original order was filed before the journal entry had been filed. A premature motion had the same effect as one filed too late. However, the court concluded that the neighbors' motion extended their time to appeal. The court also decided that the appeal was timely commenced by the amended petition in error filed three months later. The landowners argued that the appeal should have been dismissed because the neighbors cashed the court clerk's check representing the amount of a commissioners award granted by the order of the trial court. The court refused to penalize the neighbors for depositing the check when they did not make an application for payment. Therefore, the neighbors were allowed to proceed with their appeal.


OUTCOME: The court denied the landowners' motion to dismiss the appeal and ordered the appeal to proceed.

 

51 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


David V.R. v. Wanda J.D.


No. 80,280


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK 111; 907 P.2d 1025; 1995 Okla. LEXIS 130; 66 O.B.A.J. 3289



October 17, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Counsel Amended October 31, 1995.



DISPOSITION: CERTIORARI PREVIOUSLY GRANTED; COURT OF APPEALS OPINION VACATED; TRIAL COURT'S GRANTING OF SUMMARY JUDGMENT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The matter before the court was the writ of certiorari granted by the appellate court (Oklahoma), which vacated the trial court's grant of summary judgment to appellee father on appellant putative father's paternity action. The appellate court found that the irrebutable presumption of the father's paternity, because the child was born during the father's marriage to the mother, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The putative father had filed an action to determine the paternity of a child, claiming that the child was the result of an extramarital affair he had with the mother. The trial court had granted summary judgment to the father, concluding that there was an irrebutable presumption in the father's favor because the child was born during the marriage with the mother. The appellate court had vacated the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the father, finding the irrebutable presumption of paternity was unconstitutional because it deprived the putative father's due process rights to paternity. On appeal again, the court held that the putative father was barred by Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 3 (1991) for disputing the presumption of legitimacy because his claim was not timely brought. Finally, the court did not find any due process violations because the right to prove paternity was not a constitutionally protected interest, but was a legislative question to be determined by each state. The court concluded that the trial court was correct in granting summary judgment to the father.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the writ of certiorari that was granted by the appellate court. The court reinstated the trial court's judgment that granted summary judgment to the father on the putative father's paternity action. The court did not find that the irrebutable presumption of the father's paternity, because the child was born during the father's marriage to the mother, was unconstitutional.

City of Oklahoma City v. State ex rel. Oklahoma DOL


NO. 85,888


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


918 P.2d 26; 1995 Okla. LEXIS 118; 66 O.B.A.J. 3184; 2 Wage & Hour Cas. 2d (BNA) 1615; 130 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P58,007



October 10, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [**1] As Corrected October 13, 1995. Supplemental Opinion on Rehearing of May 14, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Okla. LEXIS 104.


PRIOR HISTORY: APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. Honorable James B. Blevins, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the Oklahoma Department of Labor, appealed a judgment from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) that, in a declaratory judgment action brought by plaintiffs, the City of Oklahoma City and its four trust funds, granted plaintiffs' summary judgment and declared unconstitutional Oklahoma's Minimum Wages on Public Works Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 40, §§ 196.1- 196.14 (1991).


OVERVIEW: Concerned with dramatic increases in the prevailing wage, the City requested that the state's labor commissioner review the wage determinations. The commissioner responded that, pursuant to the Act, the determinations were made by the United States Department of Labor and that she had no statutory authority to investigate errors on inaccuracies in the federal determinations. The City and the funds filed an action for injunctive relief against enforcement of the Act and a determination that the Act was unconstitutional. The trial court ruled that the Act was unconstitutional without articulating the bases upon which the Act was constitutionally infirm. On appeal, pursuant to the accelerated procedures found in Okla. R. Appealed. P. 1.203, Okla. Stat. tit. 12, ch. 15, app. 2 (Supp. 1994), the court ruled that the Act violated Okla. Const. art. IV, § 1, and art. V, § 1. Specifically, the Act delegated the power to determine prevailing wages to a department of the federal government without setting standards for the exercise of that determination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

City of Bethany v. Public Employees Relations Bd. of State of Okla.


No. 81,003


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK 99; 904 P.2d 604; 1995 Okla. LEXIS 114; 66 O.B.A.J. 3071; 151 L.R.R.M. 2138



October 3, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal From the District Court of Oklahoma County. Honorable Charles L. Owens, District Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged a decision from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which affirmed a reviewing board's decision in appellee firefighter union's unfair labor practice charge that the city committed an unfair labor practice by proposing and insisting upon illegal bargaining proposals and which determined that Okla. Stat. tit. 11, § 51-111 (1985), of the Fire and Police Arbitration Act (Act) was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: The city and the union were negotiating a collective bargaining agreement. The city proposed that certain issues would not be subject to arbitration under the new agreement. The union declared an impasse because every item of the agreement had to be arbitrable under § 51-111. The union filed an unfair labor practice charge against the city. An administrative board held that the city committed an unfair labor practice. The city challenged the decision and the constitutionality of § 51-111. The district court affirmed and upheld the constitutionality of § 51-111. The court affirmed. The court held that § 51-111 permitted the parties to negotiate over the exclusion of certain substantive issues from the collective bargaining agreement. Once terms were included in the collective bargaining agreement, however, they had to be subject to grievance arbitration. The court held that the city violated its duty to bargain in good faith when it asserted a position that would have required the union to agree to terms contrary to those mandated by § 51-111. The court held that § 51-111 did not violate the Oklahoma Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that the city committed an unfair labor practice and that mandatory arbitration under the Act was constitutional.

Hergenreder v. Madden (In re Adoption of J.R.M.)


No. 82,274


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK 79; 899 P.2d 1155; 1995 Okla. LEXIS 101; 66 O.B.A.J. 2400



July 18, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEALS, DIVISION III. Honorable Charles Kelley, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: CERTIORARI PREVIOUSLY GRANTED; COURT OF APPEALS OPINION VACATED; TRIAL COURT AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART; CAUSE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father filed a petition for certiorari relief challenging an order from the Court of Appeals, Division III (Oklahoma), which affirmed a decision granting appellee adoptive parents' petition to adopt the father's child.


OVERVIEW: The mother and the father were married and had one child. The couple divorced, and the mother was awarded custody of the child. The father paid child support, but ceased such payments after he lost his job. The adoptive parents filed a petition to adopt the child without the father's consent, alleging that consent was unnecessary because the father had not provided court ordered support during the previous year. Without notice to the father, the trial court entered a final decree of adoption terminating the father's parental rights. The appellate court affirmed. The father then initiated an action for certiorari relief. In affirming the trial court's decision in part, the court found that there was clear and convincing evidence of the father's wilful failure to pay support. The evidence established that the father lost his job due to illegal drug activities. In reversing the decision in part and remanding, the court found that the father was deprived of a constitutionally protected right when his parental rights were terminated without notice of the adoption proceeding.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the appellate court's opinion. The court affirmed that portion of the trial court's decision, which held that there was clear and convincing evidence of the father's failure to support the child. The court reversed that portion of the trial court's decision, which held that the father's parental rights could be terminated without notice based upon the non-support finding, and remanded for further proceedings.

In re Initiative Petition No. 362 State Question 669


No. 84,769


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK 77; 899 P.2d 1145; 1995 Okla. LEXIS 93; 66 O.B.A.J. 2313



July 11, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL OF BALLOT TITLE AND PROTEST TO INITIATIVE PETITION NO. 362, STATE QUESTION 669.



DISPOSITION: THE BALLOT TITLE IS DEFICIENT AND A SUBSTITUTE SHALL BE PRINTED ON THE BALLOTS. INITIATIVE PETITION NO. 362, STATE QUESTION 669, IS LEGALLY SUFFICIENT AND SHALL BE SUBMITTED TO THE PEOPLE OF THE STATE OF OKLAHOMA FOR A VOTE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Proponent citizens and some protestant citizens appealed from the attorney general's wording of the ballot title for an initiative petition. Further, protestants claimed that, if passed, the initiative would have been unconstitutional. The initiative would have amended the constitution to limit the dollar amount of ad valorem taxes payable on real property and change the manner in which such taxes could have been increased.


OVERVIEW: The attorney general approved wording for a ballot initiative to amend the constitution with respect to ad valorem taxes on real property and methods for increasing taxes. Both parties challenged the wording of the initiative. The court found the ballot title deficient and corrected the wording pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 34, § 10.A (1991). The proposed amendment stated that any ad valorem tax increase must have been approved by "not less than 60 percent of the qualified electors of an assessing jurisdiction." The court noted that the title led voters to believe that 60 percent of all registered voters in an assessing jurisdiction had to approve any ad valorem tax increase, whether or not they voted. The court also employed the language "general election," which, pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 26, § 1-101 (1991), was held on the first Tuesday succeeding the first Monday of November. The court also found that the gist of the initiative satisfied Okla. Stat. tit. 34, § 3 (Supp. 1992) because it explained that the proposition would have limited annual increases in property taxes, established a vote of the people to increase them, and defined procedures for increasing them.


OUTCOME: The court corrected the language used in the ballot initiative. The court also held that the initiative petition was legally sufficient and was to have been submitted to the people for a vote.

 

56 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Unit Petroleum Co. v. Okla. Water Res. Bd.


No. 81,030


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK 73; 898 P.2d 1275; 1995 Okla. LEXIS 87; 66 O.B.A.J. 2221



July 5, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEALS, DIVISION 1.



DISPOSITION: CERTIORARI PREVIOUSLY GRANTED, COURT OF APPEALS OPINION VACATED, TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT REVERSED AND REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mineral owner sought review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Oklahoma) affirming the trial court's decision that appellee Oklahoma Water Resources Board correctly interpreted Okla. Stat. tit. 82, § 1020.11.D (1991) in denying the mineral owner a permit to use water underlying the property.


OVERVIEW: The mineral owner sought a permit from the Board to use water underlying the property to explore for oil and gas. The Board denied the application on the ground that § 1020.11.D prohibited it from doing so unless the mineral owner first obtained a water lease from the surface owner. Reversing, the court held that the trial court erred in applying § 1020.11.D prospectively to mineral lessees, but not to owners of severed minerals. The Legislature could make a mineral owner's right to water subject to the sole discretion of the surface owner, but only if the operation of the statute was prospective. The distinction between mineral owners and mineral lessees drawn by the trial court was discriminatory, and § 1020.11.D had to be applied equally to both. The court further held that § 1020.11.D had to be interpreted as applying prospectively only in order to be constitutional. A severed mineral interest was a "vested right," which could not be taken away except by legislation that was effective prospectively. Thus, owners of severed mineral rights acquired before May 28, 1985 had vested water rights with respect to oil and gas operations.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the appellate court's judgment and reversed and remanded the trial court's judgment, ordering the trial court to issue a declaratory judgment ordering the Board to apply § 1020.11.D prospectively only.

Okla. Empl. Sec. Comm'n v. Carter


No. 85,465


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK 74; 903 P.2d 868; 1995 Okla. LEXIS 89; 66 O.B.A.J. 2223



July 5, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]  [*P0] Oklahoma Employment Security Commission denied benefits to Lori Earls and the appeal tribunal affirmed. Earls appealed to the Board of Review which also denied benefits. In her petition for review to district court, Earls failed to name the Oklahoma Employment Security Commission as a party, and Commission specially appeared and moved to dismiss on grounds that trial court lacked jurisdiction for failure to include all necessary parties required by 40 O.S. 1991 § 2-160. Trial judge denied the objection to jurisdiction and granted Earls ten days to amend her petition to add Commission as a party. Commission has filed application to assume original jurisdiction and petition for writ of prohibition. We assume original jurisdiction and prohibit Respondent from proceeding further in the cause.



DISPOSITION: ORIGINAL JURISDICTION ASSUMED. WRIT ISSUED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Oklahoma Employment Security Commission filed a petition for a writ of prohibition wherein it sought to prohibit respondent district court from proceeding further in an appeal of a denial of unemployment benefits filed by real party in interest claimant.


OVERVIEW: The claimant appealed the Commission's denial of her application for unemployment benefits to an appeal tribunal. After the tribunal affirmed the denial, she appealed to the Commission's Board of Review. It also affirmed the denial of benefits and the claimant filed a petition seeking judicial review in the district court. The Commission objected to jurisdiction because it was not named as a defendant as required by Okla. Stat. tit. 40, § 2-610 (1991). The district court granted the claimant's subsequent application for leave to name the Commission as a party to the appeal. The Commission filed the instant prohibition proceeding to preclude the district court from proceeding further on the claimant's appeal. The court held that § 2-610 required that the Commission be named a codefendant in petitions for judicial review of denials of unemployment benefits. It further held that when the 10 day appeal period provided by § 2-610 had run without all necessary parties being named, the district court was without jurisdiction to hear the appeal. The court held that the district court exceeded its jurisdiction because the 10 day appeal period had expired and it could not be waived.


OUTCOME: The court issued a writ of prohibition and restrained the district court from proceeding further on the claimant's petition for review of the denial of her application for unemployment benefits.

In re C.J.S.


NO. 82,618


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK 70; 903 P.2d 304; 1995 Okla. LEXIS 82



June 27, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CERTIORARI TO THE OKLAHOMA COURT OF APPEALS, DIVISION II. Honorable David E. Winslow, Judge of the District Court of Tulsa County.



DISPOSITION: CERTIORARI PREVIOUSLY GRANTED; COURT OF APPEALS OPINION VACATED; JUDGMENT OF TRIAL COURT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged a judgment of the Oklahoma Court of Appeals, Division II, which upheld adoption proceedings as to the biological mother's daughter, but reversed and remanded for further proceedings with regard to twins.


OVERVIEW: The biological mother claimed that she did not know who the father of her daughter was, but that appellant father was the father of the twins. The trial court, in adoption proceedings in which the biological mother consented, sent notice to the biological mother's ex-husband and published notice without specifically naming the father. The trial court approved the adoptions. The appeals court reversed as to the twines on the ground that publication notice to the father was faulty. Affirming the trial court's judgment, the court held that the father was not within the group of persons entitled to notice as he had not been adjudicated as the children's father, was not openly living with or married to the mother, was not listed on the birth certificate as the father, and did not hold himself out as the father at the time the proceedings were initiated. The court found that the publication notice was, therefore, not required and any defect therein was immaterial.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the appeals court's judgment and affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Muskogee Urban Renewal Auth. v. Excise Bd. of Muskogee County


No. 74,424


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK 67; 899 P.2d 624; 1995 Okla. LEXIS 85; 66 O.B.A.J. 2124



June 27, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] ON APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT IN MUSKOGEE COUNTY, THE HONORABLE BRUCE SEWELL, DISTRICT JUDGE.

Original Opinion of June 15, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Okla. LEXIS 102.



DISPOSITION: TRIAL COURT WRIT OF MANDAMUS IS DISSOLVED; TRIAL COURT JUDGMENT REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a city and its urban renewal authority, sought declaratory judgment and a writ of mandamus directing defendant county excise board to apportion ad valorem tax millage to the city for payment of a 30-year bond. The District Court in Muskogee County (Oklahoma) issued the writ and granted a money judgment to the urban renewal authority. The excise board appealed.


OVERVIEW: The urban renewal plan was amended to provide an urban renewal project for the rehabilitation of a hotel building and clearance and demolition of surrounding property. The city included the hotel project as an item in its estimate of need or budget, and the excise board refused to apportion ad valorem tax millage to the city. The court held that the city was not entitled to revenues generated by a tax levied outside the city's territorial boundaries and that the duties of the excise board to calculate and apportion the millage to be levied on behalf of the city did not extend the city's taxation boundaries to include county-wide taxable property. The legislature could not direct apportionment of ad valorem tax revenues for payment of a long-term debt for urban renewal if the voters had not approved the debt. Thus, the matter had to be remanded to the district court for a determination of whether the city had become indebted in an amount exceeding the income and revenue provided for such year without first receiving the assent of three-fifths of the voters of the city. Legislation authorizing tax increment financing was constitutional and did not usurp power of the excise board.


OUTCOME: The court dissolved the writ of mandamus and reversed and remanded the action to the district court to decide the issue of whether the city had become indebted to an amount in excess of the income and revenue for the year in question.

Okla. Ass'n for Equitable Taxation v. City of Okla. City


No. 85,287


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK 62; 901 P.2d 800; 1995 Okla. LEXIS 78; 66 O.B.A.J. 2037



June 20, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. Honorable Carolyn Ricks, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff association appealed a decision from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) entering judgment in favor of defendant, the City of Oklahoma City, in the association's declaratory judgment action. The association's action challenged the validity of Oklahoma City, Okla., Ordinance No. 20,045, § 52-20.3(F) (1993).


OVERVIEW: The City passed the ordinance, which levied an additional one percent excise tax on the gross proceeds or gross receipts derived from all taxable sales. Section 52-20.3(F) of the ordinance was a refund provision that granted City residents over the age of 65 the right to a refund of all or a part of the sales tax paid by them during a calendar year up to $ 32 per person. The association claimed that the refund provision violated the uniformity requirement of Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 2701 (1991) and equal protection principles. The association initiated an action and the trial court entered judgment for the City. In affirming the decision, the court found that the City could create classes of taxpayers pursuant to § 2701. The language of § 2701 demonstrated a legislative intent to allow municipalities to create classes of taxpayers. The refund provision did not violate equal protection principles because policies favoring retirement-age senior citizens are recognized as legitimate. The provision was established to provide senior citizens, whose income may be lower than younger taxpayers, some tax relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

61 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Taylor v. State & Educ. Emples. Growp Ins. Program


No. 82,609


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK 51; 897 P.2d 275; 1995 Okla. LEXIS 65; 66 O.B.A.J. 1835



May 23, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY, OKLAHOMA, HONORABLE CAROLYN R. RICKS, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: DISTRICT COURT JUDGMENT AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school district employees sought review of a judgment of the District court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which granted a motion for summary judgment filed by appellee state officials who were responsible for administration of the State and Education Employees Group Insurance Act, 1988 Okla. Sess. Laws ch. 165, § 1 et seq. Appellants were members of a competing plan and they argued that the act was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Appellants objected to transfer of pension funds under the State and Education Employees Group Insurance Act in that the funds were in the nature of trust funds, which constituted a part of the compensation for services previously rendered to the public. Appellants contended that such transfer violated Okla. Const. art. V, §§ 51, 62 and art. X, §§ 14, 15. The court held that the transfer satisfied constitutional requirements. A statute that transferred public moneys from one legislatively created fund to another had nothing to do with equality and uniformity of payments from public funds according to duration of service and remuneration. The fund created by the transfer was neither given away nor spent. Moreover, even though the retirement funds were trust funds that established contractually based pension rights in the beneficiaries, the legislature was permitted to modify such arrangements provided that the modifications were reasonable, necessary and that the disadvantages of modification were offset by advantages created. Furthermore, the law satisfied the requirement that the actuarial soundness of the fund was not impaired nor were vested rights detrimentally affected.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's grant of appellees' motion for summary judgment.

Herring v. Okla. ex rel. Okla. Tax Comm'n


No. 83,380


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK 28; 894 P.2d 1074; 1995 Okla. LEXIS 37; 66 O.B.A.J. 1107



March 28, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. Honorable Bryan Dixon.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed an order from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which granted summary judgment in favor of defendants, a special indemnity fund and other state agencies, in a worker's compensation action that alleged the unconstitutionality of Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 173(J) (Supp. 1993). The employee contended that the amendment to the statute impermissibly impaired his vested rights by diverting moneys from the fund.


OVERVIEW: On February 2, 1993, the employee was awarded workers' compensation benefits against the fund. The employee attempted to collect but, because of insufficient resources in the fund's account, he did not receive payment for the award until March 20, 1994. At the time of the injury, the tax commission collected a percentage of total disability payments from workers' compensation insurers under Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 173(J) (1991), and the entire amount collected was credited to the fund. Section 173(J) was amended in 1993 to provide that 10 percent of the amount collected for the fund would be credited to other state agencies. The employee filed suit, contesting the constitutionality of the amendment. The employee argued that the amendment impermissibly impaired his vested rights by diverting moneys from the fund. The trial court granted summary judgment in favor of defendants. The employee appealed, and the court affirmed. The court held that the evidence showed that the amendment did not cause any delay in the employee being compensated. The employee failed to show that he suffered any injury resulting from the amendment and, therefore, lacked standing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Chambers v. City of Ada


No. 78,629 (Consolidated with 78,767, 78,768, 78,770, 78,771 and 78,772)


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK 24; 894 P.2d 1068; 1995 Okla. LEXIS 35; 66 O.B.A.J. 1116



March 21, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF PONTOTOC COUNTY, OKLAHOMA. HONORABLE G. C. MAYHUE, TRIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: ORDER OF THE DISTRICT COURT REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal, plaintiff landowners challenged separate orders from the District Court of Pontotoc County (Oklahoma) that dismissed the landowners' suits against defendant, the City of Ada, in which the landowners sought to recover damages for loss of value to their homes, under the Oklahoma Solid Waste Management Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 63, § 2251 et seq. (Supp. 1987), recodified at Okla. Stat. tit. 27A, § 2-10-101 et seq. (Supp. 1993).


OVERVIEW: The state department of health issued the City a permit to operate a landfill adjacent to the landowners' properties. The landowners and others filed an administrative appeal in the district court, seeking review of the permit issuance proceedings. That action was dismissed and the landowners filed suits for damages. On appeal, the court ruled, inter alia, that the district court erred by: (1) finding that the landowners' were collaterally estopped by the administrative proceeding from alleging that they occupied residences located within 500 yards of a landfill site, a prerequisite to a suit under Okla. Stat. tit. 63, § 2258. The issue as to the location of their residences was never raised by the parties or their privies nor addressed and ruled on by a court; (2) ruling that the issuance of the permit did not cause the landowners any cognizable damages. The issuance of the permit was immaterial to the landowners' suits for damages; and (3) ruling that the Act was unconstitutional because it diverted municipal revenues to assist in funding the state service of issuing permits, as prohibited by Okla. Const. art. 10, §9. The Act required the City to pay for damages, not for permits.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's orders and remanded the cause.

 

64 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Williams Natural Gas Co. v. State Bd. of Equalization


No. 84,097


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK 150; 891 P.2d 1219; 1994 Okla. LEXIS 173; 65 O.B.A.J. 4201



December 20, 1994, FILED



DISPOSITION:  [***1] ORIGINAL JURISDICTION ASSUMED; PETITION FOR WRIT OF PROHIBITION DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, public service corporations, asked the court to assume original jurisdiction and requested a writ prohibiting respondent State Board of Equalization from assessing their public service corporation property at a greater ratio than that applied to public service property owned by railroads and airlines. The Oklahoma Tax Commission was also made a respondent.


OVERVIEW: The Board adopted an assessment ratio of 12.08 percent for airline and railroad property and a ratio of 22.85 percent for corporate property. Petitioners claimed that the assessments violated the Equal Protection Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment, violated Okla. Const. art. X, § 5, which required uniform taxation within a tax class, and violated the Ad Valorem Tax Code, Okla. Stat. tit. 68, §§ 2801-3152 (1991), which required uniform treatment in ad valorem taxation. The court assumed original jurisdiction. In denying the petition for writ of prohibition, the court found that the Board's assessments did not violate the Equal Protection Clause. A separate tax class had been created for railroads and airlines and the classifications created were rational and furthered a legitimate state interest. Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 2864(C) was enacted to bring Oklahoma's ad valorem taxing scheme into compliance with federal laws that gave special protection to railroads and airlines. Compliance with federal law achieved by legislative creation of a tax subclass did not violate the Equal Protection Clause.


OUTCOME: The court assumed original jurisdiction and denied the petition for writ of prohibition.

 

65 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


ANDERSON v. EICHNER


No. 79,517 cons. w/79,507


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK 136; 890 P.2d 1329; 1994 Okla. LEXIS 154; 65 O.B.A.J. 4037



December 6, 1994, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] ON APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT, OKLAHOMA COUNTY. Virgil C. Black, Judge, in No. 79,507. Niles L. Jackson, Judge, in No. 79,517.



DISPOSITION: THE TRIAL COURT'S SUMMARY JUDGMENTS IN NO. 79,507 AND NO. 79,517 ARE REVERSED AND THE CAUSES REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS NOT INCONSISTENT WITH THIS PRONOUNCEMENT


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, survivors of patients, appealed judgments from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which granted summary judgment to defendants, physician teachers and students, in the survivors' claims for wrongful death resulting from the alleged medical malpractice of the physician teachers and students, brought under the Governmental Tort Claims Act (Act), Okla. Stat. tit. 51, § 151 et seq. (1991).


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court reversed the summary judgment award, concluding that the Act specifically omitted physician teachers and students who were engaged in the practice of medicine from state immunity to tort claims. The actions of the physician teachers and students were protected by the Act when they were acting within the scope of their employment under Okla. Stat. tit. 51, § 152(5) (1986). The scope of their protected actions was when they were engaged in administrative or teaching duties. The practice of medicine was specifically excepted under § 152(5), even though they may have been engaged as a teacher or a student at the time. The legislature had created a dichotomy based on the specific acts in which the physician teachers or students were engaged. Under rational basis scrutiny, the court held it was not violative of the Equal Protection Clause to hold physician teachers and students potentially totally liable up to the statutory cap under the principles of general tort law. The court held that the legislative choice to treat physician teachers and patients differently from other government employees was based on a legitimate state interest.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment award to physician teachers and students, holding that the state immunity of the Governmental Tort Claims Act did not encompass the activities of the practice of medicine or the providing of treatment to patients.

Sharp v. Tulsa County Election Bd.


NO. 82,903


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


890 P.2d 836; 1994 Okla. LEXIS 119; 65 O.B.A.J. 3055



September 20, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected January 31, 1995. Rehearing Granted January 31, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Okla. LEXIS 6. Supplemental Opinion On Rehearing of January 31, 1995, Reported at: 890 P.2d 836 at 846.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] APPLICATION FOR EXTRAORDINARY RELIEF



DISPOSITION: We vacate the writ, and allow petitioner to resign his seat on the board within thirty days to avoid penalties set forth by Section 5-113.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner candidate filed an action for a writ of mandamus requiring respondent county election board to place the candidate's name on the school board ballot. The court issued the writ so as to allow the candidate's name to remain on the ballot, but reversed its opinion on the merits of the case.


OVERVIEW: The candidate's name had been removed from the ballot by the election board. The candidate was prohibited from running in the election under Okla. Stat. tit. 70, § 5-113 because his wife was a teacher in the school district. The court initially issued a writ to allow the candidate's name to remain on the ballot until the merits of the case could be decided. After reviewing the merits of the case, the court vacated the writ and upheld the action of the election board. The court held that § 5-113 specifically prohibited family members of school district employees to be candidates for school board. Because his wife was a teacher, the candidate was ineligible for school board candidacy. The court also concluded that § 5-113 was constitutional. The state's interest in avoiding conflicts of interest, favoritism, and the appearance of favoritism was sufficient to uphold the legitimate regulation of candidacy for the school board. The school held that the right to participate in the political process as a candidate was neither an absolute nor fundamental right, but and was subject to impose reasonable, non-discriminatory regulations.


OUTCOME: The court vacated its previously granted writ of mandamus and upheld the action of the election board.

FAIR v. STATE ELECTION BOARD

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, a legislator and a voter, sought a writ of mandamus against respondent state election board to annul a board ruling that found that the legislator was prohibited from being a qualified candidate for the office of Oklahoma Labor Commissioner.

OUTCOME: The court denied the writ.

In re INITIATIVE PETITION NO. 360


No. 82,648


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK 97; 879 P.2d 810; 1994 Okla. LEXIS 115; 65 O.B.A.J. 2546



July 19, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] ORIGINAL PROCEEDING TO DETERMINE THE VALIDITY OF INITIATIVE PETITION NO. 360, STATE QUESTION NO. 662 AND APPEAL ON BALLOT TITLE SUBMITTED BY ATTORNEY GENERAL.



DISPOSITION: INITIATIVE PETITION NO. 360 IS DECLARED LEGALLY SUFFICIENT FOR SUBMISSION TO THE PEOPLE OF OKLAHOMA; BALLOT TITLE PREPARED BY ATTORNEY GENERAL DECLARED LEGALLY DEFICIENT AND IT IS AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Protestants, a citizen of Oklahoma and an association, filed an original action brought pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 34 § 8 (Supp. 1992), which challenged the legal sufficiency of an initiative petition. Pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 34 § 10 (1991), appellants, an individual and a corporation, challenged the ballot title prepared by appellee Oklahoma Attorney General. Appellants on the title issue were proponents of the initiative petition.


OVERVIEW: The initiative petition sought to amend Okla. Const. art. 2 by adding a new section. Two general issues were before the court concerning the proposal: the legal sufficiency or facial constitutionality of the proposal under both the Oklahoma and United States Constitutions, and the propriety of the ballot title prepared by the Oklahoma Attorney General. The court was unconvinced both that the constitutional infirmities asserted by protestants were clear or manifest, or that reaching the merits of those challenges would have prevented the holding of a costly and unnecessary election. Accordingly, the court declined to reach the constitutional challenges lodged by protestants. The court held that protestants failed to establish that the proposed initiative was violative of the one general subject rule under Okla. Const. art. 24, § 1. The objective of the initiative was clearly term limitations for Congressional delegates. Proponents asserted that the ballot title prepared by the Attorney General, in various particulars, violated Okla. Stat. tit. 34 § 9(B)(2)-(5) (1991). The court held that the ballot title was legally deficient because it was argumentative and amended the title.


OUTCOME: The court declared the initiative petition sufficient for submission to a vote of the people of the State of Oklahoma. The ballot title submitted by the Attorney General was declared legally deficient and was amended by the court.

 

69 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


PRIVATE TRUCK COUNCIL, INC. v. OKLAHOMA TAX COMMN.


No. 68,401


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK 96; 879 P.2d 137; 1994 Okla. LEXIS 113; 65 O.B.A.J. 2539



July 19, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] ON REMAND FROM THE UNITED STATES SUPREME COURT



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENT REINSTATED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action by plaintiffs, a transportation company, an industry council, and an individual, against defendants, the Oklahoma Tax Commission and others, the trial court held that plaintiffs could not seek a tax refund and other relief under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 for a violation of the Commerce Clause, and the court affirmed. The United States Supreme Court vacated the judgment and remanded the matter to the court for further consideration.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed suit under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 alleging that two state taxation statutes, Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 607.1 (Supp. 1982) and Okla. Stat. tit. 47, § 1120(K) (Supp. 1986), violated the Interstate Commerce and Privileges and Immunities Clauses of the United States Constitution. They sought declaratory and injunctive relief, attorneys' fees, and a refund of all taxes paid pursuant to the statutes. On appeal, the court determined that the statutes violated the Interstate Commerce Clause. However, the court determined that plaintiffs could not seek relief under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. In another case, the U.S. Supreme Court held that a party could seek relief under § 1983 for a violation of the Commerce Clause. The Supreme Court remanded the matter to the court for reconsideration in light of its decision. On remand, the court held that under principles of comity, plaintiffs could not seek relief under § 1983, or attorney fees under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988, in state court because they had an adequate state law remedy and, therefore, a federal court would have been prohibited from granting the requested federal relief under the Tax Injunction Act, 28 U.S.C.S. § 1341.


OUTCOME: The court reinstated the judgment of the trial court.

STALLINGS v. OKLAHOMA TAX COMM'N


No. 73,769


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK 99; 880 P.2d 912; 1994 Okla. LEXIS 114; 65 O.B.A.J. 2532



July 19, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected July 21, 1994.


PRIOR HISTORY: CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEALS, DIVISION III



DISPOSITION: CERTIORARI PREVIOUSLY GRANTED. OPINION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS VACATED. JUDGMENT OF THE DISTRICT COURT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employees, retired from federal civil service, filed an action against appellee Oklahoma Tax Commission, pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 226 (1981), seeking a refund of the state income taxes voluntarily paid on their federal employee retirement benefits. The Oklahoma Court of Appeals, Division III, reversed the district court's judgment, which dismissed the action for the lack of jurisdiction. The Commission was granted certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The employees voluntarily paid state income taxes on their federal employee retirement benefits. They later sought a refund of those taxes on the basis that the taxes were collected in violation of constitutional equal protection and 4 U.S.C.S § 111 because their federal retirement benefits were taxed at a discriminatorily higher rate than the retirement benefits of state and local government employees. On certiorari, the court held that under Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 226 (1981), the district court properly dismissed the employees' action for the lack of subject matter jurisdiction. The court explained that although § 226 contained no exhaustion requirement, before the employees were permitted to file a tax refund suit in the district court pursuant to § 226, they were jurisdictionally required to first pay the taxes under protest and at the time of payment give notice of their intent to file suit. Having failed to meet these provisions, their action was properly dismissed. The court reasoned that the action's dismissal did not offend federal due process because the state had provided a sufficient statutory remedy for challenging the tax.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the appellate court's opinion and affirmed the district court's judgment.

DUNCAN MED. SERVS. v. STATE ex rel. OKLAHOMA TAX COMM'N


No. 76,240


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK 91; 911 P.2d 247; 1994 Okla. LEXIS 110; 65 O.B.A.J. 2510



July 19, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected May 16, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] ON CERTIORARI TO THE COURT OF APPEALS, DIVISION I



DISPOSITION: CERTIORARI PREVIOUSLY GRANTED; OPINION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS VACATED; OKLAHOMA TAX COMMISSION ORDER NO. 90-08-07-020 REVERSED AND REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of a decision by the Court of Appeals, Division I (Oklahoma), which vacated the order by appellee, Oklahoma Tax Commission (OTC), regarding a tax assessment and concluded that Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 1366 (1981) violated Okla. Const. art. 10, § 5. The appellate court also determined that the rental or sale of oxygen concentrators by the taxpayer was exempted from the sales tax levy.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer recorded its daily sales of medical equipment in a monthly journal. The taxpayer participated in the Medicare program, and it reduced the gross receipts reported for sales tax purposes in order to recover sales taxes that it had paid. The taxpayer was assessed additional sales tax for unauthorized reductions, and the administrative law judge denied its protest. The OTC agreed, and the appellate court vacated the OTC's order. On appeal, the court reversed the OTC's decision regarding the assessment of sales tax because it was unclear whether the taxpayer paid sales tax based on the Medicare approved charges or whether it reduced the approved charges by the sales tax percentage. The court held that the sales tax should be added to the gross receipts, not included in the gross receipts pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 1361 (1991). The court disagreed with the taxpayer that the sales of the oxygen concentrators were the sale of medicines because the legislature intended for the sale to be that of medical equipment. Therefore, the court stated that the sale was a taxable transaction during the audit period, and the taxpayer was not entitled to a refund of sales tax.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the appellate court's decision regarding the proposed assessment of sales tax and held that the taxpayer was not entitled to a refund, reversing and remanding for further proceedings.

Tinker Inv. & Mortg. Corp. v. City of Midwest City


No. 78,844 cons. w/80,396, No. 80,396


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK 41; 873 P.2d 1029; 1994 Okla. LEXIS 47; 65 O.B.A.J. 1422



April 19, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT, OKLAHOMA COUNTY. Bryan Dixon, Judge



DISPOSITION: THE APPEAL IN CAUSE NO. 78,844 IS DISMISSED BECAUSE THAT APPEAL IS PROSECUTED FROM AN UNAPPEALABLE SUMMARY JUDGMENT; THE MOTION TO AMEND THE PETITION IN ERROR IN CAUSE NO. 80,396 IS DENIED; AND THE JUDGMENT OF THE TRIAL COURT IS AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated cases, appellant corporation sought review of judgments of the District Court, Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which granted appellee city's motion for summary judgment and entered judgment in favor of appellee developer.


OVERVIEW: A developer sued for declaration of its rights under the local ordinances and alternatively, for a writ of mandamus to compel their enforcement. The corporation filed a separate action against the city to compel enforcement of pay-back ordinances. The cases were consolidated. The trial court granted the city's motion for summary judgment against the corporation and entered judgment in favor of the developer. The corporation appealed. On appeal, the court determined that the corporation's appeal regarding summary judgment was dismissible because it sought to review an unappealable summary judgment. With regard to the second appeal, the corporation argued that the developer should have first pursued its quest for relief from the review board created by the city's pay-back ordinances. However, the court determined that it would have been futile for the developer to resort to a board that could not have granted an effective remedy. Therefore, the court found no fatal remedial impediment to the developer's pursuit of its court action.

Southwestern Bell Tel. Co. v. Okla. Corp. Comm'n


No. 80,579


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK 38; 873 P.2d 1001; 1994 Okla. LEXIS 48



April 13, 1994, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] APPLICATION TO ASSUME ORIGINAL JURISDICTION AND PETITION FOR WRIT OF PROHIBITION

REHEARING GRANTED AND OPINION OF THE COURT ISSUED MAY 25, 1993, IS WITHDRAWN AND THIS OPINION ORDERED SUBSTITUTED THEREFOR.

This Opinion Substituted by Court for Withdrawn Opinion of May 25, 1993, Reported at: 1993 Okla. LEXIS 91.



DISPOSITION: APPLICATION TO ASSUME ORIGINAL JURISDICTION GRANTED. PETITION FOR WRIT OF PROHIBITION DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner telephone company sought a court order disqualifying respondent, Corporation Commissioner (Commissioner), from further participation in the Corporation Commission rate hearing proceeding and all pending and future telephone company cases pursuant to allegations of bias on the part of the Commissioner.


OVERVIEW: The telephone company filed this action after the Commissioner presiding over their rate hearings announced that he had been secretly acting as an investigator and informant for the FBI regarding the conduct of the telephone company. The telephone company argued that the Commissioner was biased and prejudiced and sought to have him removed from hearings in which they were a party. The court denied the telephone company's motion. The court held that the authority to establish rates for all public service corporations was exclusively vested in the Corporation Commission by Okla. Const. Art. 9 § 18. The court held that rate hearings were legislative in nature and that the telephone company's assertion that the proceeding was of a judicial nature was erroneous. The court held that it had no power to grant relief sought against constitutional officers acting in a legislative capacity. The court held that because the Commissioner was acting in a legislative capacity, he was not required to comply with judicial standards of conduct.


OUTCOME: The court denied the telephone company's motion to disqualify the Commissioner from further participation in a rate hearing with the telephone company.
