STATE ex rel. CORPORATION COMM'N v. TEXAS COUNTY IRRIGATION & WATER RES. ASS'N


No. 66,698


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1991 OK 63; 818 P.2d 449; 1991 Okla. LEXIS 72; 62 O.B.A.J. 2078; 115 Oil & Gas Rep. 532



July 2, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals, Tulsa Division 4. Appeal from the Corporation Commission of the State of Oklahoma. 



DISPOSITION: CERTIORARI PREVIOUSLY GRANTED. OPINION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS VACATED. ORDERS OF THE CORPORATION COMMISSION AFFIRMED. 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees, two applicants seeking approval to inject enhanced recovery fluids in their oil wells and the Oklahoma Corporation Commission, challenged a judgment from the Oklahoma Court of Appeals, Tulsa Division, which reversed the Commission's orders approving the applications, and ruled in favor of appellant water association. The court of appeals held that the applicants' notice was constitutionally defective.


OVERVIEW: The applicants obtained orders from the Commission that authorized the injection of enhanced recovery fluids in their oil wells. The water association opposed the applications. The Court of Appeals reversed the Commission's orders. The Oklahoma Supreme Court granted certiorari. The court held that the orders of the Commission were valid as a matter of law and the court of appeals should not have disturbed them. The only notice requirements were those mandated by the rules of the Commission which were sufficient to apprise parties who were affected by the proposed injection orders of the proceedings to be conducted. Although the orders affected owners of water rights in the Ogallala Aquifer, individual notice to each of them was not required. The required notice adequately informed parties of the nature of the proceedings before the Commission even though it was not specified that fresh ground water could be used as an injection fluid. There was no requirement that a permit from the Oklahoma Water Resources Board needed to be obtained before the Commission could authorize the injection of enhanced recovery fluids, only a requirement that one be obtained before fresh water was used.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the court of appeals that reversed the Commission's orders that authorized the injection of enhanced recovery fluids.

In re INITIATIVE PETITION NO. 347


No. 76,109


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1991 OK 55; 813 P.2d 1019; 1991 Okla. LEXIS 63; 62 O.B.A.J. 1880



June 11, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original Proceeding to Determine the Validity of Initiative Petition No. 347, State Question No. 639, and an Appeal from the Ballot Title Thereof.



DISPOSITION: INITIATIVE PETITION NO. 347 IS DECLARED SUFFICIENT NUMERICALLY AND LEGALLY FOR SUBMISSION TO THE PEOPLE. THE BALLOT TITLE SUBMITTED BY THE ATTORNEY GENERAL IS APPROVED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Protestants brought an original election action against proponents seeking to determine the validity of Initiative Petition No. 347, which was also known as State Question No. 639, and an appeal from the ballot title thereof.


OVERVIEW: Protestants filed objections to the count of signatures on the petition and objections to the legal validity. They argued that the petition was facially invalid because it sought to repeal comprehensive appropriation and tax legislation and that it was invalid because it was deceptively worded, seriously misleading, and not readily understandable. The court was also presented with an objection to the proposed ballot title. After consideration, the court ruled against the protestants. The court held that where the title submitted by the Attorney General was found sufficient it was generally approved and utilized regardless of the sufficiency of those submitted by other parties. The court found that the determination was made that the Attorney General's proposed ballot title fulfilled the requirements of Okla. Stat. tit. 34, § 9 (Supp. 1989) because it accurately reflected the effects of the proposition by informing the electorate concerning the principle thrust of the proposition. The court ruled that a petition would not be declared invalid on the mere allegation that some signers could have been misled by statements of circulators relative to the effect of the proposed law.


OUTCOME: The court declared Initiative Petition No. 317 sufficient, both numerically and legally, for submission to the vote of the people of the State of Oklahoma as State Question No. 639. The ballot title submitted by the Attorney General was approved.

 

116 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Abrego v. Abrego


No. 75,633


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1991 OK 48; 812 P.2d 806; 1991 Okla. LEXIS 54; 62 O.B.A.J. 1665



May 21, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to review a Certified Interlocutory Order; District Court of Tulsa County; The Honorable Gordon McAllister, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: CERTIORARI PREVIOUSLY GRANTED; ORDER SUSTAINING MOTION IN LIMINE REVERSED; CAUSE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent father's estate appealed a decision in favor of petitioner mother by the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma) in an action to establish a lien for child support over the father's life insurance benefits and in the father's claim for attorney fees.


OVERVIEW: When the father died, he owed child support. The mother filed a request for a lien to be placed on his life insurance benefits. The estate claimed that the benefits were not subject to the claims of creditors, that is, the children, and that the lien was improper where the child support obligation terminated at his death. The court held that a first priority lien was properly levied on the benefits for accrued child support. The children were not creditors under Okla. Stat. tit. 36, § 3631 (1981) where § 3631 was intended to protect dependents from creditors, not from themselves. The action for child support did not abate at the father's death where there was unpaid child support at his death. Because Okla. Stat. tit. 43, § 116 (Supp. 1989) allowed for a trial court to require a parent to post a security to ensure payment of child support, the lien was proper. There was no violation of the Equal Protection Clause where married persons did not have to secure life insurance because of a rational distinction between married and divorced parents. However, no security was required for child support accruing after his death. Thus, no lien was permitted for future support.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision.

Sharp v. 251st St. Landfill, Inc.


No. 66,105


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1991 OK 41; 810 P.2d 1270; 1991 Okla. LEXIS 43; 62 O.B.A.J. 1299



April 23, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals, Division III Appeal from District Court of Okmulgee County; Honorable John Maley, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: CERTIORARI PREVIOUSLY GRANTED; COURT OF APPEALS OPINION VACATED; TRIAL COURT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellees, individual area residents and landowners (residents), sought review of the decision of the Court of Appeals, Division III (Oklahoma), which reversed the trial court's granting of a temporary injunction against appellant landfill company (company) in the residents' action that challenged the decision of the Oklahoma Department of Health (department) to grant the company a permit to construct and operate a solid waste disposal facility.


OVERVIEW: The residents had challenged the location of a solid waste landfill in their area. The court vacated the appellate court's decision and affirmed the trial court. The court held that under the Oklahoma Administrative Procedures Act (OAPA), Okla. Stat. tit. 75, § 301 et seq., the granting of the permit by the department was not subject to review under the OAPA. The court determined that the Okla. Solid Waste Management Act (OSWMA), Okla. Stat. tit. 63, § 2251 et seq., permitted an injunction challenging a landfill permit and that OSWMA did not preempt an anticipatory nuisance action by the residents. The OSWMA did not give the department exclusive jurisdiction to control sanitary landfills and provided for involvement of local governing bodies and the courts in the decision-making process. The court found that the residents had adequately shown that they were entitled to some form of injunctive relief on the merits and that the decision of the department to grant the permit did not comport with the legislative purposes to prevent nuisances or groundwater pollution. There was no error in setting the bond under Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 1392 securing the company's damages it might suffer.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the appellate court's decision and affirmed the trial court's granting of a temporary injunction to the residents in their action against the company in regard to the location of a landfill.

 

118 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Oklahoma Tax Com. v. City Vending of Muskogee, Inc.


No. 65,602


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1991 Okla. LEXIS 47



April 23, 1991, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals, Oklahoma City Division; Honorable William Bliss



DISPOSITION: CERTIORARI PREVIOUSLY GRANTED, COA OPINION VACATED, ORDER VACATED, JUDGMENT OF LOWER COURT REVERSED, AND CAUSE REMANDED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant cigarette wholesaler challenged a judgment of the Court of Appeals, Oklahoma City Division (Oklahoma), which affirmed a judgment of the county district court granting appellee Oklahoma Tax Commission's request for permanent injunctive relief to prohibit the wholesaler from selling cigarettes to an Indian tribe without purchasing tax stamps for the cigarettes. The wholesaler claimed that the cigarettes were exempt from taxation.


OVERVIEW: The ruling of the county district court enjoined the wholesaler from selling cigarettes and revoked its license. The court of appeals upheld the trial court's ruling on the basis that the appeal from the Oklahoma Tax Commission's order was not timely filed. No court had considered the merits of the wholesaler's constitutional argument. The court granted certiorari and reversed the ruling of the county district court and vacated the court of appeals' opinion. The court held that the State of Oklahoma, via the Oklahoma Tax Commission, did have subject matter jurisdiction to assess taxes against those sales made by tribal smokeshops to non-Indian and non-member customers. However, the commission was without jurisdiction to assess taxes on those sales made to tribal members. The commission's order did not distinguish between sales to tribal members and those to non-Indians and non-members; rather it validated all taxes assessed against the wholesaler on the basis that the state taxing statutes, without regard to federal case law, appeared to support the taxing of such sales. The commission did not have the jurisdiction to tax all such sales alike, and therefore its order was void.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the opinion of the court of appeals. The court also vacated the order of the Oklahoma Tax Commission as being void ab initio. The court reversed the judgment of the district court, and remanded the cause for vacation of the permanent injunction rendered in that court.

Stat. tit. 12, § 2011 (Supp. 1988). The corporation sought sanctions against the law firm for failure to dismiss a counterclaim in an underlying suit filed by the company against the law firm's client.


OVERVIEW: The company filed suit against several defendants including the client, seeking a money judgment, a declaratory judgment, and foreclosure of the company's lien against certain gas wells. The client filed a counterclaim, which resulted in a directed verdict in the company's favor. Thereafter, the company filed a motion for sanctions under § 2011 against the law firm for filing a counterclaim that lacked any legal or factual basis. The trial court found that § 2011 only applied to the signing of pleadings and denied the company's motion. In affirming the trial court, the court held that liability under § 2011 did not extend to the law firm represented by an attorney signing a document. Sisson v. Elkins


No. 72,578


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1990 OK 123; 801 P.2d 722; 1990 Okla. LEXIS 135; 61 O.B.A.J. 3082



November 20, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected November 26, 1990. As Corrected December 4, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from The District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma; The Honorable Jack R. Parr.



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the trial court AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patient's next friend (patient) appealed the judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) that was entered on a jury verdict in favor of defendant surgeon in the patient's medical malpractice cause of action for the brain damage that occurred when the surgeon inadvertently cut into an implanted artificial conduit, which acted as a major blood vessel, while replacing the conduit.


OVERVIEW: Because inadvertently cutting the conduit was a known risk of the operation, the patient's expert opined that the surgeon should have placed the patient on bypass prior to the surgery, instead of allowing her to remain with reduced blood pressure and oxygen to her brain for 30 minutes. On appeal, the patient contended that the trial court erred in refusing to provide a res ipsa loquitur instruction as she requested and in instructing the jury as to the duty of a non-specialist physician as opposed to a specialist's duty. In affirming the trial court's judgment, the court determined that the patient was unable to establish, pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 76, § 21.3 (1981), that her injury would not ordinarily have occurred exclusive of the surgeon's negligence. The patient's expert did not so testify nor did she provide evidence on the point. Thus, the trial court did not err in refusing to instruct the jury on the doctrine. Nor was there error in the physician's duty charge inasmuch as the trial court followed the non-specialist charge with the specialist charge and the concurrent presentation of the instructions to the jury was not confusing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

124 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. Vickers, Inc.


No. 72,724


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1990 OK 108; 799 P.2d 621; 1990 Okla. LEXIS 116; 61 O.B.A.J. 2717



October 16, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On Certiorari to the Court of Appeals, Div. 2.



DISPOSITION: THE COURT OF APPEALS' OPINION IS VACATED; THE WORKERS' COMPENSATION COURT'S ORDER DENYING THE CLAIM IS SUSTAINED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner claimant sought workers' compensation for loss of hearing from exposure to high levels of industrial noise during eight years of work as a machinist for respondent employer. The Court of Appeals, Division 2 (Oklahoma) sustained the denial of the claim. The claimant filed a request for certiorari review, which was granted.


OVERVIEW: The employer maintained that no on-the-job injury had occurred because hearing tests conducted upon the claimant at the beginning of his employment showed the same amount of hearing loss as those conducted after eight years of employment. The parties further disputed whether Workers' Comp. Ct. R. 37, Okla. Stat. tit. 85, ch. 4, app. (Supp. 1981) or Workers' Comp. Ct. R. 32 applied. Rule 37 was in effect at the time of the claimed injury while Rule 32, which replaced Rule 37, was in effect at the time the claim was filed. The court held that it was irrelevant which rule applied and that the only pertinent question was whether the trial tribunal's finding that no work-related injury had occurred was supported by probative evidence. The court believed that it was. The court held that orders denying or awarding compensation had to be supported by competent evidence, that which was probative of the ultimate facts upon which the order rested. Much like a medical opinion that appeared competent on its face and was received into evidence, the employer's initial audiograms had probative value unless, through cross-examination, a fatal flaw was revealed. No such flaw appeared.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the opinion of the court of appeals and sustained the order of the Workers' Compensation Courts denying the claim.

Clifton v. Clifton


No. 70,357


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1990 OK 88; 801 P.2d 693; 1990 Okla. LEXIS 97; 61 O.B.A.J. 2366



September 18, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied December 4, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to The Court of Appeals Tulsa Division; Honorable Niles Jackson, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: CERTIORARI PREVIOUSLY GRANTED; COURT OF APPEALS OPINION VACATED, TRIAL COURT REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner wife applied for a writ of certiorari, which sought review of the Court of Appeals', Tulsa Division (Oklahoma), decision reversing the trial court's granting of her motion to modify a divorce decree to include half of respondent husband's gross military retirement pay as jointly acquired property.


OVERVIEW: The husband served in the military for 20 years, 16 of which occurred during his marriage to the wife. The wife filed for divorce, the parties entered into a settlement agreement, and a divorce was granted. Four years later, the wife filed a motion to modify the divorce decree to include half of the husband's gross military retirement pay as jointly acquired property. Citing 12 O.S. 1987 § 1289(F), which provided for the retrospective application with regards to modifications for the purpose of obtaining support or payments pertaining to a division of property on divorce decrees, the trial court awarded wife a portion of the retirement pay and the court of appeals reversed. The court granted the wife certiorari and reversed the trial court's decision, holding that § 1289(F) did not provide the means to alter final divorce decrees for the division of military retirement benefits as jointly acquired property. The court found that § 1289(F) applied only to payments for support alimony because subsection (F) referred the reader to subsection (E), which provided for the modification of alimony for support. There was no reference in subsection (E) to modification of a property division.


OUTCOME: The court granted the wife's petition for writ of certiorari and reversed the trial court's decision granting the wife's motion to modify a divorce decree to include half of her husband's gross military retirement pay as jointly acquired property.

Michael F. v. State ex. rel. Dep't of Human Servs. (In re D.D.F.)


No. 70,785


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1990 OK 89; 801 P.2d 703; 1990 Okla. LEXIS 95; 61 O.B.A.J. 2374



September 18, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied December 18, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to Oklahoma Court of Appeals, Division 3; Honorable Bradford Griffith.



DISPOSITION: COA OPINION VACATED; TRIAL COURT'S RULING AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father appealed the order from the Court of Appeals, which entered judgment in favor of appellee State and affirmed a decision to terminate the father's parental rights. The court of appeals also affirmed a finding that the father's two adopted daughters were deprived. The father claimed that his parental rights were improperly terminated because Okla. Stat. tit. 10, §§ 1130(A)(5) and (7) required a "final" conviction.


OVERVIEW: The father, a divorced and single man, adopted two children from an orphanage in Brazil. The girls, ages five and six, were sisters. Shortly after the adoption, the father was convicted of Obtaining Money by False Pretenses and was sentenced to prison. The girls were placed in the protective custody of the Department of Human Services (DHS). The DHS became aware that the girls had been sexually abused by the father. He was later convicted of two counts of Lewd Molestation of his adoptive daughters. While the convictions were pending appeal, the trial court determined the children to be deprived and ordered the father's parental rights terminated. The orders were affirmed. On appeal, the court found that the father's molestation conviction could not be the basis of the termination decision because, while it was pending appeal, it was not a final conviction. However, the court found that the termination was authorized under Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 1130A(5)(a), which authorized termination if there was a finding that the parent had sexually abused the child. The court held that the evidence supported such a finding and affirmed the orders of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the opinion of the Court of Appeals and affirmed for different reasons the termination of the father's parental rights.

 

127 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lynch


Nos. 74,319; 74,259


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1990 OK 82; 796 P.2d 1150; 1990 Okla. LEXIS 88; 61 O.B.A.J. 2102



July 24, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] An Appeal from the District Court of Seminole County. Honorable Gordon R. Melson, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: Original jurisdiction assume judgment of the trial court affirmed as modified in case No. 74,319.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state of Oklahoma sought review of a decision of the District Court of Seminole County, which awarded attorney fees greater than those allowed by 21 Okla. Stat. Tit. 21§701.14 to defendants, court-appointed attorneys.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were appointed to represent a death-eligible criminal defendant. They expended a combined 280 hours on the case and incurred out-of-pocket expenses. Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 701.14 provided for a maximum statutory fee, which would have caused defendants to lose certain amounts per hour in overhead expenses. The trial court approved defendant's requested fees and deviated from the statute. The court affirmed a deviation from the statute. The court held that § 701.14 was unconstitutional as applied to defendants because such a low rate of compensation was a taking of private property. The court held that attorneys must be provided a postappointment opportunity to show good cause why they cannot represent an indigent defendant. The court held that there was an equal protection violation because Oklahoma attorneys who practiced in certain counties were immunized from the representation of indigent defendants. The court recommended that the hourly rate for court-appointed attorneys be tied to the hourly rate of the prosecutors and public defenders and that they be reimbursed for overhead fees and litigation expenses.


OUTCOME: The court held that defendants were entitled to greater fees than those allowed by statute, that the statute was unconstitutional as applied to defendants, that the court appointment system pressed lawyers into service without affording them an opportunity to show cause why they should be excused, and that the statute provided an arbitrary and unreasonable rate of compensation that could result in an unconstitutional taking of private property.

 

128 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Dean Witter Reynolds, Inc. v. Shear


No. 73,947


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1990 OK 67; 796 P.2d 296; 1990 Okla. LEXIS 76; 61 O.B.A.J. 1946



July 17, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the District Court, Oklahoma County, Charles L. Owens, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant investor appealed a judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) which decreed the enforcement of an arbitration award that plaintiff securities broker won against the investor after a dispute arose under the parties' securities transaction contract.


OVERVIEW: The investor's contract with his security broker stipulated that New York law was to control any dispute arising thereunder and that arbitration would be used to resolve such disputes. When a dispute arose between the parties, the broker won before the arbitrator because the investor refused to participate in the proceedings. The broker then sought judicial enforcement of the arbitration award in Oklahoma. The trial court entered a "summary judgment" in the form of a judgment on the pleadings in the broker's favor. On the investor's appeal, the court found in favor of the broker. The investor's attempt to rely on Okla. Const. art. 23, § 8 to void the choice-of-law and arbitration clauses failed because the investor did not preserve that issue for appeal by arguing it to the trial court. Therefore, the investor's failure to challenge the efficacy of the choice-of-law clause that made New York law operative in the parties' dispute meant that the investor was estopped to rely on fundamental Oklahoma law to undermine his contractual concession.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment entered in favor of the broker.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following appellee teacher's reprimand, the teacher filed a request for arbitration and appellant school board refused to participate in the arbitration. The school board challenged the decision of the District Court of Craig County (Oklahoma), which required the school board to comply with binding arbitration.


OVERVIEW: The issue presented to the court was whether a binding grievance arbitration provision in a collective bargaining agreement between the school board and the teachers' organization impermissibly delegated the school board's authority to reprimand a teacher. The court held that to subject disciplinary decisions to binding arbitration would seriously interfere with school board's ability to maintain adequate standards and discipline among its teachers. The court further held that under Okla. Stat. Therefore, the court concluded that the trial court erred in requiring the school board to comply with the binding arbitration provision of the collective bargaining agreement.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court that required the school board to comply with the binding arbitration provision of the collective bargaining agreement.

Stewart v. Rood


No. 64,932


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1990 OK 69; 796 P.2d 321; 1990 Okla. LEXIS 83; 61 O.B.A.J. 1914; 21 ELR 20026



July 17, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals, Division III; Appeal from the District Court of Pottawatomie County, Oklahoma, Honorable Glenn Dale Carter, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: Certiorari previously granted, court of appeals opinion vacated, trial court decision affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners sought review of a decision of the Court of Appeals, Division III (Oklahoma), which affirmed the trial court's judgment denying them relief in their action to void a permit for the operation of a landfill issued by defendant Oklahoma Department of Health (ODH). The landowners raised constitutional and procedural challenges to the issuance of the permit.


OVERVIEW: Defendant applicant sought a permit to operate a landfill next to the landowners' property. Notice was published and, upon request, a public meeting was held at which the landowners registered their opposition. The meeting was not a trial type proceeding under Article II of the Oklahoma Administrative Procedures Act. ODH issued the permit on the same day that the landowners filed a complaint to restrain its issuance. The landowners contended that they were entitled to an "individual proceeding," as the full Article II hearing was called. They also contended that issuance of the permit violated their due process rights and effected an unconstitutional taking of their property. The court of appeals disagreed with the trial court and held that they were entitled to a trial type hearing. The court held they were not. The legislature carefully used the word meeting instead of hearing in the statute. There was no statutory or constitutional basis for entitlement to a trial type hearing. Fears that the landfill could become a nuisance and diminution in the value of their property did not furnish legally protected interests under the due process clause.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the decision of the court of appeals and affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Rollow v. City of Ada

Supreme Court of Oklahoma

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners sought review of the decision of the Court of Appeals, Tulsa Division (Oklahoma), which affirmed the order of the district court that upheld the creation of an improvement district by appellee city.


OVERVIEW: The city established an improvement district for the purpose of enhancing downtown business, including the purchase of two parking garages from holders of revenue bonds that were used to build the garages. The property owners challenged the creation of the district on the ground that the city intended to pay more than the fair market value for the garages and that the garages could have been obtained through eminent domain for a lesser amount. The district court and the appellate court affirmed the creation of the district. On review, the court vacated the opinion of the appellate court and reversed the trial court's judgment. The court found that a substantial amount of property, which was directly benefited by the improvement district, was selectively excluded from taxation and that such exclusion was prohibited.


OUTCOME: The court granted certiorari. The court vacated the opinion of the appellate court and reversed the judgment of the trial cour that upheld the creation of the improvement district.

Private Truck Council of Am., Inc. v. Okla. Tax Comm'n


No. 68,401


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1990 OK 54; 806 P.2d 598; 1990 Okla. LEXIS 68; 61 O.B.A.J. 1757



June 28, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 24, 1990. As Amended March 5, 1991.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County; Honorable John M. Amick, Trial Judge.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED FOR FURTHER PROCEEDINGS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant truckers challenged the decision of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which denied their motion for summary judgment, upheld the constitutionality of Okla. Stat. tit. 47, § 1120(K) (1982) and Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 67 (1982), and granted a final judgment as a matter of law in favor of appellee Oklahoma Tax Commission.


OVERVIEW: The truckers argued that § 1120(K) and § 607.1 were a blatant and egregious violation of the Commerce Clause, because they were discriminatory on their face against nonresident motor carriers. The truckers sought a declaratory judgment declaring Oklahoma's retaliatory statutes unconstitutional, and also requested a permanent injunction against collection of the challenged taxes and refunds of all taxes and fees paid. The Commission argued that because the truckers failed to produce any factual evidence showing actual damages resulting from the alleged discriminatory effect of the statutes, the trial court properly rejected the truckers' claim. The court found that the statutes were plainly discriminatory in that they imposed excessive fees and taxes on out-of-state registered motor carriers that were not imposed on Oklahoma registered motor carriers. The court held that the challenged statutes violated the Commerce Clause and were unconstitutional. However, the court concluded that under the inequities of the particular case, the truckers were only entitled to a partial refund under Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 226.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, ordered the Commission to refund a portion of the taxes that the truckers wrongfully paid, and remanded the case to the trial court for a determination of interest.

In re INITIATIVE PETITION NO. 341


No. 74,409


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1990 OK 53; 796 P.2d 267; 1990 Okla. LEXIS 62; 61 O.B.A.J. 1641



June 19, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected June 22, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original action protesting Initiative Petition No. 341, State Question No. 627, proposal to constitutionally create Ethics Commission. Petition found constitutional and in statutory compliance. New ballot title adopted.



DISPOSITION: Amended ballot title is remanded to Secretary of State for submission to State Election Board.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Protestants brought an action challenging the constitutionality of a proposed constitutional amendment, arguing that it violated the First Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. I. The proposed amendment sought to create a five member Ethics Commission that had the power, subject to legislative approval, to promulgate rules of ethical conduct for campaigns for elective state offices and for initiative and referenda.


OVERVIEW: Protestants challenged an initiative petition that sought to create an Ethics Commission that would have the power, subject to legislative approval, to promulgate rules of ethical conduct for campaigns for elective state officers and for initiative and referenda. Protestants argued that this proposed constitutional amendment violated the First Amendment because it gave the Commission the unfettered discretion to make rules. The court concluded that the creation of the Commission and the delegation of authority, without more, did not violate the First Amendment. Until rules or statutes which restricted conduct became effective, the overbreadth doctrine was not applicable. Further, the court held that the petition did not give the Commission unfettered discretion in violation of the Oklahoma Constitution. After a rule was adopted, the Legislature could repeal or modify the rule. Any rule promulgated by the Commission would not become effective without legislative ratification. The court held that the petition did not prohibit, either prospectively or retrospectively, or "chill" any First Amendment activities and was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court found that the petition was constitutional and in statutory compliance. The court ordered that the new ballot title was to be adopted.

Franco-American Charolaise, Ltd. v. Okla. Water Res. Bd.


No. 59,310


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1990 OK 44; 855 P.2d 568; 1990 Okla. LEXIS 49



April 24, 1990, Filed; This Opinion Substituted by Court for Withdrawn Opinion of May 19, 1987


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] ON APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT, COAL COUNTY, OKLAHOMA, Lavern Fishel, Trial Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, state water board and city, challenged the decision of the District Court, Coal County (Oklahoma), which ruled in favor of appellees, riparian owners and in-basin appropriators, in their appeal from the approval of the city's application to increase its appropriation of water from a spring.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, riparian owners and in basin-appropriators, challenged the decision by appellant state water board approving appellant city's application to increase its appropriation of spring water. The trial court ruled in favor of appellees. On further review, the court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that riparian owners had a vested common-law right to the reasonable use of the stream, which could not be taken for public use without compensation. The court further held that to the extent that the 1963 amendments to Okla. Stat. tit. 60, § 60 (1981) limited the riparian owner to domestic use and declared all other stream water public water, the statute violated Okla. Const. art. 2, § 24. The court found that the statutory mechanism for protection of a riparian owner's beneficial uses was constitutionally inadequate because it judged the use by its priority in time rather than by its reasonableness. The court directed the trial court to determine the reasonableness of each of the riparian owners' asserted uses and reversed the trial court's holding requiring the board to consider all of the city's water sources in assessing its need for the stream water.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, and reversed in part, rulings in favor of appellees, riparian owners and in-basin appropriators, in their challenge to appellee city's application to increase its water appropriation. The court held that the statutory limitation on the riparian owners' use of stream water was unconstitutional and remanded the case for a determination of the reasonableness of each of the riparian owner's asserted uses.

Branch Trucking Co. v. State ex rel. Okla. Tax Comm'n


No. 68,620


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1990 OK 41; 801 P.2d 686; 1990 Okla. LEXIS 40

The cooperatives' motion requesting the court to stay the effect of the regulation without posting a bond was denied.


OVERVIEW: The Commission adopted a regulation requiring rural electric cooperatives to collect sales tax on the sale of electricity to the consumers. The Commission issued an order allowing any party affected by the regulation to stay the effect of the order by posting a bond in the amount of one percent of the gross total sales of electricity. The cooperatives' motion requesting a stay without posting the bond was denied. On appeal, the court vacated the Commission's order. The court held that because the cooperatives were not required to collect the tax, the settled policy could not be reversed absent legislative action. Since there was no legislative action to reverse the Commission's interpretation of the Rural Electrification Act, 7 U.S.C.S. § 901 et seq., the regulation has the force of law. The court ruled that the cooperatives were exempt from collecting the sales tax. However, the court lacked the authority to grant the cooperatives a refund, because the action was filed under Okla. OUTCOME: The court vacated the Commission's order requiring the cooperatives to collect sales tax on the sale of electricity.

Okla. Broadcasters Ass'n v. State Tax Comm'n


No. 65,983


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1990 OK 30; 789 P.2d 1312; 1990 Okla. LEXIS 31; 17 Media L. Rep. 1994



March 27, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected May 1, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appellees have brought a declaratory judgment action to challenge three provisions of the Oklahoma Sales Tax Code, 68 O.S. 1981, § 1354 (A) and (R) and 68 O.S. 1971, 1304 (i) as it stood prior to amendment. These provisions were challenged under the First Amendment and on equal protection violations in that, either the statute on its face, or the Tax Commission's application, subjected members of the broadcast media to taxation for which members of the print media were exempt. After submission of the case for non-jury trial, the trial court found all three challenged provisions to be unconstitutional. Appellant Tax Commission now challenges the trial court's ruling.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Citing the First and Fourteenth Amendments, appellee broadcasters brought a declaratory judgment action against appellant Oklahoma Tax Commission to challenge three sales tax provisions: Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 1354(A) and (R) (1981) and Okla. Stat. tit. 68, 1304(i) (1971) before 1980 Okla. Sess. Laws ch. 288, § 2 amended it. The District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) held all three provisions unconstitutional. The Tax Commission appealed.


OVERVIEW: The broadcasters argued that the statutes either on their face or their application subjected the broadcast media to taxation for which the print media were exempt. The taxes were on gross receipts from licensing agreements, advertising, and equipment. The court explained that where the press was concerned, the state was required to provide a compelling interest for different treatment, and the raising of revenue was not sufficient. The court explained that it was presumptively unconstitutional to favor one type of media over another because freedom of the press was guaranteed, not just freedom of the print media. The court explained that the exemptions selectively taxing certain members of the press favored the print media over the broadcasting media and no argument was presented offering a justification that survived strict scrutiny. It was not shown that a counterbalancing interest of compelling importance could not have been achieved without differential taxation. Accepting the broadcaster's argument that the Tax Commission might have decided to apply the Okla. Stat. tit. 68, 1304(i) (1971) to years before the amendment, the court ruled that it was properly considered.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision.

City of Okla. City v. Okla. Tax Comm'n


No. 68,405


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1990 OK 27; 789 P.2d 1287; 1990 Okla. LEXIS 30



March 27, 1990, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected May 1, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals Oklahoma City Division, Honorable Leamon Freemon, Trial Judge. The trial court dismissed with prejudice the appellant/City of Oklahoma City's (City) petition for failure to state a claim. The City had sought a declaration that interest earned on municipal tax revenues collected by the appellee/Oklahoma Tax Commission was an accretion to principal, and an accounting of interest due. The Court of Appeals reversed finding that the appellant was entitled to interest earned on sales taxes as accretion to the principal. The issues presented are: 1) whether a municipality which contracts with the Oklahoma Tax Commission for the collection of municipal taxes under the authority of 68 O.S. Supp. 1986 § 2702 is entitled to interest earned by taxes deposited in the State Treasury; and 2) if the municipality is entitled to investment interest, whether it may recover interest deposited to the state's general revenue fund. We find that: 1) the interest earned on municipal sales tax revenues is an accretion or increment to the principal tax. Pursuant to the Okla. Const. art. 10, § 19, the total i.e., principal and interest, must be expended for the purpose levied; and 2) because the fund representing interest earned on the investment of the municipal sales  [***2] taxes has been appropriated, it is not recoverable. CERTIORARI GRANTED; OPINION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS VACATED; REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city contested the opinion of the Oklahoma Court of Appeals (Oklahoma City Division) that reversed the trial court's prejudicial dismissal of the city's petition against appellee Oklahoma Tax Commission in the parties' litigation arising under Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 2702 (Supp. 1986).


OVERVIEW: The city contracted for the Commission to collect the municipality's sales taxes. The city sought a declaratory judgment that it was entitled to the interest that the taxes earned during their deposit in the state treasury before being disbursed to the city. The city's petition was prejudicially dismissed for failure to state a claim. The city's successful appeal to the lower court led the court to grant certiorari and relief. The interest earned on the city's municipal sales tax revenues was an accretion or increment that became part of the principal tax. Under Okla. Const. art. 10, § 19, the interest had to be expended for the same purpose for which its underlying principal had been levied. As a matter of fiscal accounting, the city could not recover interest earned on investment of municipal sales taxes if those monies had been appropriated and disbursed. Consequently, there was no fund from which the interest at issue could be recovered. Accounting problems did not justify depriving owners of their funds, however.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the lower court's opinion and reversed the cause.

Kirschstein v. Haynes


No. 67,655


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1990 OK 8; 788 P.2d 941; 1990 Okla. LEXIS 9



January 30, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals, Oklahoma City Divisions, Appeal from the District Court of Cleveland County, Honorable Noah Ewing, Trial Judge. Appellant brought actions for defamation and intentional infliction of emotional distress alleging Appellee Moore procured an affidavit from Appellee Haynes which was false and defamatory, which in turn was published by Appellee Kilgore. Appellant also brought a cause for determination of heirs. The trial court granted summary judgment for Appellees ruling the affidavit and its publications privileged as it had been obtained for use in a proceeding to be initiated by Kilgore to procure a birth certificate. The Court of Appeals affirmed as to the first two causes on the basis an absolute privilege attaches to communications made in the course of preparation for judicial proceedings, relying on the Restatement (Second) of Torts, § 586 (1977). The Court of Appeals did not reach the merits of arguments raised in regard to the determination of heirs cause because it ruled Appellant did not preserve any issue as to said claim by failure to raise such in her petition in error. Held: We generally adopt the Restatement's view as to absolute privilege for communications preliminary to a judicial or quasi-judicial proceeding in regard to attorneys, parties and witnesses. We further affirm the  [***2] grant of summary judgment in favor of Appellees. We also hold Appellant failed to preserve any issue or claim of error as to the determination of heirs claim by failing to raise such in her petition in error. CERTIORARI PREVIOUSLY GRANTED; OPINION OF COURT OF APPEALS VACATED AND WITHDRAWN FROM PUBLICATION; TRIAL COURT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual sought review by certiorari of the order of the Court of Appeals, Oklahoma City Division (Oklahoma), which affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of appellee individuals on appellant's claims of intentional infliction of emotional distress and defamation.


OVERVIEW: Appellant brought an action for intentional infliction of emotional distress and defamation alleging that an appellee obtained a false and defamatory affidavit, which in turn was published by another appellee. The trial court granted summary judgment for appellees, ruling that the affidavit and its publications were privileged in that they had been obtained for use in a proceeding initiated by appellant to procure a birth certificate. The appellate court affirmed, holding that an absolute privilege attached to communications made in preparation for judicial proceedings, and did not reach the merits of arguments raised in regard to a determination of heirs cause because it ruled that appellant did not preserve the issues by raising the claims in the petition in error. The court recognized an absolute privilege for communications made preliminary to judicial or quasi-judicial proceedings in favor of attorneys, parties, and witnesses and found that the privilege applied to the intentional infliction of emotional distress claim. The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment; holding that the appellate court properly found that appellant failed to preserve the claim of error.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of appellees. The court affirmed the appellate court's decision to forego deciding the merits of any issues in relation to appellant's determination of heirs on the grounds that appellant failed to preserve the error.

Dow Jones & Co. v. State ex rel. Okla. Tax Comm'n


No. 70663


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1990 OK 6; 787 P.2d 843; 1990 Okla. LEXIS 8; 17 Media L. Rep. 1401



January 30, 1990, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the Oklahoma Tax Commission. Taxpayer appeals from an Oklahoma Tax Commission order denying its protest against use tax assessment on publications delivered within the state. ORDER REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of the order of appellee Oklahoma Tax Commission, which denied its protest against Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 1402 (Supp. 1987) use tax assessment on its publications delivered within Oklahoma.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer, a publisher of printed materials, sold the majority of its publications by subscription, which were delivered by mail. The taxpayer was assessed a use tax deficiency under § 1402. By the terms of Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 1404(e) (1981), the Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 1357(C) (1981) sales tax exemption for printed materials, based upon sales price and mode of delivery, extended to the use tax. The taxpayer challenged the assessment. The Commission denied the taxpayer's protest. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held the Commission properly concluded that, as an administrative agency, it was powerless to strike down a statute for constitutional repugnancy. However, raising revenue alone was insufficient justification for selective exaction, and the State of Oklahoma did not meet its burden to advance some compelling interest. Further, it was not appropriate to sever the sales and use tax exemptions because they were interwoven with the taxes. Thus, the sales and use taxes violated the First Amendment. Finally, there was no First Amendment impediment preventing the legislature from reenacting both taxes, so as to burden all sales of printed publications within Oklahoma.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the Commission's order.

Willow Wind, Inc. v. City of Midwest City


Nos. 68,805, consolidated with No. 68,834


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1989 OK 171; 790 P.2d 1067; 1989 Okla. LEXIS 198



December 26, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On certiorari from the Court of Appeals, Oklahoma City Divisions. The City of Midwest City enacted ordinances allowing private developers to construct water and sewer lines running from city subdivisions and providing for repayment of a portion of the cost of those lines through a collection process administered by the city. The ordinances provided that any subsequent developers would be assessed a tie-on fee, and that ninety percent of that fee would be returned to the original developers, with ten percent of the fee going to the city for the cost of administration. When the city failed to collect the fee, the appellants sued and the city repealed the ordinances. The district court granted summary judgment to the city finding the ordinances to be unconstitutional. The Court of Appeals reversed and remanded for a hearing on the merits.



DISPOSITION: CERTIORARI PREVIOUSLY GRANTED. COURT OF APPEALS OPINION VACATED AND THE JUDGMENT OF THE TRIAL COURT REVERSED AND REMANDED FOR A HEARING ON THE MERITS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The case was before the court on certiorari from the Court of Appeals, Oklahoma City Divisions (Oklahoma). Appellee city had repealed certain ordinances after finding them to be unconstitutional. The trial court granted summary judgment to the city and against appellant developers, agreeing that the ordinances were unconstitutional. The appellate court reversed and remanded for a hearing on the merits.


OVERVIEW: The city enacted ordinances allowing private developers to construct water and sewer lines running from city subdivisions and providing for repayment of a portion of the cost of those lines through a collection process administered by the city. The ordinances provided that any subsequent developers would be assessed a tie-on fee, and that 90 percent of that fee would be returned to the original developers, with 10 percent of the fee going to the city for the cost of administration. When the city failed to collect the fee, the developers filed suit. The city repealed the ordinances on the ground that the ordinances created a tax in violation of Okla. Const. art. 10, §§ 14,17, 26, 27. The court held that the ordinances did not create impermissible taxes or debts; thus, the ordinances were valid. The ordinances were special assessments because they were used to reimburse the initial developers and the assessments were levied only occasionally. The ordinances did not create debts because the city did not owe a specific amount.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment.

 

142 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Okla. Gas & Elec. Co. v. Dist. Court


No. 72,037


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1989 OK 158; 784 P.2d 61; 1989 Okla. LEXIS 193



December 12, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original proceeding for a prerogative writ. After a light plane collided with an electrical transmission powerline, the plane's pilot and a passenger commenced actions for bodily injury against the petitioner powerline owner. Following consolidation of the two cases for trial, the petitioner sought leave to amend its answer and to press a counterclaim for contribution from the pilot as a joint tortfeasor, urging that the consolidation made its claim for contribution a compulsory counterclaim. The trial court denied petitioner's request.



DISPOSITION:  APPLICATION TO ASSUME ORIGINAL JURISDICTION GRANTED; PETITION FOR WRIT OF MANDAMUS DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner electric company filed an application for a writ of mandamus directing the respondents, the District Court for the 15th Judicial District, Cherokee County, Oklahoma, and the district court judge, to permit the electric company to amend its answer in the underlying personal injury action.


OVERVIEW: A pilot flew a plane into a power line established and maintained by an electric company. The passenger filed a personal injury action against the electric company and the pilot. The pilot was later dismissed from the action. The electric company filed a motion seeking to amend its answer to bring a claim for contribution against the pilot. The district judge denied the motion, and the electric company filed an application for a writ of mandamus, seeking to compel the district court and the district judge to allow the amended answer. The court noted that mandamus was an extraordinary remedy that was only granted upon a showing of a clear legal right. The court noted further that mandamus was warranted only if the electric company's contribution claim was compulsory. The court held that the electric company's claim for contribution was not a compulsory counterclaim, and the denial of leave to assert it in the underlying action did not deprive the electric company of a clear legal right.


OUTCOME: The electric company's petition for a writ of mandamus was denied.

 

143 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


SKZ, Inc. v. Petty


Nos. 68,037, 68,117, 68,118


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1989 OK 150; 782 P.2d 939; 1989 Okla. LEXIS 180; 107 Oil & Gas Rep. 63



November 14, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Corporation Commission of Oklahoma. Unit operator appeals from orders of the Corporation Commission allowing appellees, owners of leasehold interests, to participate in increased density wells drilled by appellant's predecessor, even though appellees, or their predecessors, had previously elected not to participate in the first test well in the unit. Principal issue on appeal is whether Corporation Commission has authority to force pool by the wellbore instead of force pooling by the drilling and spacing unit.



DISPOSITION:  CORPORATION COMMISSION ORDER NOS. 306469, 307103 and 307104 REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant unit operator sought review of orders from the Corporation Commission of Oklahoma, which allowed appellee owners of leasehold interests to participate in increased density wells drilled by the operator's predecessor, even though the leaseholders, or their predecessors, had previously elected not to participate in the first test well in the unit.


OVERVIEW: The principal issue on appeal was whether the Commission had authority to force pool by the wellbore instead of force pooling by the drilling and spacing unit. The leaseholders argued that because prior orders from the Commission allegedly pooled the wellbore, any alteration would constitute a collateral attack on those orders and deprive the leaseholders of procedural due process. The leaseholders further alleged that such alteration would be an unconstitutional taking of private property for private use in violation of Okla. Const. art. II, §§ 7 and 23. The court held that the decision of the Commission allowing the leaseholders to participate in the increased density wells was erroneous. In two previous cases, where pooling orders in dispute referred to "the well" in singular form, the orders were held to pool the entire unit. The addition of the word "unit" in front of "well" in the instant case did not warrant distinction. Therefore, the orders pooled the entire drilling and spacing unit. By repooling the unit, absent a showing of changed conditions or an infirmity in the original pooling orders, the Commission exceeded its statutory authority. The orders were reversed.


OUTCOME: The orders were reversed.

TURLEY v. FLAG-REDFERN OIL CO.


No. 72,408


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1989 OK 144; 782 P.2d 130; 1989 Okla. LEXIS 174; 105 Oil & Gas Rep. 553



October 31, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Corporation Commission of Oklahoma. The appellee, Flag-Redfern Oil Company, filed an application with the Corporation Commission to vacate a previous order establishing 640-acre spacing and establishing 80-acre drilling and spacing units in Section 9, Township 15 North, Range 25 West, Roger Mills County, Oklahoma. The appellant, Windle Turley (Turley/surface owner), filed a motion to reopen Cause No. 146981 and a motion to stay the effectiveness of Order No. 333344. The Corporation Commission en banc dismissed the motion to reopen and denied the motion to stay effectiveness of Order CD No. 333344 because the surface owner lacked standing. We find that: 1) surface owners do not have standing as "persons aggrieved" within the meaning of 52 O.S. 1981 § 113 to appeal Corporation Commission orders; 2) because surface owners hold no interest which entitles them to protest applications to establish, reestablish, or reform drilling and spacing units, 52 O.S. Supp. 1988 § 87.2 is not unconstitutional for failure to provide surface owners with notice and an opportunity to be heard; and 3) the exclusion of surface owners from those parties entitled to protest drilling and spacing applications under § 87.2 does not violate  [***2] equal protection. The surface owner's remedy is under the Oklahoma Surface Damages Act, 52 O.S. Supp. 1982 § 318.2 et seq. CORPORATION COMMISSION ORDER SUSTAINED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant surface owner appealed from the decision from the Corporation Commission of Oklahoma that dismissed its motion to reopen and denied its motion to stay effectiveness of a previous order in appellee mineral rights owner's drilling and spacing applications.


OVERVIEW: The surface owner did not have any mineral rights in the land in question. Appellee mineral rights owner filed an application with the Commission requesting drilling and spacing units for the production of oil. The Commission found that the surface owner lacked standing to protest the drilling and spacing application and dismissed his motion to stay the order. On appeal, the court held that the surface owner did not have standing as a "person aggrieved" within the meaning of Okla. Stat. tit. 52, § 113 (1981) to appeal Commission orders. Because the surface owner held no interest which entitled it to protest applications to establish, reestablish, or reform drilling and spacing units, Okla. Stat. tit. 52, § 87.2 (1988) was not unconstitutional for failure to provide surface owners with notice and an opportunity to be heard at protest hearings. The exclusion of surface owners from those parties entitled to protest drilling and spacing applications under § 87.2 did not violate equal protection. The surface owner's remedy was under the Oklahoma Surface Damages Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 52, § 318.2 et seq. (1982).


OUTCOME: The order of the Corporation Commission was sustained.

ST. PAUL FIRE & MARINE INS. CO. v. GETTY OIL CO.


No. 63,340


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1989 OK 139; 782 P.2d 915; 1989 Okla. LEXIS 169



October 24, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals, Tulsa Division, Honorable Robert E. Scott. Certiorari granted to review published opinions of Court of Appeals, Tulsa Division which reversed trial court's orders sustaining defendant's demurrers and motions to dismiss, and declared 12 O.S. 1981 § 109 unconstitutional. Opinions of Court of Appeals are vacated, and trial court's orders relating to defendant architects and builders are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court granted certiorari in a subrogation action brought by plaintiff insurer to recover from defendants, the building contractors, the architects, and the ceiling plasterers. The trial court found in favor of defendants and dismissed the action. The Court of Appeals, Tulsa Division (Oklahoma), reversed and declared that Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 109 (1981) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: A building had been standing approximately 20 years when the ceiling collapsed. The buildings tenant suffered damages which were paid by its insurer. Subsequently, the insurer filed a subrogation against defendants. The action was brought under both tort and contract theories. The trial court found that the insurer's action was barred by Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 109 (1981), which limited defendants liability for injuries occurring more than 10 years after the completion of construction to a real property. The appellate court reversed. The court granted certiorari and found that § 109 was constitutional. The court did not measure the constitutionality of § 109 against Okla. Const. art. 23, § 7. The court found that Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 109 did not disturb the insurers vested right because there was no cause of action for the injury. Thus, there was no vesting of substantive rights and no denial of a remedy. The court further found that § 109 was a statute of repose. Accordingly, the court vacated the appellate court's decision and affirmed the trial court's order dismissing the action.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the decision of the appellate court and affirmed the trial court's order dismissing the action.

BANE v. ANDERSON, BRYANT & CO.


No. 68048


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1989 OK 140; 786 P.2d 1230; 1989 Okla. LEXIS 170



October 24, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended November 2, 1989..


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Honorable Jack Parr, Judge. Defendants appeal a jury verdict returned on plaintiff's claims of state securities violations, breach of contract, fraud and negligence. Individual defendants Bryant and Phillips ask to be made parties appellant. Phillips' request to file petition in error out of time is denied. Bryant's request is in substance an amended petition in error, and correction of the style to show him as a party appellant is permitted. Finding no reversible error in the proceedings below the judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff investor sought recovery from defendants, a brokerage firm, and two brokers, for state securities violations, breach of contract, fraud, and negligence regarding the handling of her Keogh account. The District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) awarded the investor recovery from the firm and the brokers, jointly and severally, as well as attorney's fees and costs. The firm and the brokers sought review.


OVERVIEW: The investor placed her Keogh account with the firm in a limited partnership securities project after she was advised that it was approved for Keogh status and that the firm was authorized to make Keogh investments. After the 60-day period for the transfer of such an investment without penalty elapsed, the firm advised the investor that it was not qualified to maintain Keogh accounts. On appeal, the court affirmed the lower court's judgment. Even though he was not specifically named as a party, the court held that the broker who was represented by the same lawyers as the firm properly invoked the court's appellate jurisdiction because many of the issues raised by the lawyers concerned him. However, other broker's appeal was rejected because his appeal was not timely. The court affirmed the award against the broker individually on the basis that an agent was individually liable for acts of fraud or negligence. The court held that most of the objections to the damage award were not properly preserved for review, but that the award was based on competent evidence. The court also held that the objections to the award of attorney's fees were waived because they were not timely filed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment.

ANDERSON v. DYCO PETROLEUM CORP.


No. 61,637


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1989 OK 132; 782 P.2d 1367; 1989 Okla. LEXIS 159; 107 Oil & Gas Rep. 504



October 10, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Roger Mills County, Honorable Gary P. McGinn, Trial Judge. Appellants, owners of various percentages of the working interest in a natural gas well located in Roger Mills County sued another working interest owner, Dyco Petroleum Corporation and two gas purchasers, El Paso Natural Gas Company and Panhandle Eastern Pipe Line Company, who had been purchasing gas from the well from Dyco and other working interest owners. Appellants brought three causes of action for monetary relief: 1) a common law claim for conversion as to that percentage of gas asserted to be equal to their individual percentages in the working interest; 2) a claim pursuant to certain Oklahoma statutes, 52 O.S. 1981, §§ 23, 24, 24.1, 233, 239 and 240, that the gas purchasers were required to purchase gas ratably from the various working interest owners in proportion to their interests in the well and the two gas purchasers failed to fulfill this obligation; and 3) a claim pursuant to 52 O.S. Supp. 1983, §§ 541-547, that the gas purchasers were required to pay each working interest owner for gas purchased in proportion to their individual interests. In addition, Appellants claimed in the third cause pursuant to §§ 541-547 that Dyco was similarly required to pay them for gas sold  [***2] and although required, it had refused to allow them to ratify agreement(s) between Dyco and the gas purchasers for sale of the well's gas. Upon motion for summary judgment of Appellee, Panhandle, the trial court ruled it was without subject matter jurisdiction over the causes of action in relation to Panhandle. It ruled the causes against it were preempted by force of the Supremacy Clause to the United States Constitution [U.S.CONST. art. VI, cl. 2] because of the existence of two federal enactments [the Natural Gas Act, 15 U.S.C. § 717 et seq. and the Natural Gas Policy Act, 15 U.S.C. § 3301 et seq.] which contain regulations relating to the natural gas industry, particularly interstate pipeline companies, of which Panhandle is one. The causes of action were dismissed as to Panhandle and judgment was rendered in its favor. Held: The dismissal of Panhandle from the case is upheld for reasons which do not require reaching the federal preemption issue deemed dispositive by the trial court. Dismissal was appropriate as to the first cause of action because under the material facts as to which there is no genuine dispute Appellants have no common law claim for conversion against Panhandle.  [***3] As to the second cause Appellants have no claim because the statutes relied on either do not apply to mandate "ratable" purchasing of working interest owners' proportionate share of gas in one well, but rather to purchasing patterns in relation to multiple wells in a common source of supply or between sources of supply or they do not apply to regulate purchasing of natural gas at all, but to the transportation or production thereof. Finally, Appellants have abandoned or waived any issue or error concerning the trial court's ruling as to §§ 541-547 relied on in their third cause by their failure to present any argument or authority in relation to those provisions in their briefs submitted to this Court. AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a group of working interest owners in a natural gas well, challenged a summary judgment from the District Court of Roger Mills County (Oklahoma) in favor of appellee, a natural gas pipeline company. The owners had brought multiple causes alleging that they were entitled to be paid in proportion to their respective working interests in the well for the gas purchased, but that neither the company or other parties, so paid.


OVERVIEW: Only the pipeline company obtained the summary judgment, but other named parties included various petroleum concerns. The first cause alleged by the owners sounded in tort for conversion of their respective proportionate share of gas. The second was for violation of Oklahoma "ratable" take statutes. The third cause sought to allow the owners the opportunity to ratify any agreement to sell gas entered into by another working interest owner and a purchaser under certain guidelines and to be paid in proportion to their interest. The court held that: (1) State regulations requiring interstate purchasers to take or purchase gas ratably from producers were preempted by federal regulatory power over interstate pipelines' costs and purchasing patterns exercised by the Federal Energy Regulatory Commission; (2) the "ratable" take statutes that did apply to regulate gas purchasing did not apply to mandate nondiscrimination on the part of natural gas purchasers in relation to their purchasing practices between working interest owners in a single well; and (3) rather, they applied only to situations where multiple wells were involved in a common source of supply or between sources of supply.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision from the trial court.

TAYLOR v. CITY OF OKLAHOMA CITY


No. 68,409


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1989 OK 129; 782 P.2d 1363; 1989 Okla. LEXIS 155



October 3, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals, Division IV, original proceedings to review order of the Workers' Compensation Court, Honorable Clint G. Livingston, Trial Judge. Original Proceedings to review order of three judge panel of Workers' Compensation Court affirming the trial judge's finding that claim for change of condition for the worse was barred by limitations. The Court of Appeals, Division IV, reversed. CERTIORARI PREVIOUSLY GRANTED. COURT OF APPEALS OPINION VACATED. ORDER OF THE WORKERS' COMPENSATION COURT SUSTAINED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, City of Oklahoma City, Oklahoma, own risk, and the Oklahoma worker's compensation court, sought review of an order of the Court of Appeals, Division IV (Oklahoma), which reversed an order of respondent worker's compensation court's three-judge review panel. The panel's order affirmed a prior denial of petitioner employee's motion to reopen his claim on change of condition for the worse on the ground that it was not timely filed.


OVERVIEW: The employee was awarded permanent partial disability benefits. He later moved to reopen his claim on change of condition for the worse. The city did not reply to his motion. However, at trial it raised the defense that the motion was time-barred under Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 43 (1981). The worker's compensation court trial judge ruled for the City. A three-judge panel of that court affirmed that ruling. However, the intermediate appellate court reversed the panel's order. On further appeal, the court held that the City did not waive the limitations defense by failing to raise it in a reply to the motion. The court found that Worker's Comp. Ct. R. 9, Okla. Stat. tit. 85, ch. 4, app. (1981) did not require that such an issue be raised before a hearing on the merits. The court noted that the motion was a form 9 proceeding, and that there was no rule or statute requiring a response to such a proceeding. Further, the court held that the employee failed to preserve the waiver issue for review by setting it forth in his request for review, as required by Worker's Comp. Ct. R. 30, Okla. Stat. tit. 85, ch. 4, app. (1981). Therefore, the employee was deemed to have waived that alleged error.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the intermediate appellate court's opinion, which reversed the worker's compensation court's three-judge review panel's order in favor of the City. The court reinstated the panel's order, which denied the employee's motion to reopen his claim on change of condition for the worse as untimely.

WELLS FARGO CREDIT CORP. v. ZIEGLER


No. 70,539


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1989 OK 113; 780 P.2d 703; 1989 Okla. LEXIS 134



July 18, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Tulsa County, Oklahoma, Honorable Robert Caldwell, Trial Judge. Pending a mortgage foreclosure suit wherein mortgagee had filed a notice of lis pendens, the mortgagee failed to receive notice sent by certified mail of a tax resale of the mortgaged property. Owner of resale tax deed was held to take title subject to the mortgage. AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant purchasers sought review of the decision of the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which invalidated their purchase of property at a tax resale pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 24331 (1986), because the mortgagee had not received notice of the sale. The purchasers asserted that their publication of the sale and their mailing of the notice were sufficient to meet the requirements of § 24331.


OVERVIEW: The trial court invalidated the purchase of certain property at a tax resale pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 24331 (1986), because the mortgagee had not received notice of this sale. This decision was affirmed by the court. Although the purchasers had published their sale and attempted to mail the mortgagee, the court noted that in the absence of reasonable diligence, the requirements of § 24331 could not be said to have been met. Further, the court noted that the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment required notice to be given to any person facing the deprivation of a property right. In this sense, the act of mailing did not constitute notice. The court rejected the mortgagee's argument that the posting of a bond was a prerequisite to the appeal and also found that attorney's fees were properly awarded to the mortgagee under Okla. Stat. tit. 42, § 176.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's award of judgment to the mortgagee.

Dow Jones & Co. v. State


No. 70,663


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1989 Okla. LEXIS 114; 16 Media L. Rep. 2049



July 5, 1989, Filed; As Amended July 18, 1989


PRIOR HISTORY: ON APPEAL FROM THE OKLAHOMA TAX COMMISSION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of a judgment of the Oklahoma Tax Commission, which denied its protest against the assessment of a use tax deficiency against the taxpayer on distribution of its publications within the state.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer published and circulated several newspapers. Most issues of the publications were sold by subscription and delivered by mail. Oklahoma assessed a use tax deficiency against the taxpayer on distribution of its publications within the state during a five-year period of time. The taxpayer challenged the assessment, by arguing that a subscription to one of its papers was a series of transactions, each less than 75 cents, and should hence be exempt from taxation by Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 1357(C) (1981), and taxation of its publications base on sales price or distribution method offended both the United States and the Oklahoma Constitutions. An administrative law judge concluded that the purchase of a magazine or newspaper subscription was a single transaction and since § 1357(C) exemption did not apply, the assessment was proper because during the assessment period the price of a subscription one of the newspapers was found to exceed 75 cents. Based on the administrative judge's conclusion the Commission denied the taxpayer's protest. On review, the court reversed. The court held that § 1357 (C) was invalid as an impermissible burden on the right to disseminate information.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the Commission's judgment that denied the taxpayer's protest.

Ingram v. Oneok, Inc.

Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1989 OK 82; 775 P.2d 810; 1989 Okla. LEXIS 96; 4 I.E.R. Cas. (BNA) 1531; 117 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P56,468



May 30, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals, Division I. On appeal from the District Court, Tulsa County, Robert J. Scott, Judge, Court of Appeals, Division 1, reversed the trial court's order dismissing employee's retaliatory discharge claim as barred by the two-year statute of limitations. The Court of Appeals, Hunter, P.J., rejected the opinion of its sister division rendered in Mullins v. John Zink Co., 733 P.2d 888 (Okl. App. 1986), and held employee's claim was governed by the three-year statute of limitations.



DISPOSITION:  CERTIORARI PREVIOUSLY GRANTED, OPINION OF COURT OF APPEALS AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant employer appealed on certiorari a judgment of the Court of Appeals, Division I (Oklahoma), which reversed a trial court order dismissing plaintiff employee's retaliatory discharge claim as time-barred, rejected the opinion of a sister division, and found that the employee's claim was governed by the three-year statute of limitations in Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 95 (1981).


OVERVIEW: The employee filed an action under the Workers' Compensation Retaliatory Discharge Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 85, §§ 5-7 (1981) (act), more than two but less than three years after the discharge. The trial court, following a sister division of the appeals court decision, dismissed the action as time-barred under Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 95 (Third)(1981). The appeals court reversed, finding that Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 95 (Second)(1981) applied. The court granted certiorari in order to resolve the conflict between the divisions. Affirming, the court held that the liability imposed under the act was purely statutory because there was no common law liability for discharging an employee at will with or without cause; therefore, the three-year statute of limitations applied because "but for the statute" no liability would have existed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appeals court's judgment.
