Bowlin v. Alley


No. 61,099


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1989 OK 66; 773 P.2d 365; 1989 Okla. LEXIS 72



May 2, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals, Division No. 4. In a temporary and permanent injunction suit, the trial court vacated the temporary injunction against appellees, denied permanent injunction and quieting title to appellees' property against all claims by appellants. The trial court further entered judgment against appellants for reasonable attorney's fees. From an unpublished opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division No. 4, affirming, appellants sought certiorari, which has been previously granted. Court of Appeals Opinion Vacated. District Court's Judgment Denying Permanent Injunction, Vacating Temporary Injunction and Quieting Title to Appellees' Property Against all Claims by Appellants is Affirmed; Judgment Awarding Attorney's Fees is Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimants sought certiorari review of a decision of the Court of Appeals (Oklahoma), which held that the claimants lacked standing to challenge Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 1392 (1981) and affirmed a trial court judgment that vacated a temporary injunction against appellee landowners to restrain them from interfering with claimants' ingress and egress rights, denied a permanent injunction, quieted title, and awarded fees under § 1392.


OVERVIEW: An access road dividing the parties' properties had been built on the eastern half of a formerly unimproved dedicated street. The claimants utilized the access road as the only route to their driveway; however, the landowners alleged that the access road was deeded to them. The court found that the trial court properly made its decision based upon the original deed and that there was sufficient evidence to show that the deed's omission of the road was inadvertent. Further, when the street was vacated, the access road reverted to the former owners, and the claimants had no right to the property that entitled them to injunctive relief. The appellate court erred in finding that the claimants lacked standing to challenge § 1392, because the claimants had a personal stake in the outcome where the claimants were obligated under the statute to pay the fees. The statute provided for damages occasioned by a temporary deprivation if the deprivation proved to be erroneous. The court found that § 1392 was constitutional and did not violate equal protection. The provision related to no suspect classifications, and the litigants were distinguished as dissimilar upon a permissible basis.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the appellate court's opinion and affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Cities Serv. Gas Co. v. Okla. Tax Comm'n


No. 70,127


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1989 OK 69; 774 P.2d 468; 1989 Okla. LEXIS 79; 103 Oil & Gas Rep. 648



May 2, 1989 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Honorable Bryan C. Dixon, Trial Judge. After the appellants paid the Oklahoma conservation excise tax under protest, they filed this action alleging that the severance tax on natural and casinghead gas was unconstitutional seeking a refund. The trial court found that the tax neither discriminates nor places an undue burden on interstate commerce. It further found that the tax did not violate the Supremacy Clause, the Due Process Clause or the Equal Protection Clause. We find that: 1) The conservation excise tax is in harmony with the Commerce Clause, Due Process Clause and the Equal Protection Clause. It is fairly apportioned, it does not discriminate against interstate commerce, and it is fairly related to services which the state provides to the taxpayer. 2) The conservation excise tax is not in conflict with the Federal Natural Gas Act, the Supremacy Clause, or the authority of the Federal Energy Regulatory Commission under 15 U.S.C. § 3320 (1978).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant pipeline companies sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which determined that the Oklahoma Conservation Excise Tax, set forth in Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 1108 (1981), and imposed by appellee Oklahoma Tax Commission, did not violate the Commerce Clause, the Supremacy Clause, the Due Process Clause, or the Equal Protection Clause.


OVERVIEW: Oklahoma levied a tax on the severance of natural gas and casinghead gas. Although the tax was levied on the producers, the pipeline companies, which purchased natural gas in Oklahoma and sold it outside the state, paid the tax under protest. The pipeline companies commenced an action alleging that the tax violated the provisions of both the United States and Oklahoma Constitutions. On appeal, the court held that the tax did not violate the Commerce Clause, Due Process Clause, or the Equal Protection Clause. Applying a four-pronged test to determine whether the state excise tax on interstate commerce was permissible, the court held that: (1) the tax had a substantial nexus to Oklahoma because it was applied to the severance of natural gas in Oklahoma; (2) the tax was fairly apportioned because the tax was computed at the same rate regardless of the gas's final destination; (3) the tax did not discriminate against interstate commerce because the tax was a compensatory one; and (4) the tax's purpose was to provide funds for energy preservation programs and other state programs. The court also held that the tax did not conflict with either the Supremacy Clause or the Natural Gas Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the Commission.

 

155 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Richardson v. Mustang Fuel Corp.


No. 65,361


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1989 OK 53; 772 P.2d 1324; 1989 Okla. LEXIS 53; 104 Oil & Gas Rep. 56



April 4, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals, Division No. 3, District Court of Oklahoma County, Honorable Leamon Freeman, Judge. Landowners seek certiorari to review decision of the Court of Appeals reversing the trial court's order permanently enjoining pipeline operator from curtailing gas supply pursuant to right of way contracts. Certiorari having been granted, the Court of Appeals opinion is vacated and is withdrawn from publication. The order of the trial court is AFFIRMED AS MODIFIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners appealed a decision in favor of defendant gas supplier by the Court of Appeals (Oklahoma) in an injunctive action to prevent the supplier's termination of gas services to the landowners.


OVERVIEW: The landowners gave the supplier an easement across their land for the supplier's pipeline in exchange for a specific reservation on the right for the landowners to purchase gas at the same cost as a nearby city. When the supplier sought to shut off the gas pursuant to later contracts, the landowners claimed that the supplier was bound by the original easement agreement to continue the provision of gas. The Court of Appeals reversed the decision in favor of the landowners because the supplier provided notice of termination of service under the later contracts. The court held that the supplier had to continue to supply gas as long as it did not abandon the right of way. The later contracts did not replace or rescind the original contracts because it did not mention the original contracts. The covenant to supply gas was a covenant that ran with the land because it touched and concerned the land. The court reasoned that the supplier and the landowners both had benefits and burdens under the easement contract, which gave the supplier the right to run the pipeline. The decision to grant an injunction to require the continuation of gas services was within the trial court's discretion.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the decision in favor of the supplier, ruled in favor of the landowners, and modified the trial court's order so as to state that the supplier's covenant to provide gas to the landowners ran with the land.

 

156 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Trett v. Okla. Gas & Elec. Co.


No. 67,352


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1989 OK 54; 775 P.2d 275; 1989 Okla. LEXIS 60



April 4, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals, Oklahoma City Divisions, Appeal from District Court of Murray County, Honorable J. Kenneth Love, Trial Judge. Appellee Trett was injured by an electrical shock he received while moving concrete bridge panels when the machinery transporting the panels touched a high voltage line owned by O.G.&E. Appellee brought this suit against O.G.&E. alleging negligence in the maintenance of its lines in that the lines were too low to the ground or that O.G.&E. did not act timely to move the lines when it had knowledge of the pending bridge construction. The trial court overruled O.G.&E.'s demurrer to the evidence and motions for directed verdict and sent the case to the jury. The jury returned a verdict for Trett finding O.G.&E. to be 34.17 percent negligent and Trett's employer to be 63.33 percent negligent. O.G.&E. appealed and the Court of Appeals, Oklahoma City Divisions, affirmed. This Court has granted certiorari on petition by O.G.&E. to review the application of the appropriate standard of review which should have been applied by the Court of Appeals. OPINION OF COURT OF APPEALS VACATED; JUDGMENT OF TRIAL COURT REVERSED AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.



DISPOSITION:  OPINION OF COURT OF APPEALS VACATED; JUDGMENT OF TRIAL COURT REVERSED AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On certiorari to the Court of Appeals, Oklahoma City Division (Oklahoma), appellant electric carrier challenged a judgment of the District Court of Murray County (Oklahoma), finding the carrier partially negligent in a personal injury action brought by appellee. The injury resulted from an electrical shock received by appellee when he touched construction equipment that came into contact with a high voltage line maintained by the carrier.


OVERVIEW: The height of the carrier's lines conformed to state and federal safety codes. Appellee's employer, however, commenced bridge construction work under the lines knowing that its actions violated both the "six-foot clearance" rule set forth in Okla. Stat. tit. 63, § 981 (1981) and its agreement with the carrier to move the lines before commencement of construction. Accordingly, the court held that in order to establish the carrier's liability, appellee was required to offer evidence to establish that it was foreseeable to the carrier that the employer would undertake construction activities in violation of state statutes and would also ignore the contractual provisions agreed to between the carrier and the employer in conformance with those same statutes. Having offered no such evidence, appellee failed to establish the exceptional circumstances needed to create a duty on the part of the carrier.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the opinion of the court of appeals, reversed the judgment of the district court, and remanded the matter with directions to enter the judgment for the carrier.

 

157 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Beacon Realty Invs. Co. v. Cantrell


No. 59,790


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1989 OK 44; 771 P.2d 602; 1989 Okla. LEXIS 49



March 21, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals, Division No. 4. Action by taxpayers against Tulsa County Treasurer and other county officials to obtain refund of ad valorem taxes. The trial court granted summary judgment to defendants. The Court of Appeals vacated the trial court judgment and remanded with directions. CERTIORARI PREVIOUSLY GRANTED; COURT OF APPEALS OPINION AFFIRMED IN PART, VACATED IN PART; CAUSE REMANDED WITH INSTRUCTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, county treasurer and other county officials, sought review of the judgment of the Court of Appeals (Oklahoma), which vacated the judgment of the trial court granting summary judgment to appellants in an action by appellee taxpayers to obtain a refund of ad valorem taxes.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers claimed that the county assessor arbitrarily increased the fair cash value of their various properties by 66-2/3 percent and decreased the assessment ratio from 25 to 15 percent. No notice whatsoever of this reevaluation was given to the taxpayers, and they did not know of it until they received tax statements toward the end of the year. By then it was too late to seek relief from the county Board of Equalization. The taxpayers asserted that the valuation increase was void for lack of notice and that their properties should be assessed at 15 percent of the lesser previous year's fair cash value fixed by the assessor. The court held that: (1) the arbitrary fair cash valuation increase without notice was invalid; (2) the proper assessment percentage applicable to the property was 15 percent; (3) the taxpayers did not concede that the increased fair cash value set by the assessor was an accurate appraisal; (4) the taxpayers' failure to pay the alleged excess tax under protest did not prevent its recovery; and (5) the court's decision would apply prospectively.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part, vacated as to the summary judgment entered in favor of appellants, and remanded the cause with directions to enter judgment for the taxpayers for the amount of refund due them after figuring the ad valorem tax on the basis of 15 percent of the previous year's fair cash value.

Burkhardt v. City of Enid


No. 70,197


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1989 OK 45; 771 P.2d 608; 1989 Okla. LEXIS 45



March 21, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Garfield County, Oklahoma Honorable Richard Pickens, Judge.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers appealed the judgment of the District Court of Garfield County (Oklahoma), which ruled in favor of defendant city and intervenor university in the taxpayers' action challenging the constitutionality of an ordinance that established a voter-approved sales tax to fund the city's purchase of the university's campus.


OVERVIEW: The city was suffering a severe economic decline, and it was anticipated that the university, a private, non-profit corporation that was the city's only institution of higher learning, would fail. The city developed a plan to purchase the university's campus and lease the property back to the university. The plan was financed by a sales tax that was approved by city voters. The taxpayers filed an action challenging the ordinance that established the sales tax, and the court affirmed the trial court's judgment for the city and university. The court held that the plan did not subsidize a private institution with the use of public funds in violation of Okla. Const. art. 10, § 14 because the overwhelming benefits to the community brought the plan within the provision's definition of public purpose. There was adequate consideration to demonstrate that the plan was not an impermissible gift or loan to the university, and the plan was valid under Okla. Const. art. 2, § 5 because the university was not a sectarian institution. Finally, the ordinance was not unconstitutionally vague, as the term "economic development" was adequately defined to communicate the purpose of the tax.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

159 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


STATE v. GOFORTH


No. 66,675


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1989 OK 37; 772 P.2d 911; 1989 Okla. LEXIS 31



March 7, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals, Oklahoma City Division. Trial Judge of the Oklahoma County District Court, The Honorable Jack Parr. The trial court sustained the appellees' motion to set aside a bond forfeiture finding that 59 O.S. Supp. 1984 § 1332 should be applied to an unlicensed bondsman, because a licensed bondsman, under the same statute and circumstances, would not forfeit the bond after a plea of guilty by the defendant. The State of Oklahoma appealed, and the Court of Appeals reversed the trial court. On certiorari, we find that the Okla. Const., art. 5, § 46 requires that unlicensed bondsmen be afforded the same statutory protections concerning exoneration from liability as a licensed bondsman. CERTIORARI GRANTED; OPINION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS VACATED; JUDGMENT OF THE TRIAL COURT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant unlicensed bondsman sought review of an order from the Oklahoma Court of Appeals, which reversed the trial court's judgment that granted the bondsman's motion to set aside a bond forfeiture because Okla. Stat. tit. 59, § 1332 (Supp. 1984) should apply to unlicensed as well as licensed bondsmen.


OVERVIEW: The bondsman was the grandfather of defendant. He posted bond for his grandson. The terms of the bond form required defendant to appear before the trial court on December 16, 1985 and answer the charge against him. Defendant appeared, pled guilty, and was sentenced to 10 years in prison. Upon defendant's request, the sentencing was continued for 30 days. The bondsman was not present when defendant pled guilty and did not agree to remain on the bond during the 30 days before formal sentencing. If he had been a licensed bondsman, he would have been exonerated from liability under § 1332 at this point. Defendant failed to appear for sentencing, and the bond was ordered forfeited. Upon review, the court found that Okla. Const. art. 5, § 46 required that the statutory protections concerning exoneration from liability had to apply to both licensed and unlicensed bondsmen. The state had created an unconstitutional regulatory scheme, which created two classes in identical circumstances that were treated differently insofar as the exoneration of the bail bond was concerned.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order from the court of appeals that reversed a trial court's judgment, which granted the bondman's motion to set aside a bond forfeiture. The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Manzanares v. Manzanares


No. 70,403


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1989 OK 24; 769 P.2d 156; 1989 Okla. LEXIS 19



February 14, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Cleveland County, Honorable Preston Trimble, Judge. Wife challenges the amount of a child support award. Although the trial judge expressly declined to follow the Supreme Court's Child Support Guidelines on the basis they were an unconstitutional infringement of the trial court's discretion, he stated at a subsequent hearing the award was based on the equities of the case and on the disparity of the financial information.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant wife sought review of an order of the District Court of Cleveland County (Oklahoma), which directed the amount of a child support award to be paid to her by appellee husband.


OVERVIEW: At the time of the parties' divorce decree, the Oklahoma Supreme Court Child Support Guidelines were in effect. The trial judge declined to follow the guidelines on the basis that they were an unconstitutional infringement of the trial court's discretion. At a subsequent hearing, the trial judge stated that the amount awarded was based upon the equities of the case after consideration of the conflicting guidelines submitted by the parties. He noted that the evidence concerning the amount of the husband's gross income was disputed. The court ruled that the trial judge's statements at the subsequent hearing satisfied the requirement of a specific finding of fact justifying the deviation from the guidelines based upon the extraordinary circumstances. The court further held that the child support awarded was not clearly against the weight of the evidence and thus the trial court did not abuse its discretion. The issue regarding the constitutionality of the guidelines was moot because they were no longer effective or enforceable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

Guinn v. Church of Christ of Collinsville


No. 62,154


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1989 OK 8; 775 P.2d 766; 1989 Okla. LEXIS 10



January 17, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On appeal from the District Court, Tulsa County, Tony M. Graham, Judge. In an action for damages from invasion of privacy and intentional infliction of emotional distress, brought by a former parishioner against the congregation and its leadership, judgment was rendered on a jury verdict for the plaintiff. On appeal by the defendants. JUDGMENT IS REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former parishioner brought an action against defendants, her former church and its elders, alleging invasion of privacy and intentional infliction of emotional distress for words the elders spoke regarding her private life. The District Court, Tulsa County (Oklahoma) entered judgment in favor of the former parishioner. The elders appealed.


OVERVIEW: The issue on appeal was whether a state forensic inquiry into an alleged tortious act by the church against its former parishioner was an unconstitutional usurpation of the church's prerogatives by a secular court and hence prohibited by the First Amendment. The court answered the question in the negative. The court held that the former parishioner could not recover for the pre-withdrawal disciplinary actions of the elders. Conversely, it held that the former parishioner was entitled to recover for post-withdrawal acts of the elders, which were proven to have been tortious. The court held that in testing the constitutionality of the lower court's action against the elders, the proper inquiry was whether, on the record, the elders' decision to discipline the former parishioner constituted such a threat to the public safety, peace, or order that it justified the state trial court's decision to pursue the compelling interest of providing its citizens with a means of vindicating their rights conferred by tort law. The court held that there was competent evidence to support the jury's conclusion that the elders had intended to inflict emotional harm on the former parishioner.


OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of the former parishioner was reversed and remanded for a new trial confined to actionable post-withdrawal conduct. The court directed the lower court that on remand partial summary adjudication be rendered against the former parishioner for that portion of her claim regarding the elders' pre-withdrawal acts.

 

163 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Flint Res. Co. v. State ex rel. Okla. Tax Comm'n


No. 70,024


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1989 OK 9; 780 P.2d 665; 1989 Okla. LEXIS 9



January 17, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Oklahoma Tax Commission. After the Oklahoma Tax Commission refused to allow the deduction of either the federal "gross up" or foreign taxes from taxable income the appellant/corporation appealed asserting: (1) Inclusion of the "gross up" violates due process; (2) Failure to allow a deduction for foreign taxes contravenes the commerce and due process clauses of the United States Constitution and of the Oklahoma Constitution's uniformity clause; and (3) Interest should be remitted. We find that: (1) Because the appellant was not engaged in a unitary business, inclusion of the federal "gross up" in Oklahoma taxable income violates the due process clauses of the United States and Oklahoma Constitutions. It is deductible pursuant to 68 O.S. 1981 § 2358(A)(2); (2) There is no constitutional prohibition against inclusion of foreign taxes in Oklahoma taxable income and no provision for deduction of foreign taxes within the Oklahoma Income Tax Act. Corporations electing to take the federal foreign tax credit rather than a deduction for foreign taxes paid must include the amount representing foreign taxes within Oklahoma taxable income; and (3) Because the inclusion of foreign taxes in Oklahoma taxable income has been  [***2] adequately foreshadowed, and because no provision exists in the Oklahoma Income Tax Act for its deduction, the remittur of interest is denied. However, because the tax on the foreign "gross up" was unconstitutional, the additional assessment on the "gross up" amount and the interest on the "gross up" is ordered remitted.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporation sought review of a decision of appellee, the Oklahoma Tax Commission, which refused to allow the corporation to deduct either the federal "gross up" or foreign taxes from its taxable income.


OVERVIEW: The corporation, an Oklahoma corporation, had a foreign subsidiary in South America. The foreign subsidiary also owned a subsidiary organized under the laws of Venezuela. The Venezuelan subsidiary did not conduct business or perform services in Oklahoma. Further, the activities of the foreign subsidiary and the Venezuelan subsidiary did not constitute a unitary business. The corporation reduced the amount of the foreign subsidiary's dividend income by the foreign dividend "gross-up" amounts, and it increased its deduction for taxes paid on the Oklahoma tax return. The tax commission refused to allow the deductions for the income taxes withheld by Venezuela. On appeal, the court reversed in part, holding that taxation of the federal "gross-up" violated due process because the companies were not engaged in a unitary business. Further, there was no constitutional prohibition against including foreign taxes in Oklahoma taxable income and no provision for deduction of foreign taxes. Corporations choosing to take the federal foreign tax credit, rather than a deduction for foreign taxes paid, had to include the amount representing foreign taxes within Oklahoma taxable income.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the Oklahoma Tax Commission's decision, which refused to allow the corporation to deduct either the federal "gross up" or foreign taxes from its taxable income.

Turpen v. Okla. Corp. Comm'n


Nos. 66,038, 66,686


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1988 OK 126; 769 P.2d 1309; 1988 Okla. LEXIS 143



November 8, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended January 17, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: On appeal from the Oklahoma Corporation Commission. The Attorney General appeals from an Oklahoma Corporation Commission order which authorized Southwestern Bell Telephone Company to implement permanent rates and charges to recover a revenue deficiency of $ 47,544,561.00 over and above the interim relief the Commission had previously granted. The Attorney General brings a second appeal from the Commission's ruling that dismissed his motion for modification of the contested rate order. The two appeals stand consolidated for disposition by a single opinion.
Turpen v. Oklahoma Corp. Com., 1988 Okla. LEXIS 161 (Okla., Nov. 8, 1988)



DISPOSITION:  THE COMMISSION'S DISMISSAL OF THE ATTORNEY'S GENERAL MOTION TO MODIFY THE RATE ORDER IS AFFIRMED; THE COMMISSION'S RATE ORDER IS AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART AND PROCEEDING IS REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS TO CONDUCT FURTHER INQUIRY AND MAKE ADDITIONAL FINDINGS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Attorney General sought review of the order of appellee Oklahoma Corporation Commission, which established rates and charges allowing appellee phone company to recover a revenue deficiency. The Attorney General also sought review of the Commission's ruling that dismissed his motion for modification of the contested rate order. The two appeals were consolidated for review by the court.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the commission properly dismissed the Attorney General's motion to modify because the Commission's rate order became final after 30 days, which was not tolled by filing of the motion. The court held that the Commission had adequately investigated and addressed the impact on Oklahoma ratepayers of the phone company's status as a subsidiary of a holding company, but set minimum standards to be followed in future rate relief requests. The court held that the Commission adequately investigated imputation of income and expenses between the phone company and its directory operations subsidiary and that it was within its discretion in deferring until future rate relief requests certain issues regarding transactions between the phone company and its affiliates. The court approved the capital structure upon which the rate order was based. The court held that the Commission did not address the proper treatment of reimbursements received by the phone company from AT&T pursuant to FCC order. The court held that the Commission did not provide a sufficiently detailed explanation of why it included the phone company's prepaid expenses in the rate base.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Commission's rate order in part but remanded for the Commission to address reimbursements received by the phone company from AT&T and to explain its treatment of prepaid expenses. The court also directed the Commission to address the issue of whether it was proper for the phone company to transfer assets to its directory operations subsidiary at book value.

Wofford v. Davis


No. 61,424


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1988 OK 112; 764 P.2d 161; 1988 Okla. LEXIS 126



October 18, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On Writ of Certiorari to District Court, Garfield County, for Review of Certified Interlocutory Order, Hon. James Sears Bryant. Plaintiff brought this action to recover damages resulting from an allegedly negligent sterilization proceeding. In ruling upon various demurrers the trial court applied the three-year proviso to 76 O.S. 1981 § 18 and held it barred all claims except actual medical and surgical expenses. The trial court also held no cause of action existed in this jurisdiction for expenses of rearing an unplanned child. Held: the three-year proviso of 76 O.S. § 18 is unconstitutional and no cause of action exists in Oklahoma for the expenses of rearing an unplanned and healthy child.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents sought review of the judgment of the District Court, Garfield County (Oklahoma), which entered judgment in favor of appellee doctor in an action for damages resulting from negligent sterilization. The trial court sustained the doctor's demurrers to the parents' damages claim.


OVERVIEW: The parents brought an action against their doctor for a negligently performed sterilization that resulted in a healthy but unwanted baby. The first issue before the court was whether the parents could recover the cost of rearing a healthy child as damage properly recoverable by litigants who had sought medical treatment to prevent conception. The second issue was whether the limitation of damages recoverable in a medical malpractice action filed three years or more from the date of injury was constitutional. On appeal, the court held that the parents could not be damaged by the birth of a normal, healthy child, and could not recover damages by reason of the birth of such a child. The court held that the trial court properly allowed the demurrers to that particular claim for damages. The court determined that the limitation of damages recoverable in a medical malpractice action filed three years or more from the date of injury was unconstitutional. The court stated that the statute's three-year statute of limitation was unconstitutional as measured by the Oklahoma constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's interlocutory order sustaining a demurrer to the parents' claim for damages for raising the unwanted child. The court overruled the demurrer based on the three-year statute of limitations and remanded the case to the trial court.

Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1988 OK 99; 769 P.2d 1302; 1988 Okla. LEXIS 111



September 20, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On Appeal from the District Court, Oklahoma County Raymond Naifeh, Judge. In an action to review a decision by the Board of Trustees [Board] of the Oklahoma Public Employees Retirement System (the board that administers the Uniform Retirement System for Justices and Judges) which denied the claimant's request for military service credit toward his judicial retirement benefits and concluded that 72 O.S. 1981 § 67.13a is unconstitutional, the trial court certified as a class all affected judges and their survivors, denied certification for the other state retirement systems, gave summary judgment to the claimant but declined to assess counsel fees against the Board; instead, it ordered that counsel fee and costs be paid out of the pension funds the class members recovered in the judgment.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), entered summary judgment in favor of appellee judge in his class action against appellants, the Board of Trustees of the Oklahoma Uniform Retirement System for Justices and Judges. The Board appealed the order.


OVERVIEW: The Oklahoma Legislature amended Okla. Stat. tit. 72, § 67.13a to allow military service credit for war veterans or disabled military retirees who were members of any state retirement system. The judge requested credit for his active military service. The Board denied the judge's requesting, finding that § 67.13a violated the Oklahoma Constitution. Lastly, the court held that the Board was immune from paying attorney's fees to the judge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order to grant summary judgment to the judge in his action against the Board.

Davis v. State Election Bd. of Okla.


No. 71,495


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1988 OK 95; 762 P.2d 932; 1988 Okla. LEXIS 110



September 13, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Proceeding.  [***1] An application to assume original jurisdiction and petition for writ of mandamus to require the Secretary of the Oklahoma State Election Board to place the name of petitioner, Steve Davis, on the 1988 general election ballot as an independent candidate for the office of Corporation Commissioner. JURISDICTION ASSUMED WRIT DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner candidate sought a writ of mandamus to require respondent, the Secretary of the Oklahoma State Election Board, to place the candidate's name on the general election ballot as an independent candidate for the office of corporation commissioner.


OVERVIEW: The court noted that the candidate first sought the elective office as a republican but was defeated in the primary election. Shortly before declaring his candidacy as an independent, the candidate registered as an independent voter. The State Election Board found that the candidate had violated Okla. Stat. tit. 26, § 5-105(B) (Supp. 1987) because he had not been registered as an independent for six months prior to the first day of the filing period as required under the statute. According the Board ordered the candidate's name stricken from the general election ballot. The candidate contended that § 5-105(B) conflicted with Okla. Const. art.3, § 3. Specifically, the candidate argued that the political disaffiliation requirement for independent candidates contained in § 5-105(B) unconstitutionally restricted an independent candidate's access to the ballot. The court disagreed, upholding the constitutionality of the statute. The court held that the statute actually furthered the constitutional mandate of ballot access for independents by requiring that only truly nonpartisan candidates reach the general election ballot.


OUTCOME: The court denied the petition for a writ of mandamus.

 

169 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Short v. Kiamichi Area Vocational-Technical Sch. Dist. No. 7 of Choctaw County


No. 66,179


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1988 OK 89; 761 P.2d 472; 1988 Okla. LEXIS 97



July 19, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied September 13, 1988.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Choctaw County; G. Gail Craytor, District Judge. This appeal involves the nonrenewal of a tenured teacher's contract by the Kiamichi Area Vocational-Technical School District. The teacher asserts that the failure of the school board to afford a pretermination hearing before it decided to nonrenew his contract was a denial of procedural due process. We find that under Cleveland Bd. of Educ. v. Loudermill, 470 U.S. 532, 105 S. Ct. 1487, 84 L. Ed. 2d 494 (1985), due process requires that a tenured teacher be given an opportunity to be heard prior to the school board's nonrenewal decision. We also find that the rule in this case is applicable prospectively only, and that it will become effective on the date of the issuance of the mandate. Great N. Ry. Co. v. Sunburst Oil & Refining Co, 287 U.S. 358, 364-65, 53 S. Ct. 145, 148, 77 L. Ed. 360, (1932). REVERSED.



DISPOSITION:  Reversed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant teacher sought review of the order from the District Court of Choctaw County (Oklahoma), which entered judgment in favor of appellee vocational-technical school district and held that the school board was not required to afford a pretermination hearing before it decided to nonrenew the teacher's contract. The teacher claimed that his procedural due process rights had been denied.


OVERVIEW: The teacher was employed by the school district to teach a residential wiring course. The school board advised the teacher by certified mail that his teaching contract was being nonrenewed. In accordance with Okla. Stat. tit. 70, § 6-103.4(D) (1981), the teacher sought review of the board's action before an administrative hearing panel, which upheld the boards' decision. The decision was affirmed. On appeal, the court found that a right to a pretermination hearing for tenured teachers was mandated by both the state and federal constitutions. The court held that § 6-103.4(B), insofar as it failed to provide a pretermination hearing, was unconstitutional and that post-termination remedies, however elaborate, were insufficient. The court reasoned that procedural due process required notice and an opportunity to be heard before a decision was made to terminate or to nonrenew a tenured teacher's contract; however, it held that its new ruling, which corrected a prior defect caused by reliance on a constitutionally infirm statute, was to be applied prospectively because applying it retrospectively would adversely effect and increase the workload of school boards.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment holding that the school board was not required to afford a pretermination hearing before it decided to nonrenew a teacher's contract but ordered that its ruling was to be applied prospectively, and not to the appealing teacher's case.

Reynolds v. Porter


No. 60,253


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1988 OK 88; 760 P.2d 816; 1988 Okla. LEXIS 99



July 19, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the District Court, Oklahoma County, Jack Parr, Judge. In a medical malpractice action the trial court rendered partial summary judgment for the defendant pursuant to 76 O.S. 1981 § 18, finding that the action could be maintained as timely brought within two years of discovery of the injury but that because the action was brought more than three years from the date of the injury it is limited to recovery of actual medical and surgical expenses. The trial court certified for review the question of the constitutionality of § 18's three-year proviso. CERTIORARI GRANTED; THE TRIAL COURT'S CERTIFIED INTERLOCUTORY ORDER REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff challenged the decision of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which in a medical malpractice action rendered partial summary judgment for defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant performed an allegedly negligent operation on plaintiff. Plaintiff claimed that she did not learn that she was injured until four years later when she filed her medical malpractice action. The trial court granted defendant partial summary judgment and certified for review plaintiff's attack on the constitutionality of the three-year proviso in Okla. Stat. tit. 76 § 18 (1981) as it operated to limit damages. The court reversed, holding that because the critical provision in Okla. Stat. tit. 76, § 18 (1981), which limited the scope of recoverable damages after a three-year time lapse, was a special statute of limitation, it was absolutely proscribed by Okla. Const. art. 5, § 46.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's summary judgment in an action by plaintiff to recover for medical malpractice.

 

171 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Enter. Mgmt. Consultants v. State ex rel. Okla. Tax Comm'n


No. 66,708


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1988 OK 91; 768 P.2d 359; 1988 Okla. LEXIS 98



July 19, 1988 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Rehearing Granted in Part and Denied in Part February 6, 1989; As Amended February 6, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Oklahoma Tax Commission. A non-Indian corporation, its officers and directors appeal from an Oklahoma Tax Commission order that denied their protest of a sales tax assessment on revenues from bingo and concession activities which they conducted upon tribal lands. These taxpayers were found not to be the Tribe's agent but rather a "vendor" within the meaning of the Oklahoma Sales Tax Code and hence liable for the collection and remittance of the sales tax from the bingo operation. AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of a decision of appellee, the Oklahoma Tax Commission, denying the taxpayers' protest of a sales tax assessment on revenues from bingo and concession activities that they conducted upon tribal lands. The taxpayers were found not to be a tribe's agent but rather a "vendor" within the meaning of the Oklahoma Sales Tax Code and thus liable for the collection and remittance of the sales tax from the bingo operation.


OVERVIEW: The corporate taxpayer was a non-Indian corporation that conducted bingo games and food concession sales on tribal lands. The court found that the taxpayer had failed to prove that it was the tribe's agent in regard to the bingo operation. Thus, it was unnecessary to determine whether the imposition of a sales tax on such revenues was an unconstitutional infringement upon tribal self-government or whether a tax on bingo activities on tribal land was preempted by federal law. The court found that the contractual agreements between the corporate taxpayer and the tribe did not establish that the essential characteristics of an agency relationship were present, i.e., that the corporate taxpayer owed a fiduciary duty to the tribe and had agreed to be subject to its control. The court also rejected the taxpayers' argument that the written agreement released them from responsibility for the payment of the sales tax. The taxpayers, as a "vendor" under Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 1352(R)(1) (1987) and Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 1361(A) (1986), had the duty to collect and remit the sales tax, and such a duty could not be avoided by contrary contract provisions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Commission's denial of relief from the sales tax assessed against the taxpayers.

Travelers Ins. Co. v. L. V. French Truck Serv.


No. 63,052


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1988 OK 76; 770 P.2d 551; 1988 Okla. LEXIS 82



July 5, 1988, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Amended March 28, 1989..


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals, Div. 3. In an action by a subrogated liability carrier against an employer to recover payout made to satisfy an agreed judgment against insured-electric company in a previous tort action arising from plaintiff-employee's work-related injuries, the employer, who satisfied compensation obligation owing to employee, moved for summary judgment. The District Court, Kingfisher County, Robert Lovell, Judge, gave summary judgment to the carrier. The Court of Appeals reversed. Upon carrier's petition, certiorari is granted.



DISPOSITION:  OPINION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS VACATED; SUMMARY JUDGMENT REVERSED AND CAUSE REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff subrogated liability carrier sought certiorari review of the opinion of the Court of Appeals (Oklahoma), which reversed the trial court's award of summary judgment for the carrier in its action against defendant employer to recover a payout made to satisfy a judgment in a previous tort action arising from a work-related injury to an employee.


OVERVIEW: One of the employer's workers was injured when he suffered a severe electrical shock from a power line. Pursuant to a tort action, the carrier paid a judgment to the employee and then filed an action against the employer seeking to recover the payout. When the employer filed a motion for summary judgment, the trial court awarded summary judgment sua sponte to the carrier, and the intermediate appellate court reversed. The court vacated the intermediate appellate court's opinion, reversed the trial court's judgment, and remanded. The court held that the immunity afforded the employer by Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 12 of the Workers' Compensation Act did not extend to the liability imposed by Okla. Stat. tit. 63, § 984, the law regulating power lines. Also, because the carrier sued the employer within three years after it paid the judgment, the action was not time-barred, and claim preclusion was not applicable. However, the trial court failed to express a valid basis for giving judgment to the carrier, and there were material facts as to liability. As substantial factual issues raised by the pleadings remained undetermined, summary judgment was inappropriate and remand was warranted.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the opinion of the intermediate appellate court, reversed the trial court's judgment, and remanded the cause with directions.

Fed. Land Bank of Wichita v. Story


No. 68,077


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1988 OK 52; 756 P.2d 588; 1988 Okla. LEXIS 51



May 3, 1988 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the District Court of Craig County, Oklahoma The Honorable William J. Whistler, District Judge. Supp. 1986, §§ 492, 493. The trial court found the Act unconstitutional. The State intervened and timely filed a brief. Without hearing evidence or argument by the State, the trial court affirmed its earlier ruling that the Act is unconstitutional. The landowners and the State appeal.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee bank instituted a mortgage foreclosure action, and appellant landowner sought shelter from the foreclosure under the Oklahoma Mortgage Foreclosure Moratorium Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 62, §§ 492, 493. The District Court of Craig County (Oklahoma) held the Act was unconstitutional, and the State petitioned for writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: The bank brought a mortgage foreclosure action, and the landowners sought shelter from the foreclosure under the Oklahoma Mortgage Foreclosure Moratorium Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 62, §§ 492, 493. The trial court found the Act unconstitutional. The State intervened, and the landowners and State appealed. In affirming, the court held that the by prohibiting foreclosure of mortgages in existence prior to the effective date of the Act, the Act unconstitutionally impaired existing contracts because the moratorium operated as an arbitrary and capricious extension of time amounting to a taking of private property without compensation or protection of the rights of the mortgagee. Therefore, Okla. Stat. tit. 62, § 493 was not a reasonable exercise of the police power devoted to a legitimate end in view of the emergency.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed. The cases were remanded.

Wilson v. Gipson


No. 62,087


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1988 OK 35; 753 P.2d 1349; 1988 Okla. LEXIS 37



April 5, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Honorable David M. Cook and Carmon C. Harris, District Judges. Parents of children injured and killed in explosion of water heater at a public school brought an action against the school district and its employees. School district and insurance carrier filed an interpleader proceeding and paid the policy limits to the trial court for distribution. The court distributed all funds and relieved school district, its agents and employees, and insurance carrier from any further liability and/or duty to defend. The parents appealed. ORDERS OF THE DISTRICT COURT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parents sought review of a decision of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which distributed all insurance funds and relieved appellees, school district, employees, and insurance carrier, from any further liability or duty to defend in the parents' action to recover damages for the injuries and death of their children due to an explosion of a water heater at a public school.


OVERVIEW: A hot water heater in the cafeteria at a public school exploded killing five children. One teacher died and several other children were injured. The children's parents filed suit against the school district, three employees, and various manufacturers of the hot water tank and its component parts. The court held that: (1) the Political Subdivision Tort Claims Act, Okla. Const. art. 23, § 7, which embodied the statutory right of action for wrongful death.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the district court.

Kline v. State ex rel. Okla. Water Res. Bd.


Nos. 65,540, 65544


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1988 OK 18; 759 P.2d 210; 1988 Okla. LEXIS 21



February 23, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Woodward County, Oklahoma, Honorable Ray Dean Linder, District Judge. Pursuant to provisions of the Oklahoma Groundwater Law, 82 O.S. 1981, § 1020.1 et seq., the Oklahoma Water Resources Board determined maximum annual yield to be allocated to each acre of land overlying the groundwater basin of the alluvium and terrace deposits of the Beaver-North Canadian River in Blaine, Major, Dewey, Harper and Woodward Counties in northwestern Oklahoma. In the District Court of Woodward County, Appellant-landowners sought review of the Board's determination of maximum annual yield. Appellants were joined by the Intervenor, Western Farmers Electric Cooperative, in challenge to constitutionality of provisions of the Oklahoma Groundwater Law. The District Court affirmed the Board's determination of maximum annual yield and upheld the constitutionality of the Oklahoma Groundwater Law.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant landowners sought review of a determination by appellee, the Oklahoma Water Resources Board, of maximum annual yield. The landowners and intervenor, an electric generation facility, challenged the constitutionality of the Oklahoma Groundwater Law, Okla. Stat. tit. 82, § 1020.1 et seq. (1981). The District Court of Woodward County (Oklahoma) affirmed the Board's determination and upheld the Law. The landowners and the facility appealed.


OVERVIEW: The Board's order, which was affirmed by the district court, established the maximum annual yield of fresh ground water from the alluvium and terrace deposits of a river in five northwestern Oklahoma counties. The landowners and the electric generation facility contended that the Oklahoma Groundwater Law, Okla. Stat. tit. 82, § 1020.1 et seq. (1981), was unconstitutional. The court rejected the contention and expressly upheld the Law's constitutionality. In seeking to regulate and restrict the use and enjoyment of landowners of the natural resources of the state, so as to prevent them from waste and infringement, the Law did not unconstitutionally deprive the parties of vested property rights or abrogate prior water rights without due process of law. The landowner and the electric generation facility also protested that the differences in the area were not insubstantial, but rather, created either a subbasin or a sub-subbasin beneath their properties. The court noted that the identification of all possible subbasins within a basin was impractical, and was therefore not a strict prerequisite to the validity of an initial investigation of a groundwater basin.


OUTCOME: The court held that the district court did not err in determining the issues and affirmed the order district court judgment upholding the Board's order.

Baptist Health Care Corp. v. Okmulgee County Bd. of Equalization


No. 65,796


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1988 OK 11; 750 P.2d 127; 1988 Okla. LEXIS 19



February 9, 1988, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Okmulgee County, Oklahoma, Honorable Edgar R. Boatman, District Judge. On de novo appeal, the district court held home for the elderly operated by appellant tax-exempt corporation was not exempt from the payment of ad valorem taxes.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant not-for-profit corporation challenged the judgment of the District Court of Okmulgee County (Oklahoma) that a residential community for the elderly operated by the corporation was subject to ad valorem taxation.


OVERVIEW: Appellees, a county tax assessor and county tax authorities, placed one of the corporation's residential centers for the elderly on the county's ad valorem tax rolls. The corporation eventually sought de novo review by the district court, and appealed from that court's adverse judgment. The court reversed. The court observed that revenues from the rent paid by residents fell far short of meeting the operational costs of the facility, and that income from charitable donations provided nearly all of the funds for operating and maintaining the facility. In addition, the evidence made it abundantly clear that the overall purposes and practices of the residential center were charitable in nature. The court found that these facts were virtually identical to those of a previous decision and, following stare decisis, concluded that the district court erred in finding that the residential center was subject to ad valorem taxation. Addressing one of the arguments posed by the corporation, the court found that Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 2405 (1981) simply added definition to the words used in Okla. Const. art. 10, § 6 and did not place a limitation on that constitutional provision.


OUTCOME: The district court's judgment was reversed and the matter was remanded with directions to enter a judgment for the corporation.

No. 62,029


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1988 OK 9; 749 P.2d 1137; 1988 Okla. LEXIS 5



February 2, 1988, Filed

Nantz, filed a motion to modify support alimony on the ground that appellee, Patricia Ann Nantz, was cohabiting with a member of the opposite sex, and that the modification was therefore justified under the statutes. The trial court denied the motion.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant ex-husband sought review of the decision of the District Court of Comanche County (Oklahoma), which denied the ex-husband's motion to modify support alimony paid to appellee ex-wife on the grounds that she was cohabitating with a member of the opposite sex.


OVERVIEW: The ex-husband filed a motion to modify support alimony paid to the ex-wife pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 1289(D), which allowed modification on the basis of the party receiving the support cohabitating with a member of the opposite sex. The trial court denied the ex-husband's motion, holding that § 1289(D) was not in effect at the time that the order for alimony had been issued and that the statute was not retroactive. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court held that a number of amendments to the statute indicated that the legislature had intended that § 1289(D) was to be retroactive. The court also held that the legislature had the authority to make § 1289(D) retroactive because the right to alimony was not vested because it was subject to modification. Accordingly, the court overruled previous decisions that § 1289(D) was not retroactive and held that § 1289(D) was to be retroactively applied.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's denial of the ex-husband's motion to modify support alimony paid to the ex-wife.

Supreme Court of Oklahoma

AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff school council sought review of the order of the District Court, Oklahoma County, which granted judgment on the pleadings to defendant State in a suit for a declaration that the method of financing elementary and secondary education in Oklahoma was constitutionally infirm.


OVERVIEW: The school council brought a class action against the State seeking a judgment declaring that the method of financing public education in Oklahoma violated the United States and the Oklahoma Constitutions due to disparities in taxable wealth among the various school districts. The trial court granted judgment on the pleadings to the state and the school council sought review. There was no class-based denial of public education incompatible with the Equal Protection Clause, there was no requirement that the legislature provide equal expenditures per pupil, and there was no claim that the system denied any child a basic, adequate education.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1987 OK 107; 745 P.2d 737; 1987 Okla. LEXIS 256

A proceeding by an association of insurance carriers to review an order by the Workers' Compensation Court en banc which approved the application of a self-insurance association for a license as a group self-insurer. Order Vacated and Cause Remanded for Reconsideration in Light of After-Enacted Legislation.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner insurance association sought review of an order issued by the Workers' Compensation Court (Oklahoma), which approved the application of respondent motor carrier for a license as a group self-insurer. The insurance association maintained that Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 149 (1981) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The associated motor carrier applied to the workers' compensation court for a license as a group self-insurance association under the terms of Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 149 (1981). That statute authorized the worker's compensation court to regulate group self-insurance associations and to adopt rules and procedures governing their establishment. Shortly after the statute was passed, the Oklahoma Attorney General found that it was constitutionally infirm. Thereafter, the insurance association, which asserted an interest in the motor carriers' application, was allowed to intervene and to challenge the validity of the statute. The workers' compensation court upheld the statute's constitutionality and approved the motor carriers' application. Upon review, the court vacated the decision on the ground that after-enacted legislation encompassed the same issues covered by Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 149.1. Thus, the insurance association was entitled to an opportunity to recast its challenges and direct its arguments to be construed together with all the pertinent after-enacted legislative provisions.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the worker's compensation court's decision and remanded the case for further proceedings.

Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1987 OK 103; 746 P.2d 172; 1987 Okla. LEXIS 263



October 27, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma, Honorable Joe Cannon, District Judge. The Oklahoma Ethics Commission appeals from a judgment of the trial court setting aside the Commission's referral of a complaint against appellee to the District Attorney of Oklahoma County as null and void and restraining the Commission from any other proceedings in connection with the subject of the complaint on the basis of its finding: (1) 74 O.S. Supp. 1986 § 4207(H) of the Oklahoma Ethics Commission Act is unconstitutionally vague, (2) appellee was denied procedural due process, (3) certain loans to appellee were legal and (4) the interpretation placed on the loans by the Commission was violative of the First Amendment to the United States Constitution. REVERSED AND REMANDED WITH DIRECTIONS TO VACATE THE INJUNCTION.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Oklahoma Ethics Commission appealed a judgment from the District Court of Oklahoma County, (Oklahoma), setting aside the Commission's referral of a complaint against appellee gubernatorial candidate to the District Attorney of Oklahoma County as null and void and restraining the Commission from any other proceedings on the basis of its finding that Okla. Stat. tit. 74, § 4207(H) was unconstitutionally vague.


OVERVIEW: A gubernatorial candidate sought declaratory relief as to the constitutionality of procedural aspects of the Oklahoma Ethics Commission Act and its loan prohibition as it applied to him. The district court set aside the Commission's referral of the complaint against the candidate and restrained the Commission from any further proceedings. The Commission Appealed. In reversing, the court held that Okla. Stat. tit. 74, § 4207(H) was constitutional and that the gubernatorial candidates vagueness attack on that provision must fail. The court's reading of the statute indicated it required the Commission to conduct its investigative proceedings consistent with the minimal procedural protections of due process under the Federal and State Constitutions. U.S. Const. amend. XIV; Okla. Const. art. II, § 7. Additionally, the candidate was fully afforded all procedural due process rights to which he was entitled inasmuch as the facts were undisputed and no actual prejudice was shown. Lastly, the legality of the loans in question was not a properly tendered issue in a declaratory judgment action and therefore the trial court's ruling was in excess of its authority.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed. The case was remanded with directions to vacate the injunction and the matter shall proceed in the manner prescribed by the Oklahoma Ethics Commission Act.

October 13, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court of Woods County, Honorable John W. Michael, Trial Judge. Appellees contested the admission to probate of a codicil executed by a testatrix under a conservatorship. The basis for the contest was the failure to have the codicil executed in the presence of the judge of the district court as required by 84 O.S. Supp. 1982 § 41(B). Appellant, proponent of the codicil, attacked the requirement of section 41(B) on constitutional and other grounds. The trial court refused to admit codicil to probate. Appellant challenges that action.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The executor of the testatrix's estate petitioned for probate of a will and a codicil. The District Court of Woods County (Oklahoma) denied admission of the codicil to probate, as prayed for by appellee contestants. Appellant proponent sought review.


OVERVIEW: The codicil was executed after the testatrix had been placed under a conservatorship. The basis for the contest was that the codicil had not been executed in the presence of the judge of the district court as required by Okla. Stat. tit. 84, § 41(B) (Supp. 1982) for any person subject to a guardianship or conservatorship. The proponent attacked the statutory requirements on constitutional grounds. The trial court found no constitutional infirmity in the statute and refused to admit the codicil to probate due to its failure to conform. Affirming, the court held that the statute did not violate the principles of equal protection because the classification of those under conservatorship was a reasonable classification that bore a rational relationship to the objective of protecting those whose incapacities had increased their susceptibility to the exertion of improper influences. The court determined that it was irrelevant whether the codicil offered for probate substantially complied with § 41(B) because the statutory language required strict compliance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying admission of the testatrix's codicil to probate.

Spencer v. Seikel


No. 63,310


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1987 OK 75; 742 P.2d 1126; 1987 Okla. LEXIS 217



July 21, 1987 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals Division # 1. Appellants appeal from a jury verdict for appellees in an action for medical malpractice and cite as error the giving of improper instructions to the jury.



DISPOSITION:  OPINION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS VACATED JUDGMENT OF TRIAL COURT AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a patient and a child, appealed from judgment entered by the Court of Appeals Division One (Oklahoma), which affirmed the trial court's verdict in favor of appellee doctor in an action for medical malpractice. The patient and child cited as error the giving of improper instructions to the jury. After a timely motion, rehearing was denied, certiorari was granted.


OVERVIEW: During the course of prenatal treatment, the doctor discovered that the patient's fetus was suffering from hydrocephalus. The patient gave birth and sued the doctor under the Oklahoma Informed Consent Law alleging that the doctor was negligent in failing to disclose material information concerning an abortion as an alternative course of treatment. The doctor argued that when he first discovered hydrocephalus, the fetus was viable and therefore abortion was not an available alternative under the Oklahoma abortion statute, Ok. Stat. tit. 63 §§ 1-731-734 (1981). On appeal, the patient claimed that the abortion statute was unconstitutional, that the doctor was required to conform to national, not local, standards of care in treatment of patients, and that the doctor was negligent for not informing her that an abortion might be performed outside Oklahoma.The court determined that the patient could not recover because the doctor fully disclosed the fetus' condition, the patient knew from a previous pregnancy about abortions, the doctor had no duty to inform the patient about treatment alternatives available in other states, and the doctor's care did not cause of the child's condition.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the opinion of the appellate court and affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

184 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Petuskey v. Cannon


No. 68,671


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1987 OK 74; 742 P.2d 1117; 1987 Okla. LEXIS 223



July 21, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original proceedings commenced by the Court Clerk of Oklahoma County to prohibit/mandamus the Presiding Administrative District Judge of Oklahoma-Canadian Counties Administrative District from enforcing certain Administrative Orders entered by the Administrative Judge regarding Court Clerk personnel; the return of "no-file" bonds; collection of costs in condemnation cases; and collection of fines and costs. ORIGINAL JURISDICTION ASSUMED. WRIT GRANTED IN PART, DENIED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner court clerk of county (clerk) brought an original proceeding requesting that the court assume original jurisdiction and issue a mandamus and prohibition against respondent presiding administrative judge of county (judge) from enforcing certain administrative orders entered by the judge regarding court clerk personnel and collection of fines.


OVERVIEW: The court assumed original jurisdiction to clarify the authority of the judge and clerk. The court held that the clerk was "judicial personnel" as used in Okla. Sup. Ct. R. 2, Okla. Stat. tit. 20, ch. 1, app. 2. The clerk's duties were ministerial, except for those discretionary duties provided by statute. The clerk was subject to the control of the supreme court, and the supervisory control had been passed down to the judge in his district in the performance of the judge's ministerial functions. Pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 19, § 162 the clerk had the power to dictate who would be hired as a deputy and the deputy's rate of compensation. Pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 19, § 961 et seq., the clerk had no authority to act in a judicial capacity and demand payment of fines, fees and costs, until there had been an adjudication that the person must pay. Under Okla. Stat. tit. 59, § 1332(E) the clerk had the authority to charge a fee for the initial filing of any bond or release of defendant. The court held that the clerk had the right to collect court costs in certain condemnation proceedings. A judge did have some supervisory control over the deputy assigned to his court.


OUTCOME: The court accepted original jurisdiction and clarified the relationship between the clerk and judge in the clerk's mandamus and prohibition action against the judge.

 

185 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


R.E. v. State (In re A.E.)


No. 64,831


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1987 OK 76; 743 P.2d 1041; 1987 Okla. LEXIS 226



July 21, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals, Tulsa Division. The Court of Appeals held that the district court correctly affirmed the finding of the juvenile court referee terminating the parental rights of the appellants. The decision was based on the mother's failure to correct the conditions leading to the deprived adjudication and an abandonment by the father. On certiorari, the appellants reallege constitutional and statutory violations in the termination proceedings. We find that irregularities did occur, that the father was denied the constitutional right to trial by jury at the termination phase of the proceedings, and that the "contract" setting forth conditions to be met before the mother could regain custody was not judicially approved. To the extent that Wilson v. Foster, 595 P.2d 1329, 1331 (Okla. 1979), Matter of Keyes, 574 P.2d 1026, 1030 (Okla. 1978), and J. V. v. State Dept. of Insts., Social & Rehabilitative Servs., 572 P.2d 1283-84 (Okla. 1977), are inconsistent with the view expressed herein, they are hereby overruled. CERTIORARI GRANTED; OPINION OF THE COURT OF APPEALS VACATED; JUDGMENT OF THE TRIAL COURT REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, father and mother (parents), challenged an order of the Court of Appeals (Oklahoma) that affirmed the trial court's finding affirming the finding of the juvenile court referee that terminated the parental rights of both parents. On certiorari, the parents argued that there were constitutional and statutory violations in the termination proceedings.


OVERVIEW: The court found that the trial court correctly applied the correct burden of proof in parental termination rights case of clear and convincing proof. The attachment of a verified affidavit was not required at this time. On appeal, the court granted the parents' request for certiorari and vacated the appellate decision. It reversed the trial court's opinion. Irregularities did occur in the termination proceedings. The father was denied the constitutional right to trial by jury at the termination phase of the proceedings. The contract setting forth conditions to be met before the mother could regain custody was not judicially approved. The court overruled three state cases to the extent that they were inconsistent with the opinion. In a case of first impression, the court held that the right to jury trial was constitutionally mandated by the Oklahoma Constitution and the Oklahoma Juvenile Code in parental termination rights cases. It reasoned that parental rights were too precious to be terminated without the full protection of constitutional rights. The right to jury trial could not be annulled, obstructed, impaired, or restricted by legislative or judicial action.


OUTCOME: The court granted the request for certiorari and vacated the appellate court's decision. The court reversed the trial court's opinion.

Terry v. Gassett


No. 68,452


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1987 OK 60; 740 P.2d 141; 1987 Okla. LEXIS 207



July 7, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petitioner was filed on for contempt by reason of failure to pay child support. At arraignment he requested a jury trial. Trial court placed it on the jury docket and as required by statute set an appearance bond with time to post. Petitioner, unable to make bond, waived jury trial. In this original action petitioner/husband seeks prohibition and/or mandamus to require the trial court to set indirect contempt proceedings for jury trial without requiring that his appearance be assured by bond. ORIGINAL JURISDICTION ASSUMED, WAIVER OF JURY TRIAL VACATED, AND WRIT ISSUED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an original action, petitioner husband sought prohibition and/or mandamus against respondents, a wife and a judge, to require the trial court to set indirect contempt proceedings for jury trial without requiring that his appearance be assured by bond.


OVERVIEW: The husband was the subject of contempt proceedings for failure to pay child support. When the husband was not able to post the appearance bond, under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 567 (1981), the trial court informed him that if he continued to request a jury trial he would be incarcerated until the trial date unless he posted a bond. The husband then waived a jury trial. The court set aside the husband's waiver of a jury trial. The court held that the trial court could not condition its decision to set bail or release on recognizance upon the husband's election to demand or waive trial by jury for indirect contempt. The court found, inter alia, that (1) to condition the requirement of an appearance bond on the exercise of the right to trial by jury was erroneous; (2) where § 567 lent itself to two differing constructions, one of which would render the statute unconstitutional, the court adopted the construction, which upheld the statute because no repugnancy to the constitution was shown beyond a reasonable doubt; and (3)a person could not be held for failure to make bail simply because he requested a jury trial.


OUTCOME: The court assumed original jurisdiction, vacated the husband's waiver of a jury trial, and issued a writ to the trial court.

Fleming v. Baptist General Convention


Case Number: 54711, 54712, 54856, 54857


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1987 OK 54; 742 P.2d 1087; 1987 Okla. LEXIS 302



June 23, 1987, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] Appeal from the District Court of Ottawa County; Sam C. Fullerton, Jr., District Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED. EXECUTION ON JUDGMENT STAYED AS ORDERED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant hospital appealed the judgment of the District Court of Ottawa County (Oklahoma) in favor of plaintiff patient in the patient's medical malpractice action, arguing that the trial court erred in overruling its demurrer, motion for a directed verdict, and motion for a judgment notwithstanding the verdict where the patient's theory of negligence was unsupported by the evidence and further erred in awarding prejudgment interest.


OVERVIEW: The patient had a chronic history of pain. She presented to the hospital to receive relief from pain associated with a migraine headache. A member of the hospital staff injected medication into the patient's thigh. The injection site became infected and ultimately became gangrenous. Removal of dead tissue was required, leaving the patient with a disfiguring scar. She filed a medical malpractice suit against the doctor and hospital. The jury returned a verdict in favor of the doctor and in favor of the patient against the hospital. The hospital appealed. In affirming, the court concluded that, where the patient's expert witnesses testified that the medication was improperly injected into the subcutaneous tissue and that the negligent injection caused the resulting damages, this evidence was sufficient to establish a prima facie case of malpractice. As such, the trial court properly denied the demurrer and motions. Further, the trial court properly awarded prejudgment interest, which was mandated by Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 727 (Supp. 1979).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

Hair v. Okla. Corp. Comm'n


Nos. 58,060, 58,346 (Consolidated)


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1987 OK 50; 740 P.2d 134; 1987 Okla. LEXIS 200; 96 Oil & Gas Rep. 333



June 16, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Consolidated appeals from the Oklahoma Corporation Commission mineral owners appeal from two separate orders promulgated by the Oklahoma Corporation Commission. In the first order appealed the Commission approved and adopted a drilling and spacing order previously issued by the Administrative Review Panel acting under authority of 17 O.S. 1981 §§ 21-24 (repealed 1982) and 52 O.S. 1981 § 1, in which the Panel extended the boundaries of various common sources of supply and established drilling and spacing units for said common sources of supply retroactive from the date the application was filed. The second order appealed is an order nunc pro tunc correcting a scrivener's error in the former Commission order which improperly cited the effective date in the scheduled listing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mineral owners challenged two orders promulgated by appellee Oklahoma Corporation Commission. The first order adopted a drilling and spacing order issued by the Administrative Review Panel extending the boundaries of various common sources of supply and establishing drilling and spacing units for said common sources. The second was an order nunc pro tunc correcting an error in the first order with respect to the effective date.


OVERVIEW: A corporation filed an application to amend spacing orders to extend the boundaries of various common sources of supply and to establish proper drilling and spacing units. The Commission gave notice of the hearing by publication. The Panel issued an order granting the application, and the Commission adopted it. The Commission's order incorrectly stated the effective date, and an order nunc pro tunc was issued correcting it. The court affirmed. The Commission and Panel were acting under color of authority prior to actual notice of the Attorney General's Opinion declaring Okla. Stat. tit. 17, §§ 21 to 24 (1981) and Okla. Stat. tit. 52, §1 (1981), which created the Commission and Panel, unconstitutional. Thus, the orders were valid. The orders were made prior to the effective date of the caselaw precedent, which held that notice by publication was inadequate. Thus, the court was constrained to leave the orders undisturbed. The orders were sustained by the law and by substantial evidence. Although an appeal was pending on the first order, the Commission had jurisdiction to enter the order nunc pro tunc, as it merely corrected an error and did not render a different judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Commission's orders.

Bison Nitrogen Prods. Co. v. Lucas
