Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1987 OK 46; 738 P.2d 147; 1987 Okla. LEXIS 197



June 2, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeals from the District Court of Woodward County, Oklahoma, Honorable Joe Young, District Judge. Certiorari to Court of Appeals, Division II (57,477). These actions challenged the legality of ad valorem tax assessments on personal property owned by appellants. District court found the assessments were legally valid, and appellants brought these appeals which are considered together in this opinion.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant companies sought review of the judgment of the District Court of Woodward County (Oklahoma), which found in favor of appellees, county treasurer and county assessor, on the companies' actions, pursuant to Okla. Stat. Supp. Tit. 68, § 2469 (1965), to obtain refunds of ad valorem taxes paid under protest for taxes assessed on real and personal property for 1980 and 1981.


OVERVIEW: Under the tax scheme used by the county assessor, assessment ratios that varied from 15 percent to 27 percent of value were applied to various items of personal property. Subsequently, the companies filed an action against the county treasurer and the county assessor to obtain refunds of ad valorem taxes paid under protest for taxes assessed on real and personal property for 1980 and 1981. The companies argued that the county's application of different rates of taxation to personal property, with its resulting unequal tax burdens, was arbitrary and unconstitutional because all tangible personal property should be assessed at the same ratio and all property subject to ad valorem taxation, whether real or personal, should be assessed at the same ratio. OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed and remanded in part the judgment, which found in favor of the county treasurer and county assessor on the companies' actions to obtain refunds of ad valorem taxes paid under protest for taxes assessed on real and personal property for 1980 and 1981.

Chrysler Corp. v. Clark


No. 61,997


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1987 OK 32; 737 P.2d 109; 1987 Okla. LEXIS 180



May 5, 1987, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma, Honorable Joe Cannon, Trial Judge. Appellant automobile manufacturer brought declaratory judgment action against members of the Oklahoma Motor Vehicle Commission challenging the constitutionality of certain provisions of the legislation establishing the commission and granting it powers to control placement of new franchises. The trial court sustained a demurrer to appellant's second amended petition on the ground that it failed to present a justiciable controversy. Appellant challenges that ruling.



DISPOSITION:  The trial court's ruling is REVERSED and the cause REMANDED for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant car manufacturer sought review of the decision of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which sustained a demurrer of appellee Oklahoma Motor Vehicle Commission to the car manufacturer's declaratory judgment action that challenged the constitutionality of certain provisions of Okla. Stat. tit. 47, § 578 (1981).


OVERVIEW: The car manufacturer brought a declaratory judgment action that challenged the constitutionality of the statute that established the Oklahoma Motor Vehicle Commission (OMVC) and regulated the establishment of new car dealerships in the state. The trial court ruled in response to the OMVC's demurrer that the manufacturer had failed to present an actual controversy within the meaning of Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 1651 (1981), because it had failed to apply for permission to establish a new dealership in the state. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment of the trial court. The court noted that a portion of the manufacturer's contentions were that the statute in question was repugnant to the due process provisions of the U.S. Const. amend XIV, to the Interstate Commerce Clause of the U.S. Constitution, to 15 U.S.C.S. § 1, and to the provisions of the Oklahoma Constitution prohibiting monopolies and restraints of trade, as provided in Okla. Const. art. II, § 32 and art. V, § 44. In the court's opinion, no party who was affected by a statute was prohibited from challenging the facial validity of an act simply because they had not violated the statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which had sustained the Oklahoma Motor Vehicle Commission's demurrer to a car manufacturer's declaratory judgment action on the grounds that the manufacturer had not been denied any request under the statutory scheme.

Black v. Ball Janitorial Serv.


Nos. 62,430, 62,774 (Consolidated)


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1986 OK 75; 730 P.2d 510; 1986 Okla. LEXIS 208



December 9, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court, Tulsa County, Robert J. Scott, Judge. In a negligence-based tort action, plaintiff sought damages for bodily injury received in a slip-and-fall episode at a municipal airport. The trial court rendered judgment on the defendants' demurrers grounded on the bar of limitation.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff brought a negligence-based tort action against defendants, including a municipal corporation and a public trust. The District Court, Tulsa County (Oklahoma) rendered judgment on demurrers presented by the municipal corporation and the public trust, finding that plaintiff's action was not filed within the time limit prescribed by the Political Subdivision Tort Claims Act (Act), Okla. Stat. tit. 51, § 156(C) (1981). Plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: Almost two years after she slipped and fell at an airport, plaintiff filed suit against defendants. The municipal corporation and the public trust filed demurrers grounded on the Act's bar of limitation. When plaintiff chose to stand on her complaint, the district court rendered a judgment in favor of the municipal corporation and the public trust. Plaintiff sought review. The court affirmed, finding constitutional the time intervals prescribed in the Act for bringing an action against a municipal corporation or a public trust that was acting in its proprietary capacity when the harm occurred. Specifically, no offense was dealt to either equal protection or due process by requiring that suits against the government for tortious harm committed by its agents acting in either proprietary or governmental capacity stand subjected to the very same norms of liability. Moreover, in creating a separate class of public tortfeasors, the Act did not violate the state's constitutional prohibition against special legislation because the classification used was reasonable for the attainment of a legitimate objective and operated uniformly upon all members of the class.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment.

Luster v. Bank of Chelsea


No. 60,819


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1986 OK 74; 730 P.2d 506; 1986 Okla. LEXIS 201



December 2, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals, Division No. 2. The trial court quieted title in certain real property in appellants which they had acquired by a resale tax deed, subject to the mortgage held by appellee bank and certain rights-of-way and easements held by other defendants. On appeal of both appellants and appellees the Court of Appeals in an unpublished Memorandum Opinion reversed in part and remanded with directions that the tax resale deed extinguished the mortgage held by appellee bank. Certiorari Previously Granted. Court of Appeals Opinion Vacated. Judgment of Trial Court Affirmed in Part, Reversed in Part and Remanded with Instructions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a bank and a surface owner, challenged an opinion from the Court of Appeals, Division Two (Oklahoma), which affirmed the part of the trial court's judgment sustaining plaintiff resale tax buyers' resale tax deed whereby the county treasurer conveyed the property to them, but reversed the part sustaining the bank's mortgage on the property.


OVERVIEW: Defendants claimed the county treasurer lacked jurisdiction to sell the property and convey title to the buyers because the notices during both the original sale and the resale did not meet due process requirements. On appeal, the court vacated the court of appeals' opinion, holding that the manner of notice provided to defendants, in the circumstances of the case, did not measure up to the quality of notice required by the Due Process Clause of the Fourteenth Amendment. The county treasurer inadvertently changed his records to show an undivided mineral interest owned the property. He sent notice of the tax sale to the mineral interest owner and published it in the newspaper. These notices were not reasonably calculated, under all the circumstances, to apprise defendants of the tax sale and the subsequent sale. Therefore, the county treasurer lacked jurisdiction over the original sale and the resale on which the resale tax deed was based, and the resale tax deed was void.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the court of appeals' judgment and affirmed the part of the trial court's judgment holding that the bank had a valid mortgage, but reversed the part finding that the resale tax deed was valid and passed title.

Davis Oil Co. v. Cloud


No. 61,473


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1986 OK 73; 766 P.2d 1347; 1986 Okla. LEXIS 194; 102 Oil & Gas Rep. 318



November 18, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended January 12, 1989. Dissenting Opinion on Rehearing January 17, 1989, Reported at: 766 P.2d 1347 at 1353.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court of Haskell County, Oklahoma, Honorable John Henderson, Trial Judge. Oil Company appeals from judgment rendered on jury verdict in action brought pursuant to surface damages act, 52 O.S. 1982 §§ 318.2 through 318.9. Oil Company challenges the constitutionality of the application of this legislation in the present case on grounds that such an application retroactively impairs its vested rights. Appellant also challenges the allowance of recovery of damages on nuisance theory in this case.



DISPOSITION:  AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant oil company sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Haskell County, Oklahoma, which was rendered on a jury verdict for appellee property owner, in an action brought pursuant to the surface damages act, Okla. Stat. tit. 52, §§ 318.2-318.9 (1982).


OVERVIEW: The oil company challenged the constitutionality of the act on grounds that its application retroactively impaired its vested rights. On appeal, the court determined that the property right in question was the right to go on the property in pursuit of the oil and gas. The limitation on the operator's liability in the exercise of that right was no more than a defense, which had been provided to the operator by operation of the common law in actions for damages by the surface estate holder. The standard of liability for damages to the surface estate flowing from the exercise of the mineral estate holder's right to enter and use the land was a subject clearly susceptible to modification by exercise of the state's police power. The act, as it set forth a mechanism for determining actual damages to the surface estate, was not unreasonable in its application. Because the act had application to all instances where the mineral and surface estates had been severed, it was not arbitrary nor capricious in its effect. The means selected of awarding actual damages to the surface estate holder bore a real and substantial relation to the object of balancing the interests of the various estates.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment for the property owner.

Turner v. City of Lawton


No. 61,399


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1986 OK 51; 733 P.2d 375; 1986 Okla. LEXIS 150



July 22, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari to the Court of Appeals, Division No. 2. After illegally obtained evidence was taken from his home, the appellant-firefighter was suspended and subsequently discharged without a pre-termination hearing. After the evidence was presented in his post-termination hearing, the firefighter appealed the discharge to the district court seeking reinstatement, alleging that the exclusionary rule is applicable to civil as well as criminal proceedings and that his constitutional rights had been violated. The Honorable William M. Roberts ordered his reinstatement and the City of Lawton appealed. In a split decision, the Court of Appeals reversed and certiorari was granted. On certiorari, we find that because the affidavit was concededly facially defective, the search warrant was invalid, and that the exclusionary rule was properly applied under the Okla. Const. art. 2, § 30.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee firefighter filed a petition for writ of certiorari, challenging a judgment of the Court of Appeals, Division No. 2 (Oklahoma), which reversed the trial court decision ordering his reinstatement after he was discharged by appellant city based on illegally obtained evidence taken from his home.


OVERVIEW: After criminal charges against the firefighter were dismissed, he filed an action for reinstatement, asserting that he had been fired based on evidence seized in violation of his constitutional rights. The trial court ordered his reinstatement, but the court of appeals reversed the order. On certiorari, the court reversed the court of appeals and affirmed the trial court's order. Because the affidavit was concededly facially defective, the search warrant was invalid, and that the exclusionary rule was properly applied under Okla. Const. art. 2, § 30. Evidence obtained by a search warrant held invalid and suppressed in a criminal action was not admissible in the related civil administrative proceeding. If the evidence had been permitted to have been used to discharge the fireman even though the criminal charges had been dismissed, there would still have been a substantial incentive to the city's police officers to engage in further unlawful searches, especially when municipal employees were the targets thereof.


OUTCOME: The court granted certiorari, vacated the judgment of the court of appeals, and affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Roberts v. S. Okla. City Hosp. Trust


No. 60,999


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1986 OK 52; 742 P.2d 1077; 1986 Okla. LEXIS 154



July 22, 1986, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County Honorable John M. Amick, Trial Judge. This is an appeal from a motion for summary judgment in which the trial court determined that the failure of the surviving spouse to comply with the notice provisions of the Political Subdivision Tort Claims Act, 51 O.S. Supp. 1979 § 156(D) (Act) barred the cause of action for wrongful death. We find that because the purported public trust is illusory it is not a political subdivision; that the Act is inapplicable, and that the two year statute of limitations, 12 O.S. 1981 § 1053(A) governs.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband challenged a judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which sustained appellee hospital's motion for summary judgment in the husband's action alleging that appellee attending physician and the hospital were negligent in the care and treatment of the wife. The trial court found the hospital was a public trust and subject to the notice provisions of the Political Subdivision Tort Claims Act.


OVERVIEW: The wife was found dead in her bed in the hospital after she was admitted to a regular room. The wife was placed in a regular room because there were no available bed in the cardiac unit. The husband brought the suit more than a year after the wife's death. The hospital claimed the suit was barred because the notice provisions of the Act required the husband to give notice of the claim within one-year of the injury. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court granting the hospital's motion for summary judgment and remanded. The court held as follows: 1) the applicable statute was the two-year limitations period prescribed by Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 1053(A) (1981) because the hospital was not a public trust and therefore not a political subdivision; 2) the trust agreement between the hospital and the city was illusory because the hospital retained control of the entity which it purported to convey; and 3) the hospital was not a public trust of the city because in the absence of dissolution, there was no direct monetary benefit to the city and the hospital's business was conducted without consultation with the city or within any parameters of city sponsored policy.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment of the trial court granting the hospital's motion for summary judgment.

Price v. Reed


No. 62,195


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1986 OK 43; 725 P.2d 1254; 1986 Okla. LEXIS 144

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal From The District Court, Custer County, David E. Brooks, Judge. In a licensee's appeal from a postacquittal driver's license revocation, the trial court declared the "implied consent" provisions in 47 O.S. Supp. 1982 § 754 to be violative of the state constitution and reinstated the appellee's driver's license.



DISPOSITION:  REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Commissioner, Oklahoma Department of Public Safety (Department) sought review of a decision of the District Court, Custer County (Oklahoma), which reinstated appellee licensee's driver's license following a postacquittal revocation by the Department under the Implied Consent Law at Okla. Stat. tit. 47, § 754(5)(a) (1982). The trial court found § 754(5)(a) in violation of Okla. Const. art. 2, § 21.


OVERVIEW: The police arrested the licensee for actual, physical control of a motor vehicle while under the influence of alcohol. The trial court determined that the revocation violated Okla. Const. art. 2, § 21 and Okla. Const. art. 4, § 1 as a double jeopardy violation and separation of state powers. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case. The Double Jeopardy Clause of the Fifth Amendment and Okla. Const. art. 2, § 21 did not bar revocation of the licensee's driver's license by the Department because the licensee was not placed in jeopardy by the proceedings against him. Double jeopardy protection had a strict application to criminal prosecutions and did not bar possible criminal and civil sanctions against the licensee for the same act or omission. The revocation proceedings were civil in nature and revocation of the driver's license was not a criminal penalty. The separation of state powers under Okla. Const. art. 4, § 1 were not violated by operation of Okla. Stat. tit. 47, § 754(5)(a) (1982) because the Legislature had the power to establish the burden of evidentiary persuasion under § 754(5)(a).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court to reinstate the licensee's driver's license and remanded the case.

 

199 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Seal v. Corp. Comm'n


Nos. 61,636, 61,652, Consolidated


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1986 OK 34; 725 P.2d 278; 1986 Okla. LEXIS 135; 90 Oil & Gas Rep. 500



June 17, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected September 10, 1986. .


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Corporation Commission of The State of Oklahoma. In this consolidated appeal, appellants seek review of Rules promulgated by the Corporation Commission pursuant to Order No. 250466 to enforce and administer the provisions of 52 O.S. Supp. 1983 § 541, et seq. relating to sharing ratably in revenues from the sale of production of natural gas. Amerada challenges both the constitutionality of the Act and the Rules thereunder. Seal challenges only the constitutionality of specific provisions of the Rules.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, gas companies and well owners, sought review of a decision of appellee Corporation Commission of the State of Oklahoma, which promulgated rules to enforce and administer the provisions of Okla. Stat. tit. 52, § 541 (1983) et seq. (Act), relating to shared ratable revenues from the sale of production of natural gas.


OVERVIEW: The Act was passed under the legislature's police power to protect the rights of all interest owners of gas wells and to afford all such owners an equal opportunity to extract their fair share of gas and to sell and be paid in proportion to their interest in the wells. For these purposes and to protect owners against discrimination in purchases in favor of one owner as against another, Okla. Stat. tit. 52, § 542 (1983) provided that whenever a well was placed into production, all owners were entitled to share ratably in revenues from the sale of production. The Commission enacted rules to administer the Act. The gas companies filed an action against the Commission alleging that the Act and the rules were unconstitutional; the well owners challenged the rules. The court affirmed the validity of the Act, holding that it (1) was a proper exercise of the State's police power; (2) did not constitute a taking of property for private use; and (3) did not violate the Contract Clause of the state and federal constitutions. The court held that Rules 6-104(E), 6-102(C)(3), 6-103 (D) (3), 6-104 (C) (1), 6-104(F), and 6-112 of the Commission were inconsistent with the Act and invalid.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the validity of the Act. The court also held that certain rules of the Commission were invalid.

 

200 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Prudential Prop. & Cas. Co. v. Grimes


No. 66,589


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1986 OK 32; 725 P.2d 1246; 1986 Okla. LEXIS 134



June 12, 1986, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 7, 1986.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court of Oklahoma County Honorable John Amick, District Judge. Plaintiffs seek to enjoin State Insurance Commissioner from transferring funds from statutorily created Insurance Commissioner's Protest Fund to other agencies as authorized by anticipated legislation. From order of trial court denying injunctive relief, plaintiffs appeal. We find proposed transfers in violation of Oklahoma Constitution and reverse. Injunction issued.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, out-of-state insurance companies, sought review of a judgment entered in the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) that denied their challenge to enjoin defendant state insurance commissioner from transferring funds from the insurance commissioner's protest funds to other agencies as authorized by anticipated legislation.


OVERVIEW: The out-of-state insurance companies filed an action against the insurance commissioner, challenging Oklahoma's gross premium tax laws on the basis that they denied the out-of-state insurance companies equal protection of the law. The trial court denied the injunctive relief requested by the out-of-state insurance companies. On appeal, the insurance commissioner argued that the complaint filed by the out-of-state insurance companies was premature because there was no justiciable controversy, as the challenged legislation had not been enacted. The court rejected this argument and found that an infirmity in the procedural posture of the case did not prevent the court from addressing the vital public law issue presented. The court then examined the proposed legislation and found that Okla. Const., art 4, § 54 protected a litigant's right to pursue its rights under a repealed statute by proceedings begun before the statute was repealed. The court found that, here, the acts of the out-of-state insurance companies in paying the challenged taxes, serving notices of protest, and filing a timely suit constituted proceedings begun, which could not be interdicted by repealing the statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order that denied injunctive relief. The court enjoined the insurance commissioner from making further transfers of money from the insurance commissioner's protest fund, except in accordance with law. The court ordered the injunction to remain in effect pending determination of the out-of-state insurance companies' constitutional challenges to Oklahoma's gross premium tax laws.
